Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008 Mecom is a European content and consumer 
business whose strategy is to build upon its 
well-established publishing brands, high quality 
content and knowledge of its communities by 
generating new revenues through different 
content platforms, the development of stand-
alone digital businesses and the sale of 
branded goods and services which are relevant 
to the daily needs of our audiences.

01
Overview
Our values
Mecom is committed to building value for its owners, 
communities and employees.
Mecom creates commercial opportunities without 
compromising editorial freedom. 
By maximising the value of its content Mecom seeks to 
protect its newspaper titles whose continued existence  
is the greatest protector of quality journalism and  
editorial independence.
Mecom stands for and protects quality journalism, editorial 
freedom and independence, with publishing principles 
which ensure that no government, owner, advertiser or  
any other interest group are entitled to interfere in  
editorial decisions.
Mecom is close to all its communities with its heritage, 
trusted brands, local culture and focus on the needs  
and interests of its audiences.
Mecom recognises its employees as its greatest asset  
and is working with them to grow the business.

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 03
Overview
T ransformation
Mecom is changing the Group into 
a modern multi-platform content 
and consumer business in order to 
maximise the collection and delivery 
of high-quality relevant content, new 
revenue opportunities, efficiencies 
and savings across the Group. 
A core element of this process is the 
merging of print and online operations in 
newsrooms, editorial, marketing and sales 
departments. This enables journalists 
to work on both print and online content 
and optimises the collection, cross-
marketing and sale of the highest quality 
products and services to our communities 
whatever their choice of delivery. 
By reorganising the workflow in 
newsrooms and establishing new 
methods of content collection and 
delivery, Mecom becomes closer to the 
consumers and strengthens its relationship 
with its markets and communities.
This new business model is being 
implemented to generate more revenue 
per customer rather than relying solely 
on the price of the newspaper or a 
single advertisement and reaching 
an audience which is well beyond the 
reach of traditional newspapers.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 04 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Overview
New
revenues
In addition to generating revenues through 
new content platforms, Mecom is also 
developing new revenues through stand-
alone digital businesses, as well as the sale 
of branded goods and services targeted 
to appeal to our readers (Enterprises). 
The growth in the popularity of our 
newspaper related websites, like rp.pl 
(the online companion to Rzeczpospolita 
in Poland) or berlingske.dk (the online 
companion to Berlingske Tidende in 
Denmark), is being mirrored by the 
growth in the reach of our portfolio of 
stand-alone digital businesses that are 
not related to the Group’s newspapers 
but use new brands to target specific 
interests or markets. Whether it is the 
leading automotive classifieds site 
autotrack.nl in the Netherlands or the 
city site for Copenhagen aok.dk, these 
sites represent an increasingly important 
part of Mecom’s digital portfolio. 
In parallel, Mecom is developing a 
diversified portfolio of brand endorsed 
products and services which can be 
promoted across all content platforms. 
Mecom now sells a wide range of items 
including holidays, books, CDs, DVDs, as 
well as home-wares and theatre tickets.

Overview
Titles
Key to the transformation 
process is not only high-
quality content but also well-
established trustworthy brands 
and strong marketing platforms. 
As well as its 300 printed 
titles, Mecom has more 
than 200 websites.
More than 130 websites 
are newspaper sites which 
are essential to consolidate 
Mecom’s position as a 
leading source of news 
and entertainment in their 
respective markets. 
The other 70 websites are 
stand-alone sites targeting 
new markets with new brands 
contributing to an overall 
impressive digital portfolio.

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 09
Overview
Our
people
Mecom would not have been able to 
embark on its transformation strategy 
without the talent, commitment and 
adaptability of its employees. 
Mecom is a people business. The 
passion and drive of its people is its 
biggest asset. Mecom employees form 
part of the communities it serves, and 
they are well placed to understand 
the needs of these communities.
The key to Mecom’s approach has been 
the rigorous training of its experienced 
employees to work online as well as offline, 
creating new forms of content (including 
online TV, tools and utilities) and integrating 
user opinion and feedback across as 
many media channels as possible.
They have had to adapt to the challenge 
of established thinking and devise new 
sales methods and a fresh journalistic 
approach promoting greater productivity 
from the existing resources. 
Mecom’s employees have responded 
to change with great imagination, 
endeavour and commitment.

Overview
Our 
divisions
Mecom’s strategy is to use 
the scale of the Group and its 
very large readership base to 
create a modern content and 
consumer business which is 
no longer solely dependent on 
printed products. There is a 
new management team in place 
in all of Mecom’s geographies 
to implement this strategy. 
The Netherlands
The Group’s Dutch division, comprising 
the Wegener and Limburg Media Group 
businesses, is the largest publisher 
of regional daily newspapers and 
free door-to-door newspapers in the 
Netherlands, with approximately 60 
per cent of the regional circulation 
market and approximately 20 per cent 
of the total Dutch newspaper market. 
The division also operates more than 
35 websites and seven printing plants, 
which print both Group and third-
party publications. In a country with 
a population of over 16 million, the 
division’s publications have a readership 
of more than 11.8 million every week and 
its online operations attract more than 
9.0 million unique users every month.

Mecom’s Danish division, operating 
under the name Berlingske Media

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 12 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Overview
Overview
I am very pleased to report in my first 
Chairman’s statement to shareholders that we 
expect that Mecom will shortly secure a new 
and solid financial platform for the future. We 
have today announced that a mix of existing 
shareholders and new institutional investors 
have signed non-binding letters of support for 
an equity issue to raise £140 million (before 
expenses). Their support is conditional on, 
amongst other things, the Group agreeing 
final facility documentation with its lenders 
(the principal commercial terms of which have 
already received credit approval from each 
of the lenders); the issue of a prospectus in 
connection with an equity issue; and relevant 
shareholder resolutions being passed. The 
Group’s new bank facilities, the principal 
feature of which is a waiver of normal trading 
covenants until June 2010, are primarily 
intended to protect Mecom against continuing 
weakness in its advertising markets. 
We anticipate that a prospectus will be 
posted to shareholders in mid-May. When  
the proceeds of an equity issue are received, 
we will repay our unsecured convertible loan 
note holders in full (approximately £30.6 million) 
with the balance of the proceeds applied in 
paying down bank debt. The combination of 
the disposals earlier in the year of our German 
and Northwest Norway divisions, the new 
bank arrangements and an equity issue give 
us a good base from which to enter an upturn 
in all of the economies in which we operate, 
from which all of our newspaper titles and 
other media outlets should benefit significantly. 
Although the short-term outlook for our 
businesses remains uncertain, the Board 
is confident that the longer term promises 
greater stability and improved profitability. We 
are grateful to our shareholders and lenders 
for sharing this confidence.
Board
It was announced on 16 January 2009 that I 
had been appointed Chairman of the Group, 
having previously been a non-executive 
Director. David Montgomery, who had been 
Executive Chairman of Mecom since its 
foundation, remains the Chief Executive. This 
change is in accordance with the undertaking 
Mecom gave at the time of its move to trading 
on the London Stock Exchange’s main market 
for listed securities last year to split the roles of 
Chairman and Chief Executive.
We were pleased to welcome Stephen 
Davidson who joined the Board as the Senior 
Independent Director on 16 January 2009 as 
well as Henry Davies, who joined the Board 
as acting Finance Director on the same day 
and became Group Finance Director on 13 
February 2009. We expect to be in a position 
to announce the appointment of another non-
executive director shortly.
Chairman’s 
statement
Throughout 2008 and the first few months 
of 2009, our managers and employees in 
all departments across the Group have 
responded – in the face of extremely debilitating 
economic conditions – with enthusiasm and 
determination in the continuing transformation 
of our traditional newspaper business into a 
more broadly-based consumer and content 
business. On behalf of the Board, I thank 
them very much for their commitment and 
hard work.
Alasdair Locke
Chairman

Group
highlights
Equity issue and amendments to 
the facility terms
The agreed amendments to the Group’s debt 
facilities and the proposed equity issue to 
raise £140 million (before expenses) together 
represent material progress in restructuring 
Mecom’s balance sheet. In particular:
net cash proceeds from the equity raise of •	
£133 million (approximately €149 million);
£30.6 million (€34.2 million) of the net •	
proceeds will be used to pay down the 
Group’s outstanding convertible loan notes, 
with the balance being used to pay down 
bank debt;
pro forma 2008 net debt of approximately •	
£340 million (€350 million), after taking into 
account the net proceeds of the equity 
issue and the net proceeds of the recently 
completed disposals of the Group’s German 
and Northwestern Norwegian businesses;
testing holiday of normal trading covenants •	
under the facility agreement until June 2010;
margin of 350 bps on the term loan, 300 •	
bps on the revolving credit facilities; and
total debt restructuring costs of •	
approximately £18 million (€20 million).
Mecom expects that full banking documentation 
will be finalised in mid May 2009 following which 
the Group expects to launch the equity issue. 
Key financials
The Group has presented its financial results 
on two bases below and in the Chairman’s 
statement, the Chief Executive’s review and 
the Divisional reviews. 
The first is “like-for-like”, which presents 
comparatives for the year to 31 December 2007 
as if Mecom had owned all of its divisions for that 
entire year so as to allow a better understanding 
of the underlying trading and financial 
performance of the Mecom divisions (these 
are shown as Group revenue, Group EBITDA 
and Group operating profit in the table below); 
this like-for-like information is also stated before 
exceptional items and amortisation of acquired 
intangibles and on a constant currency basis 
(being the average exchange rates prevailing 
in the year to 31 December 2008); this like-
for-like information also includes the results of 
Mecom Germany on a line-by-line basis. 
The second basis is “reported”, that is the 
results of the operations as they appear in 
the audited financial statements, which reflect  
the ownership of Wegener and Mecom Germany 
for only part of the year to 31 December 2007 
and present the results of Mecom Germany as 
a discontinued operation in the financial years 
to 31 December 2008 and 31 December 2007 . 
The effect of the acquisitions of Wegener and 
Mecom Germany part way through the year to 
31 December 2007 results in the two sets of 
reported results not being directly comparable.

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 14 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Overview
Overview
Since the summer of 2008 Mecom has been 
making significant adjustments to its financial 
position to deal with unprecedented economic 
conditions caused by the worldwide recession. 
The downturn, which has been reflected in a 
marked decline in trading multiples of publicly 
listed newspaper groups, came within months 
of Mecom completing its largest acquisition, 
of Wegener in the Netherlands, which itself 
represented half the size of the Group. 
Clearly the Group has had to act promptly 
to install a financial structure suitable for the 
current times and one that will sustain the 
business through a volatile advertising market 
with the extent of the downturn still difficult  
to predict. 
At the beginning of 2009 Mecom agreed the 
disposal of its German assets, principally the 
newspapers in Berlin and Hamburg. The price 
achieved (7.8 times 2008 adjusted EBITDA) 
was materially in excess of the trading multiple 
of both Mecom and the sector. Later, the 
Northwest Norwegian assets were sold at 
a price (7.3 times adjusted EBITDA) which 
reflected a similar premium to sector valuations. 
The combined €210 million of proceeds (net 
of expenses) has been used to pay down 
debt. In the case of Germany, the newspaper 
sector remains ripe for consolidation and as 
Mecom had no ability to participate further in 
this at the time, the disposal was well justified 
strategically. In the case of Northwest Norway, 
the disposal still leaves the Group with a 
considerable business in that country mainly 
grouped much closer to Oslo. The lost profits 
from the disposed assets should be made 
up in the medium term by strenuous cost 
reduction including sharing of services with 
other Norwegian publishers.
The disposals do not disrupt the pursuit or 
the validity of the overall Group strategy. 
This is to consolidate regional newspapers 
across Europe within a single infrastructure 
and to transform an old-fashioned print- 
based business into a content and consumer-
focused Group. 
The intensity of the economic storm will require 
us to accelerate cost savings associated with 
our ongoing restructuring programmes. In 
2008, the Group-wide reduction in headcount 
of 830, or 7 per cent, of the workforce was 
in part offset by high salary inflation. However, 
this inflationary trend in staff and supplier costs 
is now subsiding as the recession bites.
Economic conditions will also require us 
to intensify our transformation towards a 
business which grows new revenues both 
online and by selling more products, goods 
and services to our readers and users. In 2008, 
this transformation was particularly noticeable 
Chief 
Executive’s 
review
in Norway which is the Group leader in the 
expansion of online revenues and added new 
digital businesses and staff aggressively in  
the first half of the year, with 12 per cent of the 
Norwegian advertising revenues now coming 
from online.
We have now established a Group-wide 
policy of redeployment of resources rather 
than new investment to fuel transformation, 
with journalists being encouraged to produce 
content for different media outlets rather than 
simply printed newspapers. The business is 
run on a weekly basis by a unified European 
management group that includes the CEOs 
of the country divisions, the Chief Operating 
Officer, the Group Finance Director, Group 
Digital Officer and the Group CEO. This 
format is increasingly effective as the 
modernisation programme is rolled out from 
the best performing areas. In addition, there 
is a new and parallel initiative to centralise 
certain other Group functions where there is 
currently overlap between the Group’s head 
office in London and Wegener’s head office 
in Apeldoorn.
The Netherlands
Following extensive discussions and the 
replacement of the Wegener Supervisory  
Board, the new CEO Joop Munsterman  
swiftly set to work on a cost reduction 
plan resulting in a marked improvement to 
the profitability of the daily newspapers in 
particular. Coupled with continued focus on 
profit improvement in Limburg (the results 
of which are reported jointly with Wegener 
in the Netherlands segment), EBITDA
1
 in  
the Netherlands increased from £97.1 million 
in 2007 to £103.4 million in 2008 on static  
revenues of £632.3 million (2007: £636.2 
million).
Wegener’s current reorganisation plan (the 
so-called “Delta” plan), which originally sought 
around 500 job losses, will now be extended 
to include editorial departments.
At the same time the development of online 
newspaper advertising has been slow. 
Productivity improvements in both content 
and sales departments are being sought.
The combination of the Wegener and Limburg 
titles make Mecom the largest Dutch publisher 
with almost one million subscription copies 
a day and weekly household penetration of 
around 80 per cent of the Dutch market. The 
development of that consumer market is the 
management’s priority.
1 All financial information in this review is presented on a like-for-
like basis as explained on page 13.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 15
Overview
Denmark
Berlingske Media has suffered the worst of 
the advertising downturn and has been the 
longest in recession but has been the most 
successful division in the Group in reducing 
costs, down by around six per cent in 2008. 
This cost reduction went some way to 
compensate for the £32.3 million year-on-year 
decline in advertising revenues. Total revenues 
for the year were £371.9 million (2007: £409.0 
million) with EBITDA falling from £32.0 million 
in 2007 to £16.6 million in 2008.
In addition, the business is furthest advanced 
in transformation under the leadership of 
Lisbeth Knudsen, who occupies the roles of 
both editor-in-chief of the flagship national title 
Berlingske Tidende and Danish group CEO. 
The division returned to its refurbished 
headquarters in May and many of the 
traditional departments have disappeared. 
Instead journalists and sales staff are working 
in market groups, supplying a range of 
products, print and online as an integrated 
unit. This is highly developed in business, 
sport and lifestyle market groups and is  
being extended on a monthly basis to other 
content areas. 
The more efficient and revenue building model 
will equip the Danish business to make the 
most of a future return to growth and is being 
rolled out to other divisions during 2009. Whilst 
many restructuring initiatives were completed 
in Denmark during 2008, we anticipate that 
there will be further cost reductions in 2009. 
Norway
Management in the Group’s Norwegian 
division, Edda Media, was changed in the latter 
days of 2008 with Truls Velgaard assuming 
responsibility for Edda Media in addition to his 
responsibility for the Group’s Polish division. 
After a boom in advertising revenue in the first 
months of the year, Norway had a disappointing 
result as both existing businesses and newly 
acquired digital companies saw slowing 
revenues after the summer of 2008. As a 
consequence, total revenues in Norway 
grew slightly from £258.7 million in 2007 
to £267 .6 million in 2008. However, largely 
as a result of extensive investment in new 
revenue areas which contributed to an 
increase in costs of £22.6 million (including a 
decline in associate income from £3.0 million 
in 2007 to £0.9 million in 2008), EBITDA  
fell from £41.7 million in 2007 to £28.0 million 
in 2008.
As a result of the deteriorating advertising 
environment in Norway, Edda Media’s 
aggressive expansion programme, particularly 
in online acquisitions in Norway and Sweden, 
has been halted. 
The fall-off in advertising revenues was 
particularly noticeable in the developing 
national and international markets and action 
has been taken either to curtail cost or  
make disposals. 
However, the character of the local franchises 
remains robust as they represent the leading 
media brands in their areas where increasingly 
they occupy the number one position in online 
as well as in print.
Poland
The Polish division continues to develop 
through product launches in the regional 
newspaper division, particularly in the door-
to-door segment and in online which is 
experiencing the fastest rate of growth in the 
Group, with unique users per month up over 
50 per cent to 4 million. These developments 
were accompanied by growing advertising 
for the early part of 2008 but this tailed off 
decisively in the final months, particularly in 
the national newspaper division.
Subscription sales of the national title 
Rzeczpospolita declined only modestly during 
2008 as some of its rival publications saw 
significant circulation reductions. 
Modest declines in both circulation and 
advertising revenues (the latter caused by 
the ending of national advertising sales joint 
venture, whereas underlying advertising was 
up) contributed to a decline in overall revenues 
from £143.8 million in 2007 to £136.5 million in 
2008 with cost reductions mitigating much of 
this. EBITDA in 2008 was £9.1 million (2007: 
£11.4 million).
 
Germany
Advertising decline and inflationary influences 
were countered by energetic cost control 
in Berlin and Hamburg under the leadership 
of CEO and Berliner Zeitung editor-in-chief 
Josef Depenbrock. As a result the business 
ended 2008 with a higher profit margin than 
at the time of acquisition by Mecom. In 2008, 
shortfalls in revenue were in part mitigated by 
cost control, with revenues in 2008 of £119.3 
million (2007: £123.2 million) and EBITDA in 
2008 of £15.3 million (2007: £16.9 million).
Circulation has stabilised as a result of greater 
marketing effort that curtailed some profit 
development in 2008. Berliner Zeitung, a quality 
broadsheet, is close to becoming the largest 
circulation newspaper in the city, the gap 
having narrowed with BZ, the popular tabloid, 
during Mecom’s ownership. The continuing 
strong circulations of the titles represented 
a strong selling point in negotiations with the 
new owners, DuMont Schauberg.
We thank the employees of the German 
businesses for their hard work and 
commitment during our period of ownership 
in which we sought to develop and secure the 
titles for the future.
Online
Digital revenue in 2008 was £62.8 million, up 
by £11.8 million or 23 per cent year-on-year, 
reflecting an increase in online newspaper 
advertising sales and small bolt-on 
acquisitions. Management has changed the 
strategy of having dedicated staff for online 
and introduced integrated work across both 
digital and print platforms. This is designed 
to increase productivity in sales and content 
production markedly and to create many 
products from one central hub. 
The objective is to exploit a wider market of 
consumers and advertisers with a greater 
range of products that use common content 
origination and production. This transformation 
process will gain momentum during 2009.
Outlook
The trend in advertising revenue decline 
has steepened in the first months of 2009 
against challenging comparisons in the  
early part of 2008. In the first quarter advertising 
revenues were down 20 per cent, although 
the year-on-year comparison is complicated 
by the timing of Easter. Cost reduction has 
also accelerated in the first quarter to partly 
compensate for this trend. Subscription 
revenues remain broadly stable. The benefit of 
the efficiency measures is now less likely to be 
affected in the future by inflationary pressures.
The outlook continues to be unpredictable 
without great prospect of rapid improvement. 
Nevertheless the management is focused on 
a rapid modernisation programme to create 
a content and consumer business which is 
not only efficient but can take advantage of  
broader markets when the economy improves.
David Montgomery
Chief Executive

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 17
Overview
In addition the holders of a £30.6 million 
convertible loan note which was due for 
payment on 12 April 2009, have agreed an 
extension of the maturity date to 12 July 2009, 
although this extension will accelerate to 31 
May 2009 should the Group not proceed with 
its equity raising or if certain insolvency events 
arise.
Note 4 in the consolidated financial statements 
sets out the going concern considerations 
related to the above.
Like-for-like financial performance
Group revenue fell by 3 per cent from 
£1,570.9 million to £1,527 .6 million in the  
year to 31 December 2008, driven by a  
decline in advertising revenue for the full year 
of 6 per cent. 
Full-year advertising fell £50.0 million to 
£772.6 million and was down in all the 
Group’s operations apart from Norway, which 
benefited from the effect of some local bolt-
on acquisitions and strong digital growth. 
The steepest decline in advertising was in 
Denmark, at 17 per cent, as the current 
economic conditions compounded the effect 
of an already highly competitive advertising 
market. The Dutch advertising market in 
contrast performed relatively strongly and 
was only down 4 per cent on 2007 as the 
economic downturn took longer to affect  
that country. 
Circulation revenue grew by 2 per cent across 
the Group, as falling volumes continued to 
be more than offset by price increases. Over 
75 per cent of circulation revenue derives 
from subscriptions; this proportion is over 
95 per cent in the Netherlands and Norway. 
Circulation revenues fell in Germany and 
Poland, where the proportion of newsstand 
sales is highest.
Printing revenue increased marginally from 
£95.0 million to £96.7 million. Enterprises 
revenues grew by 30 per cent, which included 
strong growth in the Netherlands especially  
in the Wegener business. Other revenues fell 
by £9.8 million, including decreases in third-
party distribution.
An increase of £3.1 million in Group revenue 
in the first half of 2008 was followed by a 
reduction of £46.4 million in the second 
half of the year. The main cause of this was 
a decrease in advertising revenue of £41.7 
million, or 10 per cent, in the second half, 
caused by the continuing competition and the 
difficult economic conditions that affected the 
countries in which Mecom operates. 
Digital revenue, which is largely included 
within advertising above, increased from 
£51.0 million to £62.8 million, an increase of 23 
per cent. Strong growth in the first half of the 
year and the effect of acquisitions made early 
in 2008 were dampened by the effect of the 
economic downturn on some digital activities, 
in particular online recruitment.
New financial platform
As announced in the October 2008 Interim 
Management Statement, the Board of Mecom 
recognised the need to deleverage the balance 
sheet to address a more challenging economic 
outlook. Since then, Mecom has completed 
two significant asset disposals in Germany 
and Northwestern Norway at the same time 
as increasing focus on cost minimisation 
and cash conservation. Simultaneously 
Mecom has been in discussions with both 
its banks and its shareholders concerning an 
agreement on an appropriate capital structure 
for the long-term. 
On 29 April 2009, certain Mecom  
shareholders and new institutions signed non-
binding letters of support for an equity issue 
to raise approximately £140 million (before 
expenses). This support is conditional on, 
amongst other things, the Group agreeing 
final facility documentation with its lenders 
(the principal commercial terms of which have 
already received credit approval from each 
of the lenders); the issue of a prospectus in 
connection with an equity issue; and relevant 
shareholder resolutions being passed. 
The key terms of the new bank deal, assuming 
the equity issue takes place as planned, will 
include:
total facilities of circa €600 million, including •	
a term facility maturing in October 2013 of 
€350 million, a revolving credit facility of up 
to €200 million maturing in October 2013 
and an additional term loan facility of circa 
€50 million; 
the amount of the revolving credit facility •	
will vary according to the Group’s projected 
working capital requirements and to the 
amount of gross cash on the Group’s 
balance sheet;
margin on the term loan facility of 350 basis •	
points over the relevant inter-bank rate, 
with a 200 basis points additional non-
cash margin on the additional term loan 
facility accruing from 1 January 2010 and 
increasing by a further 200 basis points 
on 1 June 2010 and by a further 200 basis 
points on 1 January 2011;
margin on the revolving credit facility of 300 •	
basis points;
cash margin under both the term and •	
revolving credit facilities are subject to 
downward adjustment in the event that the 
Group’s leverage falls below 3.0 times or 
2.0 times respectively;
leverage, interest cover and operating cash •	
flow covenants tested at 30 June 2010, 31 
December 2010 and quarterly thereafter; 
June 2010 leverage covenant of 5.25 times, •	
falling to 4.50 times at 31 December 2010;
covenants on the total capital expenditure •	
and exceptional items of the Group, tested 
annually from 31 December 2009; and
warrants over the Company’s shares •	
issued to the banks which would represent 
5 per cent of the existing (pre-equity issue) 
share capital of the Company.
The Group’s cost base (including share of 
results of associates) was reduced by 1 per 
cent, or £15.2 million. This net reduction reflects 
the Group’s restructuring programmes and 
the effect of disposals, offset by inflationary 
pressure on the cost base and additional costs 
from acquired businesses. On an underlying 
basis, stripping out the effect of inflation and 
acquisitions, staff costs were down 5 per cent 
on the prior year. Average full-time equivalent 
employees fell by 830, or 7 per cent, between 
2007 and 2008. 
The cost base fell in all countries other than 
Norway, where high country inflation and 
acquisitions and investment in new businesses 
drove a cost base increase of 10 per cent. The 
cost base fell by 6 per cent in Denmark, which 
has carried out a substantial reorganisation of 
its Copenhagen operations.
Restructuring the business is continuing and 
management is targeting a further reduction 
of the cost base by €75 million in 2009 driven 
by a combination of the full year effect of 
2008 initiatives, further headcount reduction, 
the benefits of the Danish print restructuring 
and a further clampdown on discretionary 
spend. The tough economic conditions mean 
management teams are constantly reviewing 
additional cost saving measures.
Group EBITDA fell by £28.1 million, or 15 per 
cent, from £191.4 million to £163.3 million, 
reflecting the excess in the reduction of 
revenues, in particular advertising, over the 
reduction in the cost base. EBITDA grew in  
the Netherlands, which was affected last by  
the fall in advertising revenue and benefited 
from cost reduction measures, but reduced 
in all other countries. The falls were most 
pronounced in Denmark, down £15.4 million 
or 48.1 per cent, where advertising revenue 
decline was sharpest of all the Group’s 
operations, and Norway, down £13.7 million or 
33 per cent, where the growth in the cost base 
could not be contained to match a second half 
decline in revenue. Central costs increased to 
£9.1 million from £7.7 million reflecting a full 
year of the London full head office. EBITDA 
margin was 10.7 per cent, down 1.5 points 
from 2007. EBITDA margin was highest in the 
Netherlands at 16 per cent (2007: 15 per cent) 
and lowest in Denmark at 4 per cent (2007: 8 
per cent). 
Depreciation increased by 8 per cent to £58.7 
million reflecting the significant investment in 
print assets in the Netherlands, the refit and 
refurbishment of the Copenhagen office and 
investment in IT systems. The depreciation 
charge for the disposed German and 
Northwest Norwegian assets was £5.0 million. 
Operating profit was £104.6 million (2007: 
£137 .0 million), with an operating margin of 
6.8 per cent, down 1.9 points from 2007. As 
with EBITDA, the range of operating margins 
is wide, from 13 per cent in the Netherlands 
per cent to 1 per cent in Denmark.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 18 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Overview
Mecom has 
substantial 
operations in 
the Netherlands, 
Denmark, Norway, 
and Poland managed 
by Country CEOs 
with extensive 
journalistic and 
industry experience.
Market 
overview
The Netherlands
The Netherlands has a population of 16 million 
and GDP grew by 2 per cent in 2008.
The paid-for newspapers saw their circulation 
decline by an average of 2.4 per cent over 
the year, with the circulation decline highest 
amongst the national dailies. Newspaper 
circulations in the paid-for daily regional 
markets declined by 1.6 per cent in 2008. 
The newspaper market in the Netherlands was 
estimated to be worth £1,244 million in 2008 
and has been growing at an annual rate of 
0.3 per cent since 2003. In 2008, newspaper 
advertising constituted approximately 20 per 
cent of the total advertising market which 
grew by 3.7 per cent. However, the markets 
deteriorated in the second half of 2008.
There are three major operators in the Dutch 
market: Mecom, Telegraaf Media Group 
(“TMG”) and PCM Uitgevers. These operators 
constitute 75 per cent of the total newspaper 
market. The remainder of the market consists 
of various medium sized and smaller players. 
TMG is the market leader in the national daily 
market, through its title De Telegraaf, with a 15 
per cent share of the total newspaper market. 
Mecom is the leader in the regional newspaper 
market and has a 59 per cent market share. 
The weekly free-sheet market is fragmented, 
with Mecom the market leader with a 38 per 
cent market share. 
The Netherlands has the highest internet 
penetration in Europe, reaching almost 90 
per cent of the population. Online advertising 
has continued to grow rapidly in 2008 and 
constituted 10 per cent of the Dutch advertising 
market, up from 8 per cent in 2007 . Online 
advertising sales in the Netherlands were 
approximately €450 million in 2008.
Sources: PricewaterhouseCoopers – Global Entertainment and 
Media Outlook report, HOI, Media Audit Bureau, Nielsen Media 
Research.
Denmark
Denmark has a population of over five million 
and GDP declined by 0.9 per cent in 2008. 
Newspaper circulations in the paid-for national 
daily market in Denmark declined by 6.8 per 
cent across 2008, and regional newspaper 
circulations declined by approximately 4.5 per 
cent. The newspaper market in Denmark was 
estimated to be worth £991 million in 2008 
and has declined 5 per cent since 2007 . 
Newspaper advertising was estimated to be 
worth £565 million in 2008 and constituted 37 
per cent of the total advertising market against 
42 per cent in 2007. The total advertising 
market is expected to be £1,502 million in 
2008, a decline of 3 per cent compared with 
2007 . Newspaper advertising declined by 5 per 
cent in 2008 compared with 2007. Advertising 
in the paid-for newspapers declined by 16.7 
per cent with nationals down by 18.2 per cent, 
regionals down by 14.2 per cent and locals 
down by 13.4 per cent.
There are two major newspaper publishing 
operators in the Danish market: Berlingske and 
JP/Politikens Hus. These operators constitute 
50 per cent of the total newspaper market.
Sondagsavisen publishes the leading weekly 
free-sheet, Sondagsavisen, with several 
regional editions and has a significant 
distribution business (which is in the process 
of being disposed). The daily free-sheet 
market has been intensely competitive, with 
three daily titles including MetroXpress (Metro 
International), URBAN (Mecom), 24 Timer (JP/
Politikens Hus). The weekly local free-sheet 
market is concentrated, with Berlingske and 
JP/Politikens Hus being the market leaders. 
Berlingske has an estimated 20 per cent 
share of this market. In 2008, MetroXpress 
and 24 Timer merged their activities into one 
company but still publishes two newspapers. 
Following the merger, 24 Timer reduced its 
circulation.
Online advertising is estimated to be worth 
£304 million and has continued to grow at 
an estimated 20 per cent in 2008. Denmark’s 
internet penetration in 2008 was over 80.4 per 
cent; 90 per cent of those who have an internet 
connection at home have broadband.
Sources: Danske Dagblades Forening, Danmark Statistik, FDIM, 
Gallup, Dansk Oplagskontrol, www.internetworldstats.com, 
www.dst.dk, www.delokaleugeaviser.dk.
 
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 19
Overview
Norway
The population of Norway is over four million 
and GDP in 2008 is estimated to have grown 
by 2 per cent in 2008.
The newspaper advertising market in Norway 
(excluding inserts and free-sheets) was 
estimated to be worth £680 million in 2008 
and declined by 4.4 per cent compared to 
2007. 
Newspaper advertising (including inserts and 
free-sheets) constituted 41 per cent of the total 
advertising market in 2008, a small decrease 
compared to 2007. The total advertising market 
declined by 0.5 per cent in 2008. Newspaper 
circulations declined by 2.8 per cent in 2008. 
Whilst the national tabloid declined by 8.4 
per cent, the circulation of local newspapers 
market remained stable. 
There are three major operators in Norway 
who, between them, account for 64 per cent of 
the total newspaper market. Schibsted has a 
33 per cent market share through the national 
tabloid, VG, the morning paper, Aftenposten, 
and its majority ownership of the main regional 
newspapers such as Bergens Tidende, 
Stavanger Aftenblad, Faedrelandsvenennen 
and Adresseavisen. Edda Media had a 13 
per cent share in 2008 through its strong 
position in the local newspaper segment. 
It also owns a number of local online news 
websites, national online niche positions and 
several local radio and television stations. 
Edda Media’s market share after the disposal 
of Northwestern assets to Polaris Media ASA, 
is 10 per cent. A-pressen has a 17 per cent 
market share through its strong position in the 
local newspaper segment. Dagbladet, owned 
by the Berner Group, is the second largest 
national tabloid with a 5 per cent share of the 
national newspaper circulation. The weekly 
free-sheet market consists of local community 
based weekly free-sheets, where Edda Media 
is the dominant and leading player with a total 
of 12 titles (17 editions) and a 50 per cent share 
of the free-sheet advertising market.
Online advertising has continued to grow 
rapidly and in 2008 constituted 10 per cent 
of the Norwegian advertising market, up from 
9.5 per cent in 2007. The online advertising 
market was estimated to be worth £180 
million in 2008. Norway is one of the leading 
European internet markets with penetration of 
88 per cent.
Sources: TNS-Gallup, Norwegian Circulation Control, IRM.
Note: Numbers disclosed includes Northwest Norway assets 
unless mentioned otherwise.
Poland
The population of Poland is over 38 million and 
GDP grew by 4.9 per cent in 2008. 
The newspaper market in Poland was 
estimated to be worth £456 million in 2008. 
The total advertising market grew by 10.5 per 
cent in 2008 against 12.8 per cent in 2007 . 
The advertising market in Poland has been 
growing in recent years in line with the strong 
economy. The newspaper advertising market 
grew by 5.4 per cent in 2008 representing 13 
per cent of the total advertising market.
The newspaper circulation market is estimated 
to be worth approximately £317 million. 
Newspaper circulations in the paid-for national, 
daily free-sheets and daily regionals markets 
have declined by 6 per cent, 12 per cent and 
14 per cent respectively in 2008. Despite this, 
the value of this market increased by 2 per 
cent due to the growth of cover prices.
Competition within the paid-for newspaper 
market is very strong, especially in newspaper 
sales. There are four major operators in Poland 
who, between them, account for 76 per cent of 
the total paid-for newspaper market. Mecom 
owns Rzeczpospolita, the leading upmarket 
daily newspaper, business daily Parkiet and 
12 regional newspapers across Poland, giving 
a 19 per cent share of the total market. Axel 
Springer, with a 28 per cent share, publishes 
Fakt, Poland’s largest newspaper, two sports 
dailies and Dziennik, a daily national. Grupa 
Wydawnicza Polskapresse is the largest 
publisher of regional newspapers with a 13 per 
cent share of the total newspaper market. 
Agora publishes the daily Gazeta Wyborcza 
and the national free paper Metro, and has a 
16 per cent market share. 
Online advertising grew by 33 per cent in 
2008, constituting 10 per cent of the Polish 
advertising market. There are approximately 
15.4 million internet users in Poland, a 10 
per cent increase from 2007 . Broadband 
penetration in 2008 was 79 per cent, a 7 per 
cent increase on 2007 .
Sources: GUS, CR Media Consulting, Expert Monitor, ZKDP, 
NetTrack, Millward Brown.

Divisional review
Divisional 
review
The Netherlands
The Group’s Dutch division comprises 
Wegener and Limburg Media Group (“LMG”). 
In May 2008, Jan Houwert stepped down as 
the CEO of Wegener and was replaced by 
Joop Munsterman; Johan Boermann is the 
CEO of LMG.
Wegener is the largest publisher of regional 
daily newspapers and free door-to-door 
newspapers in the Netherlands. LMG is a 
significant regional newspaper business in the 
Dutch province of Limburg and in the south 
and east of the Netherlands. With its online 
portfolio of newspaper websites and stand-
alone niche websites serving customers, 
communities and advertisers, the Dutch 
division now has nine million unique users 
every month up from eight million in 2007 . 
This supplements its newspaper readership 
of 11.8 million every week and extending the 
reach of the division’s content well beyond  
its traditional newspaper audience. 
In a challenging year, Mecom increased its 
share of the total Dutch printed newspaper 
advertising market from 25.3 per cent to 25.6 
per cent and its circulation market share from 
19.9 per cent in 2007 to 20.6 per cent in 2008. 
Wegener improved the market position of its 
dailies by limiting the decline in circulation to 
1.8 per cent, compared to a national decline 
of 5.5 per cent for all dailies, and increased 
revenues from circulation by 3.3 per cent due 
to price rises. The Wegener free door-to-door 
newspapers had another good year with 
advertising revenues rising by 5.8 per cent as 
the strategy of achieving national coverage 
continued to be implemented, in particular 
through the repositioning of De Weekkrant 
as a national brand for regional free door-to-
door newspapers. Wegener strengthened its 
position in the Netherlands’ three northern 
provinces through the launch of new weekly 
newspapers at the beginning of 2008 and 
has continued to expand in 2009 through two 
joint ventures with Buijze Pers and Rodi Pers 
covering the western part of the Netherlands.
In Wegener, there has been a continued  
growth in the internet as an advertising  
medium by 16 per cent in 2008, following an 
increase of 28 per cent in 2007 . 
All Wegener and LMG dailies have a website 
operating alongside the printed newspaper 
and they increasingly refer readers and 
visitors to one another. By concentrating on its 
leading regional brands (such as BN/De Stem, 
Brabants Dagblad, Dagblad De Limburger, 
De Gelderlander, De Stentor, De Twentsche 
Courant Tubantia, Limburgs Dagblad), the 
Dutch division grew its newspaper site  
unique users by over 38 per cent. During  
2008 this portfolio was expanded by the 
launch of a new website, deweekkrant.nl, an 
online companion site for the division’s free 
door-to-door newspapers, which provides 
local communities across the Netherlands with 
access to local news. This new site attracted 
more than 500,000 unique users per month 
within three months of its launch.
A year of change
New management tackles  >
radical cultural change
Major restructuring >
Now circa 50 per cent  >
of Mecom’s revenue
Relaunch of LMG  >
titles as tabloid
Sources: HOI, Nielsen Media Research.
The unique users of the division’s stand- 
alone sites grew by over 25 per cent with 
autotrack.nl (the Netherlands’ leading 
automotive niche portal) and jobtrack.nl  
(one of the leading job search portals) both 
improving their positions in highly competitive 
markets. LMG launched many new websites 
in 2008 and increased its number of unique 
users by 50 per cent compared to 2007 .
Wegener’s Enterprises business made good 
progress during 2008, selling increasing 
volumes of goods and services to readers by 
marketing them through the division’s print 
and online portfolio. The Dutch Enterprises 
portfolio now includes holidays, home interior 
products, ticketing, wine, as well as books 
and collections of CDs and DVDs.
In addition to the synergies and savings 
generated by reorganisation, during the course 
of 2008 the Dutch businesses invested over 
£36.0 million in their printing plants, improving 
office automation for all employees, renewing 
all the news sites of the Wegener dailies 
and developing new platforms for autotrack.
nl and jobtrack.nl. The largest portion of this 
investment was devoted to upgrading and 
expanding the printing facility in Best and 
upgrading the existing presses in Apeldoorn 
and Enschede. This provides more colour 
capacity so that all dailies can be printed in 
full colour. The investment in the Best facility, 
which has resulted in the closure of the Breda 
facility and will in 2009 result in the closure 
of the Nijmegen facility, will deliver greater 
efficiency as well as the availability of full colour 
printing for all Wegener newspapers. These 
investments in printing plants will not only result 
in greater efficiencies but also a better quality 
product for readers and advertisers with 
more colour positions for content including 
advertisements. This will also contribute to 
better environmental practices. 
Whilst Wegener and LMG continue to be run 
as separate businesses, 2008 has seen the 
implementation of an intensive collaboration 
programme between the two companies with 
LMG outsourcing a number of operations to 
Wegener thereby enabling both businesses to 
capitalise on economies of scale.
The Dutch division will continue to progress 
the transformation strategy in 2009 focusing 
on new multi-platform products as well as 
the integration of editorial, marketing and 
sales staff to facilitate the development of 
new revenues alongside the collection and 
production of digital and print content. 
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 21
Divisional review
Mobile  
reporting
The challenge:
To start reporting through mobile phones across all 
Wegener newspapers in a professional way.
The solution:
Half of the editorial staff of all the 
Wegener newspapers were given a 
Nokia 95 or a Nokia 96 mobile phone 
and were challenged to use it during 
their “normal work” hours after 
receiving intensive training.
The result:
Enthusiastic journalists using their 
Nokia mobile phones reporting directly 
to the websites during soccer games, 
submitting their own photos and 
articles and presenting reports from 
live events.

Financial overview – like-for-like
Total revenue fell by £3.9 million, or 1 per 
cent, from £636.2 million to £632.3 million. 
Advertising revenue fell by 4 per cent to 
£348.5 million, reflecting the onset of the 
economic downturn at the end of the year 
and the disposal of the De Trompetter titles in 
March 2008. The deterioration in advertising 
was most pronounced in the second half of 
2008, falling by 8 per cent, and has affected 
the paid-for dailies to a greater extent than the 
weekly papers. 
Circulation revenue increased by 4 per cent  
as price increases, which were brought 
forward within the year, more than offset 
declines in circulation volumes. 95 per cent 
of circulation revenue in the Netherlands is 
subscription-based.
Other revenue was higher, up £3.0 million to 
£54.3 million, as a result of greater third-party 
printing and higher Enterprises sales, which 
grew strongly albeit from a low base. Total 
costs (including share of results of associates) 
fell by £10.2 million, or 2 per cent, to £528.9 
million, reflecting the restructuring during the 
year and previously, as well as the disposal 
of De Trompetter. Considerable elements of 
back office functions from the two previously 
separate businesses were combined during 
the year.
EBITDA was £103.4 million, up £6.3 million (or 
6 per cent) from 2007 . EBITDA margins held 
up well in the full year (up 1.1pts to 16.4 per 
cent) and also in the second half of the year 
(up again 1.1pts to 16.1 per cent), despite the 
deterioration in advertising revenue, as cost 
benefits and higher circulation and other 
revenue offset the advertising decline.
Depreciation increased by £2.7 million to £22.9 
million, reflecting the investment in printing 
equipment during the year, resulting in operating 
profit up £3.6 million to £80.5 million.
Financial overview – reported
The sharp increase in the reported revenue 
and operating profit between 2007 and 
2008 results from a full year’s ownership of 
the Wegener business, which was acquired 
in October 2007. Operating exceptional 
charges totalled £45.8 million (2007: £7.0 
million), primarily related to staff redundancy. 
Amortisation of acquired intangibles was 
£34.3 million (2007: £9.7 million) and an 
impairment charge of £543.7 million (2007: 
£nil) was recognised against the carrying 
amount of goodwill, resulting in an operating 
loss after exceptional items and amortisation 
of acquired intangibles of £543.3 million (2007: 
profit of £14.0 million).

Divisional review
Denmark
A landmark year
New Copenhagen model 
provides the template 
for transformation

Rebranded and relocated  >
to a state of the art

Aggressive expansion  >

Refocus has reduced  >

Berlingske Media (“Berlingske”) is Denmark’s 
largest news publishing group producing 
content for print, online, online TV, radio  
and mobile phones. The activities of 
Berlingske span across Jutland and Zealand 
with its headquarters located in the centre 
of Copenhagen. During 2008, Berlingske 
rebranded from Det Berlingkse Officin to 
Berlingske Media, building a new identity.
Berlingske is one of two national publishers 
of quality newspapers in Denmark. It has a 
portfolio of three daily paid-for national titles, 
one national free-sheet, a weekly paid-for 
national newspaper, a national business 
magazine, six local daily newspapers operating 
under the name of Midtjyske Medier and one 
partly owned regional newspaper operating 
under the name of Syddanske Medier. Many 
of the division’s paid-for newspapers are 
subscription based. 
Berlingske is also one of the leading publishers 
of free newspapers with 50 local weekly 
titles, primarily in the Jutland and Zealand 
regions of Denmark. The division’s major 
free newspaper URBAN, which is aimed at 
the commuter market nationally, had a 2008 
daily circulation of approximately 196,000 and 
a daily readership of approximately 408,000. 
URBAN is the second largest daily free-sheet 
in Denmark in terms of readership. In 2008 
Berlingske re-launched several of its daily 
newspapers including Berlingske Tidende, 
URBAN and Århus Stiftstidende. 
Berlingske Media decreased its share of the 
total Danish dailies advertising market from 36 
per cent in 2007 to 31 per cent in 2008. The 
main reason for this decrease is the exposure 
of Berlingske to the recruitment and property 
market, two areas which are highly sensitive to 
the current economic climate. The same trend 
is seen in the regional and local newspaper 
market.
In a challenging business environment 
Berlingske Media had an intensive year. It 
moved into new headquarters in Copenhagen, 
bringing together Erhvervsbladet, URBAN, 
WeekendAvisen, B.T ., Berlingske Tidende and 
Berlingske Nyhedsmagasin, and many of its 
online activities, under one roof. Four buildings 
have now been consolidated into one modern 
media hub with over 1,100 employees, a 
newsroom for four of Berlingske’s newspapers 
and a highly professional TV studio ready to 
produce online TV. 
As well as consolidating the editorial assets 
and thinking innovatively about journalism, 
Berlingske has put in place a centralised 
advertising sales desk with two centres 
servicing east and west Denmark. It is also 
moving towards having a single point of 
contact for buyers so they can buy a package 
combining several media at once.
Berlingske has increased efforts to streamline 
purchasing by carrying out a wholesale review 
of travel, marketing, and office equipment, 
with clear goals identified for savings.
With more than 70 websites and 7.7 million 
unique users every month, Berlingske is 
focusing on the rapidly growing online 
advertising market principally through the 
cross promotion of its online newspaper sites 
such as berlingske.dk, business.dk and bt.dk, 
the three strongest national online media 
brands. Mecom also part owns several leading 
online classified sites including jobzonen.dk 
(the second largest online recruitment site) 
and bilzonen.dk (the second largest online  
motor vehicle site).
During the year, eight new content websites 
were launched as well as a new web shop 
to showcase the division’s brand endorsed 
goods and services (Enterprises). New site 
launches include lidtmere.dk, spilop.dk, 
sporten.dk, rejseliv.dk, dinepenge.dk, dinby.
dk, spotted.stiften.dk, fri.dk and new sites for 
all Berlingske’s free local weeklies.
Berlingske is leading the market with its 
development of its Enterprises business in 
Denmark, adopting a far more commercial 
approach than its rivals. In 2009, Enterprises 
growth will be driven by events and seminars, 
and new business-to-business services aimed 
at small- and medium-sized companies. 
Source: Danske Dagblades Forening.

Financial overview – like-for-like
Total revenue fell by £37 . 1 million, or 9 per cent, 
during the year to 31 December 2008 from 
£409.0 million to £371.9 million. Advertising 
revenue fell by 17 per cent to £160.1 million, 
reflecting the highly competitive advertising 
and the effects of the economic downturn. 
All the division’s main titles were adversely 
affected, particularly the national Berlingske 
Tidende title, which accounts for around 30 
per cent of the division’s advertising revenue, 
and URBAN, the largest Mecom Denmark 
free-sheet. The decline in advertising revenue 
accelerated in the second half, from 14 per 
cent to 20 per cent. 
Circulation revenue increased by 3 per cent, 
with volume declines of around 5 per cent 
more than compensated for by price increases. 
Other revenue fell by 9 per cent, mostly driven 
by lower third-party printing and distribution 
revenue (which between them comprise three 
quarters of other revenue).
Total costs (including share of results of 
associates) fell by 6 per cent, reflecting 
the benefits of the rationalisation of the 
Copenhagen operations in a single office 
and an average full-time equivalent employee 
reduction of around 10 per cent during 2008, 
as well as reduced direct costs associated 
with lower revenue (including third-party 
printing and distribution).
As a consequence, EBITDA reduced by £15.4 
million from £32.0 million to £16.6 million, with 
EBITDA margin falling from 7.8 per cent to 
4.5 per cent. Depreciation increased by 13 
per cent from £12.7 million to £14.4 million, 
reflecting the recent investment in office and 
information technology. Operating profit fell 
from £19.3 million to £2.2 million.
Financial overview – reported
Revenue and operating profit differ between 
the like-for-like and reported results only as 
a consequence of movements in foreign 
currency rates.
Operating exceptional items totalled £15.3 
million (2007: £29.1 million), primarily due to the 
costs of redundancy and the reorganisation 
and refurbishment of the Copenhagen office. 
Amortisation of acquired intangibles was 
£13.5 million (2007: £11.7 million) and an 
impairment charge of £147 .5 million (2007: 
£nil) was recognised against the carrying 
amount of goodwill and acquired intangible 
assets, with the result that Denmark recorded 
an operating loss after exceptional items and 
amortisation of acquired intangibles of £175.9 
million (2007: £24.2 million).

Divisional review
Online TV
The challenge:
Ensuring even more value is delivered to people visiting 
Berlingske online. Online TV is an obvious choice, but it  
is not the format that is important, but how it enhances  
the editorial.
The solution:
Constructing a cutting edge online TV 
studio in the main newsroom. Training 
local journalists to become mobile 
journalists, filming and uploading video 
“on the go” using low cost technology 
such as mobile phones, giving an 
immediate first-hand account of  
the news.
The result: 
News with added value, and increased 
interest and use of our websites. 
Berlingske teamed up with competitors 
in the run-up to the US presidential 
election and one national broadcaster 
opted to use Berlingske’s studio 
instead of their own. In addition, local 
newspaper websites have attracted 
visitors from national newspaper 
websites by having their editorial 
enhanced by mobile journalism.

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 26 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Divisional review
Norway
Deep local 
knowledge and 
experience
Breaking the boundaries
Digital leader in the Group >
Building national market  >
online with new products
Strong revenue growth  >
across all products
Restructuring  >
opportunities in print 
and distribution
Edda Media is a major player in the Norwegian 
media industry with daily contact with more 
than one million Norwegians, more than one 
fifth of the population. The division’s 105
1
 
editorial titles are spread across the southern 
part of Norway. 
The product portfolio comprises 44 
newspapers (dailies, weeklies and free-
sheets), 72 websites, and 10 local radio 
and television stations. Edda Media holds a 
leading market position in its core markets  
with more than 70 per cent household  
coverage in 29 geographical areas and  
between 50 per cent and 70 per cent  
coverage in 50 geographical areas.
Edda Media increased its share of the total 
Norwegian printed newspaper advertising 
market (excluding inserts and free-sheets) from 
15.7 per cent to 16.3 per cent and increased 
its circulation market share from 12.3 per cent 
in 2007 to 13.2 per cent in 2008. The division’s 
market position in its subscription-based 
titles decreased in circulation by 2.5 per cent 
compared to national decline of 1.5 per cent 
for all subscription-based titles, but increased 
its revenues from circulation by 2.2 per cent. 
The free door-to-door newspaper advertising 
increased by 2.2 per cent, compared to 
an increase in the market by 3.5 per cent, 
reducing Edda Media’s market share within 
this market by 0.7 percentage points.
The most important brands within Edda 
Media were founded in the 19
th
 century. They 
have a strong position in their respective 
societies and have highly loyal readers and 
subscribers, resulting in a stable circulation 
of more than 340,000 paid-for papers and 
350,000 free-sheets. In total the newspapers 
have 1,290,000 readers comprising 790,000 
daily readers, 175,000 weekly readers and 
330,000 free-sheet readers. 
As a locally based media group, Edda Media’s 
strategy has been to “follow the reader”. All of 
Edda Media’s titles are constantly changing 
and improving their quality and content in line 
with the evolving needs of the users and their 
changing media habits. 
During 2008, Edda Media grew its online 
portfolio with launches in new geographic 
areas, special community editions, and 
new stand-alone sites. Synergies have 
been exploited between the local online 
newspapers and the stand-alone national sites 
(which cover sport, technology, and lifestyle 
themes) enabling the local online newspapers 
to broaden their content proposition. The 
national classified site, tinde.no, and the local 
online newspapers have also worked well 
together and are now further integrated.
Edda Media’s goal is to maintain its strong 
market position and at the same time build a 
strong online market position in local media 
and to increase its digital revenues significantly. 
During 2008 the number of unique visitors for 
its online newspapers increased by 25 per cent 
to 600,000. The traffic growth on the national 
sites was even stronger at 650,000. The Edda 
Media network in total has 1,250,000 unique 
weekly visitors, which represent a growth of 
more than 30 per cent year-on-year. 
Edda Media’s national sites used to be 
organised as separate business units with 
separate editorial offices – one for technology, 
one for sport, one for lifestyle. By the end 
of 2008 all these businesses had merged 
editorial resources into one joint office. This  
has enabled them to work much more 
efficiently, with fewer management resources 
and more content production. Even though 
each journalist has his or her own unique skills, 
they now work across the sites and deliver 
content to the local online newspapers.
The “follow the reader” strategy represents 
a complete transformation of the way 
employees work in order to deliver editorial 
and commercial content. More than 700 
journalists are in the middle of a process 
involving new working methods and content 
production irrespective of platform. The 
strategy demands a new approach from  
the workforce. 
In order to execute its strategy, Edda Media 
reorganised its operational structure in 2008 
under the more cost focused leadership of 
Truls Velgaard who was appointed in October 
2008. The senior management group 
changed its structure from being product-
oriented to being market-oriented. Prior to 
the change, Edda Media had one specialist 
digital business unit but now all business units 
have responsibility for newspapers, online and 
mobile development in their respective market 
areas. Edda Media has defined three main 
markets for its activities: local (which is divided 
into 10 regions); national; and international. In 
revenue terms the local market is currently the 
largest, comprising more than 70 per cent of 
the revenues of Edda Media.
The international market of Edda Media is 
mainly built around three companies: Opoint, 
HR North and NetSprint. Opoint, a business 
providing services to both corporate clients 
and government offices, broadened its service 
offering in the year with the acquisition of Siste 
Nytt, a business offering media monitoring 
services across radio and television. In January 
2008, Edda Media also acquired the Swedish 
company HR North AB, a recruitment site. 
HR North is the market leader in the Swedish 
online recruitment market, and gained market 
share even after the start of the financial 
downturn in the second half of the year. 
NetSprint is an award winning search engine 
company operating in Poland but managed 
as part of the Norwegian operations. 
On 18 February 2009, Mecom announced the 
sale of its Northwestern assets in Norway to 
Polaris Media ASA and the disposal completed 
on 2 April 2009.
1 All numbers quoted are before the disposal of Northwestern 
assets which completed on 2 April 2009.
Sources: Norwegian Circulation Control, IRM.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 27
Divisional review
Innsida.no – from 
web to paper
The challenge:
Innsida.no is a local online news site that covers four towns 
in the highly competitive northern region around Bømlo 
Fitjar, Kvinnherad and Stord. Whilst growing its audience 
well, Edda Media realised that the Innsida brand had further 
potential, to expand its reach and its appeal to both local 
advertisers and local readers.
The solution:
In May 2008 Edda Media launched a 
new free-sheet newspaper with the 
same brand: Innsida. The newspaper  
is distributed once a week to every 
household in the area (15,000). The 
circulation figure is twice as high as 
that of the main local competitor.
The result:
This move has strengthened Edda 
Media’s market position in the region, 
increased the consumer awareness  
of innsida.no, and given people in  
the region more choice and a  
better proposition.

Divisional review
Financial overview – like-for-like
Total revenue grew by 3 per cent from £258.7 
million in the year to 31 December 2007 to 
£267 .6 million in 2008. Advertising grew by 
4 per cent: there was strong growth in the 
first half of the year and the division benefited 
from the effect of bolt-on digital acquisitions 
made early in 2008; the second half of the 
year saw a decline of 5 per cent, however, as 
the weakening economic conditions affected 
advertising markets, with recruitment revenue 
hit hardest and earliest. Circulation revenues 
grew by 3 per cent, or £2.0 million, as price 
rises more than offset declines in volume. 
Other revenue increased by 3 per cent from 
£52.0 million to £53.7 million, mainly as a result 
of increases in printing.
Total costs (including share of results of 
associates) increased by 10 per cent from  
£217.0 million to £239.6 million, reflecting 
the effect of acquisitions (accounting for 
approximately half of the increase) and the 
strong underlying cost inflation in the Norwegian 
economy. Staff inflation was 6 per cent, 
offsetting the effect of previous restructuring.
EBITDA fell from £41.7 million to £28.0 million. 
After modest growth in the first half, second 
half EBITDA of £7.0 million was £15.6 million 
lower than the equivalent period in 2007 , 
reflecting falling advertising revenues and the 
higher cost base. EBITDA margin decreased 
from 16.1 per cent to 10.5 per cent.
Financial overview – reported
Revenue and operating profit differ between 
the like-for-like and reported results only  
as a consequence of movements in foreign 
currency rates.
Operating exceptional items totalled £3.3 
million (2007: £3.3 million), primarily due to the 
costs of redundancy. Amortisation of acquired 
intangibles was £9.4 million (2007: £8.3 
million) and a goodwill impairment charge of 
£138.6 million (2007: £nil) was recorded, with 
the result that Norway recorded an operating 
loss after exceptional items and amortisation 
of acquired intangibles of £137 .0 million (2007: 
profit of £15.1 million).

Poland
Enhancing  
its position
National sales  >
brought inhouse
Continued roll out  >
of new super local 
weeklies Moje Miasto
Strong growth in  >

Rzeczpospolita  >

Media Regionalne  >

The Group’s Polish division comprises 
Media Regionalne, a regional newspaper 
and content business, and a 51 per cent 
share of Presspublica, which is the owner of 
Rzeczpospolita, one of the most respected 
titles in Poland. Presspublica also publishes a 
number of business and legal publications as 
well as operating the business website parkiet.
com. The Polish division also operates more 
than 40 websites and eight printing plants that 
print both Group and third-party publications 
and newspapers. 
Presspublica maintained its share of the total 
Polish national printed newspaper advertising 
market at 17 per cent in 2008 and maintained 
its circulation market share at 10 per cent. 
Presspublica’s market position of its dailies 
decreased in circulation by 4.5 per cent 
compared to the national decline of 5.8 per 
cent for all national dailies, and maintained 
revenues from circulation. Media Regionalne 
increased its share of the total Polish regional 
printed newspaper advertising market to 14 
per cent in 2008 from 13 per cent in 2007 and 
increased its circulation market share by 2.2 
per cent.
To reinforce Presspublica’s position in the 
market, Rzeczpospolita launched a new 
television guide, a new high-quality lifestyle and 
business monthly magazine, First Class, and a 
new daily supplement for the SOHO (“Small 
Office Home Office”) market, GPP, in 2008. 
The production teams of Zycie Warszawy and 
the Warsaw supplement of Rzeczpospolita 
were merged in 2008. Zycie Warszawy 
remains as a separate paid-for title but is 
published as a supplement to Rzeczpospolita 
in the Warsaw edition. This has led to editorial 
and marketing co-operation with a major local 
television station and with the City Council. 
Media Regionalne has embarked on an 
extensive restructuring in 2008 by merging all 
Media Regionalne entities into one company.  
This enables Media Regionalne to be better 
organised and managed and provides better 
access to information and databases for its 
customers and readers.
One initiative launched by Media Regionalne 
was the “Safe roads” project to promote 
behaviours to reduce the danger on Polish 
roads. Free door-to-door MM Lublin and four 
commuter free-sheets Teraz, were launched 
in the cities of Rzeszow, Kielce, Radom and 
Opole. With the exception of free-sheet Teraz, 
all newspapers have online companion sites.
The Polish division’s transformation into 
a content business is continuing apace. 
Integrated newsrooms are being set up and 
journalists are increasingly working across 
both print and online publications, with content 
first being published online.
Newsroom convergence in Media Regionalne 
means that web exclusive comments written 
by its leading columnists are now posted every 
morning. Video comments on the most widely 
debated issues are posted every evening and 
video interviews with prominent politicians 
and celebrities are made on a regular basis. 
Breaking news is published online and offline 
as soon as it has been thoroughly researched 
and double-checked.
A new look and feel has been created for the 
online newspapers, increasing their appeal 
to consumers, and making them the fastest 
growing media in each region. The sales 
teams attended rigorous online advertising 
training and in 2008, online advertising 
revenue reached approximately 7 per cent of 
Polish division’s total advertising revenues.
Media Regionalne had a very active year online, 
and its sites achieved 100 per cent growth in 
user numbers year-on-year. It significantly 
expanded the reach of Moje Miasto, an 
innovative combination of a local weekly free-
sheet and a local community website. It is a 
completely new product offering in the Polish 
market which is attractive to both readers and 
advertisers. In 2008 print and online Moje 
Miastos were launched in Lublin and eight 
stand-alone local community websites were 
launched in the biggest cities in Poland, being 
new markets for Media Regionalne. Moje 
Miasto is growing very fast and it currently 
attracts an average of 580,000 unique users 
per month. In addition, Media Regionalne 
launched 12 regional websites which are more 
interactive and modern. This has enabled 
Media Regionalne to increase its monthly 
unique users to an average of 2,100,000.
Poland’s digital operations achieved a 
significant increase in its audience numbers 
over the year, with monthly unique users 
increasing to over four million per month (up 
from 2.6 million per month in 2007). National 
brands like Rzeczpospolita and regional 
brands like Echo Dnia and Glos Dziennik 
Pomorza enhanced their online presence by 
re-launching their websites during the year, 
and introducing innovative concepts like 
Mobile Citizen Journalism (“MoDO”). MoDO is 
a mobile application for journalists, first used 
on the Moje Miasto websites and subsequently 
rolled out to all Media Regionalne’s online 
newspapers. This is the first example of such 
technology being applied in this way so far  
in Poland.
 
In 2008, Presspublica launched two online 
web shops. Firstly, sklep.rp.pl was launched 
to showcase the division’s brand endorsed 
products and services (Enterprises). Followed 
by e-sklep.parkiet.com, a platform on which 
Presspublica sells over 2,000 book titles 
issued by other publishers. Other Enterprises 
initiatives by Media Regionalne include warto.pl, 
an e-commerce web shop, and regiopedia.pl,  
the first Polish online encyclopaedia with 
regional appeal, co-created by Media 
Regionalne’s readers and online users. 
Holidays and tours organised by local travel 
agents are also now being marketed, as 
are local trade fairs, with a broad range of 
interest areas, including property, building and 
construction, health and fitness, fashion and 
weddings. Sources: Expert Monitor, ZKDP.

Divisional review
Financial overview – like-for-like
Total revenues fell by 5 per cent, from £143.8 
million to £136.5 million. This fall included the 
effect of the closure of a national advertising 
joint venture, a proportion of whose third-party 
revenues had been consolidated previously. 
Without this effect, total revenues fell by 1 per 
cent.
Including the effect of the closure of the 
national advertising joint venture, advertising 
fell by 3 per cent. However, advertising in 
the two continuing Polish businesses grew 
by 6 per cent, reflecting the strong growth in 
the Polish economy and the roll out of new 
revenue initiatives in the regional business. 
Total advertising fell by 9 per cent in the 
second half, however, advertising fell in the 
second half by only 2 per cent in the continuing 
businesses, with the national business’s 
financial title affected badly by the prevailing 
economic conditions.
Circulation fell by 3 per cent, or £1.9 million, 
mainly from volume declines on existing titles 
in the regional business. Other revenue fell by 
£3.4 million, or 15 per cent, mainly as a result 
of lower Enterprises sales of books in the 
national business. This business was stopped 
in the autumn of 2008.
Total costs fell by 4 per cent, or £5.0 million, 
reflecting closed operations and the benefits of 
restructuring, offset by cost investment in new 
revenue initiatives in the regional business. 
EBITDA as a result was £9.1 million, down 
from £11.4 million in 2007 and EBITDA margin 
fell by 1.2 points to 6.7 per cent. Depreciation 
was broadly flat, resulting in operating profit of 
£2.5 million (2007: £4.9 million).
 
Financial overview – reported
Revenue and operating profit differ between 
the like-for-like and reported results only as

Divisional review
Business portal
The challenge:
Presspublica’s key competitor in the business publishing arena is Infor, a company that publishes a 
whole range of specialist business and legal titles, including Gazeta Prawna. They have a very strong 
online presence and achieve high brand recognition among the division’s subscribers. The quality of 
Presspublica’s online proposition in this area has historically been inferior to Infor’s. This has been a 
competitive threat to the business and a limiting factor to growing the division’s online audience.
The solution:
Presspublica’s existing website, Dobra 
Firma, which is part of Rzeczpospolita 
website, rp.pl, was significantly 
expanded. The access to the upgraded 
site was free in 2008 but will be 
subscriber-only in 2009 as part of a 
premium package which will generate 
a new revenue stream for the division.
The result:
Presspublica’s strong response to a competitive threat  
has been appreciated by its readers. The major product 
development led to a huge improvement to the existing 
website. This provides a good justification for increasing 
the subscription price in 2009 and creating a new revenue 
stream. The enhanced subscription product allows 
Presspublica to claim “Now with Rzeczpospolita you  
can have everything – you do not need to subscribe  
to any other titles”.
Case study
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 32 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Divisional review
Germany
As announced on 13 January 2009, 
the Group sold its German division, 
Berliner Verlag, to M. DuMont Schauberg 
and this disposal completed on  
27 March 2009.
In 2008, Berliner Zeitung increased its share 
of the Berlin subscription paper advertising 
market from 15 per cent to 16 per cent and 
Berliner Kurier’s share of the Berlin tabloid 
paper advertising market increased from 8 
per cent to 9 per cent. The readership share of 
Berliner Kurier in Berlin increased from 12.7 per 
cent in 2007 to 14.7 per cent in 2008, while the 
share of Berliner Zeitung decreased from 19.9 
per cent to 17 .8 per cent. The market share 
of both titles combined remained stable at  
33 per cent of the Berlin newspaper market.
The magazine, TIP, increased its circulation 
market share from 12 per cent in 2007 to 13 
per cent in 2008, thus maintaining its leading 
position both in Berlin and Germany. The 
advertising market share however decreased 
from 40 per cent to 38 per cent as a result 
of the decreasing overall advertising market 
for print and the price cutting strategies of 
other publications. The free-sheet Berliner 
Abendblatt decreased its share of the total 
Berlin printed free-sheet advertising market 
from 40 per cent to 30 per cent and decreased 
its circulation market share from 46 per cent in 
2007 to 40 per cent in 2008.
Hamburger Morgenpost launched its sub-
local supplement Blickpunkt offering articles 
and advertisements targeted at each Hamburg 
district thus emphasising its strength in local 
coverage. Berliner Zeitung and Berliner 
Kurier are jointly publishing a new real 
estate magazine, Immobilien, attracting new 
advertising clients by offering a new quality 
platform. The editorial co-operation between 
Berliner Kurier and Hamburger Morgenpost is 
providing higher quality local news coverage 
with some of the political news editors now 
writing for the local news section.
In 2008, a newsroom was set up in Berliner 
Kurier serving News, Local, Online desks as 
well as layout and production. At the same 
time, Berliner Zeitung created a newsroom in 
which all Netzeitung editors were integrated 
and articles from Berliner Zeitung, especially 
those with nationwide interest, are now 
accessible on netzeitung.de. Most of the 
division’s websites have been relaunched 
and now include user-generated content and 
interactive forums. 
One key development during the year has 
been the development of a web shop in 
order to enable the division to market its 
brand endorsed goods and services to 
readers and users across all its titles and 
websites (Enterprises). Berliner Verlag has 
used Berlingke’s web shop lidtmere.dk as
