Financial overview – like-for-like
Total revenue fell by £3.9 million or 3 per cent 
during the year to 31 December 2008, from 
£123.2 million to £119.3 million. Advertising 
revenue fell by 9 per cent, with the decline 
accelerating from a first half decline of 6 per 
cent to 11 per cent in the second half. All 
Mecom Germany titles were affected by the 
decline, with the division’s free-sheets and bi-
weekly magazine falling most in percentage 
terms. 
Circulation revenue, which is over 55 per 
cent newsstand sales in highly competitive 
markets, fell by 1 per cent, with the loss of 
volumes more than offsetting price increases. 
Other revenue increases reflected the growth 
in a number of initiatives, including call centre 
and content sales.
Costs (including share of results of associates) 
fell by £2.3 million, or 2 per cent, reflecting 
mainly the benefit of staff restructuring, 
resulting in EBITDA of £15.3 million, down from 
£16.9 million in 2007. EBITDA and operating 
margins fell marginally to 12.8 per cent and 9.9 
per cent, respectively. 
Financial overview – reported
1
The increase in the reported revenue and 
operating profit between 2007 and 2008 
results primarily from a full year’s ownership 
of Mecom Germany in 2008 (acquired in 
April 2007) and the strengthening of the euro 
against sterling. Operating exceptional items of 
£3.6 million (2007: £2.5 million) were recorded, 
related mainly due to staff restructuring. 
Amortisation of acquired intangibles was £6.3 
million (2007: £3.9 million), increasing because 
of a full year’s ownership and currency effects. 
An impairment charge of £149.3 million (2007: 
£nil) was recorded against goodwill to write 
the net assets of Germany down to the net 
disposal proceeds on its sale in March 2009.

The financial results for the year to 31 
December 2008, and the financial position 
of the Group at that date, were affected by a 
number of important factors:
the inclusion of the results of Wegener (within •	
the Netherlands segment) and Mecom 
Germany (within discontinued operations, 
as explained below) for a full financial year 
whereas in the year to 31 December 2007 
the results of Wegener were included 
only from 25 October 2007 and Mecom 
Germany only from 12 April 2007 , the dates 
on which the Group acquired Wegener and 
Mecom Germany, respectively. This report 
explains the reported results of the Group as 
set out in the financial statements, whereas 
the Group highlights and Divisional reviews 
on pages 13, 20 to 32 provide a comparison 
of the current year’s results against the prior 
year’s on a like-for-like basis, that is as if the 
Group had owned each of its businesses for 
the entire two year period;
the treatment of Mecom Germany as a •	
discontinued operation as at 31 December 
2008, with the result that Mecom 
Germany’s result (for both the current and 
prior financial year) and the loss recorded 
in writing down Mecom Germany’s 
goodwill are shown as a single-line item in 
the income statement below the profit after 
tax result of the Group and its assets and 
liabilities recorded as “held for sale” in the 
balance sheet (more detailed information 
is given in Note 13 to the consolidated 
financial statements);
the recognition of impairment charges of •	
£861.3 million on continuing businesses, 
against the carrying amount of goodwill, 
intangible assets and other non-current 
assets of the Group’s continuing businesses 
(and the loss on the remeasurement of 
the assets of the German business of 
£149.3 million), reflecting the effect that 
the current economic crisis has had on 
the performance and prospects of the  
Group’s businesses; and
the sharp increase in the relative strength  •	
of the currencies of the countries in 
which the Group operates, in particular 
the euro, which affected the results as 
presented in sterling and the value of 
assets and liabilities in the 31 December 
2008 balance sheet – the exchange rates 
used in the consolidation of the Group’s 
financial statements are given in Note 4 
to the consolidated financial statements. 
The Group has decided to change its 
presentational currency from sterling to the 
euro from 1 January 2009 and will therefore 
present future financial statements in euro. 
In the income statement, the Group has 
presented exceptional items and amortisation 
of acquired intangibles separately and excluded 
these items in presenting the “adjusted 
results” referred to in this Annual report and 
accounts to allow shareholders to understand 
better the elements of financial performance 
in the period. The Group separates the 
amortisation of acquired intangibles because, 
whilst accounting standards require the 
recognition of amortisation as an expense, it

Group 
Finance

continued
is not an underlying operating expense of the 
Group’s businesses. The exceptional items 
and amortisation of acquired intangibles are 
set out in Note 10 to the consolidated financial 
statements. 
The Group’s financial key performance 
indicators are revenue growth, adjusted 
EBITDA margin and adjusted operating margin. 
These are considered in the Group highlights 
and Divisional reviews, on a like-for-like basis. 
Information on these performance indicators 
on a reported basis is set out in Note 6 to the 
consolidated financial statements.
Revenue and earnings before interest 
and tax from continuing operations
Revenue from continuing operations for the 
year to 31 December 2008 was £1,408.3 
million, up £503.5 million from the prior 
year. The increase includes the effect of the 
ownership of Wegener for a full year and 
the relative strength of the currencies of the 
countries in which the Group operates, in 
part offset by an underlying decrease in the 
advertising revenue of the Group’s businesses. 
The advertising revenue performance of the 
Group was affected in the final months of the 
year by the current economic crisis.
Adjusted EBITDA from continuing operations 
was £148.0 million, up £46.0 million from that 
of the prior year. The increase reflects again 
the effect of the ownership of Wegener for 
a full year and the relative strength of the 
currencies of the countries in which the Group 
operates, offset in part by a deterioration in the 
EBITDA margin of the Group as the shortfall in 
underlying advertising revenue was matched 
only in part by reductions in cost. The Group’s 
restructuring activities (and the net effect 
of acquisitions and disposals) resulted in a 
decrease in average headcount of 830 (7 
per cent) during 2008, in all areas other than 
editorial staff.
Depreciation and amortisation of software 
increased by £23. 1 million, resulting in adjusted 
operating profit from continuing operations 
of £92.8 million, up by £22.9 million from the 
year to 31 December 2007 . As with revenue 
and adjusted EBITDA, this increase is the net 
effect of increases resulting from movements 
in foreign exchange rates and the increase in 
the size of the Group, more than offsetting an 
underlying decrease in the Group’s adjusted 
operating profit margins.
Exceptional items recognised in operating loss 
totalled £74.2 million, compared with £47.2 
million for the year to 31 December 2007 , 
and included staff redundancy costs resulting 
from the Group’s restructuring activities in the 
Netherlands and Denmark, costs associated 
with the reorganisation and refurbishment  
of the Copenhagen offices and the cost of  
the Company’s admission to the main list  
of the London Stock Exchange, as explained 
in Note 10 to the consolidated financial 
statements. Management estimates that the 
level of exceptional cash cost in 2009 will be 
circa €80 million, including circa €20 million 
of costs related to the amendments of the 
facility agreement and further restructuring 
costs, including the Delta restructuring project 
to be undertaken in 2009 in the Netherlands 
and payments made on provisions related to 
previously completed restructurings. Charges 
for impairment of goodwill and of acquired 
intangibles of the continuing businesses were 
£855.9 million (2007: £nil). Full details of the 
charges are given in Notes 15, 16, 17 , 18 and 
20 to the consolidated financial statements. 
Amortisation of acquired intangibles was £60.6 
million, up by £27 .2 million from the prior year, 
reflecting the full-year effect of the acquisitions 
of Wegener and Mecom Germany as well as 
the weakening of sterling.
The resulting operating loss after exceptional 
items and the amortisation of acquired 
intangibles was £903.3 million, compared  
with £10.7 million in 2007 .
Finance items and taxation from 
continuing operations
Net finance expense before exceptional items 
was £39.7 million, up from £22.8 million in 
2007 . The increase includes the effect of 
additional borrowings taken out to finance 
the acquisitions of Wegener during 2007 and, 
since the Group’s borrowings and interest 
cost are largely denominated in currencies 
other than sterling, the relative strength of 
these other currencies during the period. 
As explained in Note 26 to the consolidated 
financial statements, the margin applicable 
to the Group’s borrowings was increased to 
350 basis points from 22 December 2008 as 
part of amendments to the facility agreement 
agreed with the Group’s lending banks; the 
terms of the revised facility agreement that 
has been agreed with the Group’s lending 
banks are set out below in Note 26 to the 
consolidated financial statements.
Exceptional finance items include costs of 
the amendments made to the bank facility 
agreement in December 2008. The total fees 
were £3.3 million, of which £2.9 million relates 
to continuing operations.
The Group’s effective tax rate on adjusted 
profit before tax (adjusted for associates 
whose earnings are presented after tax) was 
30 per cent (2007: 31 per cent), which is more 
than the weighted blended statutory rate of the 
countries in which the Group operates owing 
to the presence of non-deductible items. This 
is likely to remain at this level in 2009.
The total tax expense on the loss before tax 
after exceptional items and amortisation of 
acquired intangibles was £1.5 million (2007: 
credit of £10.2 million). Of which, the tax 
effect of exceptional items and amortisation 
of acquired intangibles was a credit of £45.6 
million. The relatively low tax credit compared 
with the total exceptional charges relates 
to the non-deductibility for tax purposes 
of the goodwill write-down. The credit in 
respect of acquired intangibles results 
from the release of deferred tax liabilities 
recorded on acquisition of the Group’s 
businesses and is therefore a non-cash item.

In addition, an exceptional tax charge of  
£32.4 million was recorded to provide against 
carried forward losses that were considered 
to be no longer recoverable. 
Discontinued operations
The profit after tax of Mecom Germany is 
shown in the “discontinued operations” 
line in the income statement. The adjusted 
result after tax of £6.3 million is £2.5 million 
higher than last year, reflecting a full year of 
ownership in 2008 compared with eight and 
a half months in 2007 . The charge of £163.0 
million for exceptional items and amortisation 
of acquired intangibles includes an impairment 
loss recognised on the re-measurement of the 
assets and liabilities of Mecom Germany to 
fair value (less costs to sell) of £149.3 million, 
exceptional items charged to operating 
profit of £3.6 million (2007: £2.5 million), the 
amortisation of acquired intangibles of £6.3m 
(2007: £3.9 million) and finance exceptionals  
of £0.9 million (2007: £2.1 million). Full details 
are set out in Note 13 to the consolidated 
financial statements.
Earnings per share and dividends
Adjusted earnings per share from continuing 
operations were 2.1 pence, down from 2.6 
pence in 2007 . Adjusted earnings per share 
from continuing and discontinued operations 
were 2.5 pence, down from 2.9 pence in 2007 . 
The retained profit used for the calculation of 
adjusted earnings per share increased from 
£36.8 million to £38.6 million and the average 
number of shares in issue increased from 
1,278 million to 1,572 million, resulting from 
share issues part way through 2007 . The 
unadjusted loss per share from continuing 
operations was 60.3 pence (2007: 2.1 pence) 
and the unadjusted loss per share from 
continuing and discontinued operations was 
70.3 pence (2007: 1.9 pence).
The Group paid no dividends in the year to 
31 December 2008 (2007: £nil).
Cash flow
Cash generated from operations (which 
includes the cash flows of Mecom Germany) 
was £111.6 million, an increase of £28.5 million 
from 2007 . Adjusted EBITDA (for the entire 
Group) increased by £50.0 million; there was 
a net inflow from working capital in the year to 
31 December 2008 of £31.2 million, compared 
with a net inflow of £21.6 million in 2007 (which 
included the effect of the timing of the Group’s 
2007 acquisitions with the working capital 
cycle of the businesses acquired). Capital 
expenditure payments were £68.8 million 
(2007: £34.6 million); receipts from the sale of 
assets were £12.0 million (2007: £8.1 million). 
Tax paid was £1.7 million (2007: £9.1 million).
In line with guidance given at the interim 
results in 2008, capital expenditure is likely to 
fall to around €50 million in 2009, as the final 
stages of the Wegener repressing programme 
are implemented.
Net finance costs paid were £37 .9 million (2007: 
£28.6 million), in addition to which the Group 
paid cash costs in respect of the amendment 
of the terms of the Group’s bank borrowings 
of £2.3 million. The income statement charge 
for net finance expense included non-cash 
expenses related to imputed interest on 
discounted liabilities of £2.3 million (2007: £1.5 
million) and the amortisation of prepaid debt 
issue costs of £2.9 million (2007: £0.3 million).
The Group recorded a net cash outflow from 
acquisitions and disposals of £1.2 million. 
Disposals comprised the De Trompetter free-
sheet business in the Netherlands segment 
(net proceeds of £15.8 million), and a Direct 
Marketing business in the Norway segment 
(net proceeds of £3.8 million). Acquisitions 
included digital businesses in the Norway 
segment (net cash outflow of £7.6 million) 
and the purchase of the remaining 7 per cent 
of Mecom Germany that the Group did not 
previously own (£5.3 million). The cash outflow 
of £502.4 million in 2007 included amounts 
related to the acquisition of 78 per cent of 
Mecom Germany (£86.9 million) and 86.4 per 
cent of Wegener (£401.1 million).
Net proceeds from borrowings, derivatives 
and obligations under finance leases during 
the year were £8.3 million (2007: net repayment 
of £97 .3 million). In 2007 , the Group raised 
£556.4 million (net of expenses) from the  
issue of share capital. 
The net increase in cash and cash equivalents 
in 2008 was £21.1 million (2007: decrease  
of £17 .4 million) which when added to the 
amount at the beginning of the year of 
£73.1 million and with net foreign exchange 
differences of £14.5 million resulted in cash 
and cash equivalents at the end of 2008 of 
£108.7 million. 
Financial position
The Group’s closing net debt was £669.3 
million (2007: £524.3 million), comprising 
borrowings of £744.6 million (2007: £588.9 
million), obligations under finance leases of 
£24.3 million (2007: £18.5 million), liabilities 
associated with interest rate swaps and 
other derivative liabilities of £9.4 million (2007: 
assets of £6.7 million) borrowings included 
within liabilities directly associated with assets 
held for sale of £4.5 million (2007: £nil) and 
cash and cash equivalents of £113.5 million 
(2007: £76.4 million). Cash balances at 31 
December 2008 included prepaid annual 
and quarterly subscription receipts collected 
at the very end of the year. In the absence of 
a fully signed revised facility agreement for its 
bank borrowings, the Group has classified all 
bank borrowings as current at 31 December 
2008. In addition, the convertible loan note of 
£30.1 million (at 31 December 2008) became 
payable within one year. 
The effect of foreign currency movements was 
to increase the Group’s net borrowings by 
£135.0 million; the euro sterling exchange rate 
at 31 December 2008 was 1.03, compared 
with 1.36 at 31 December 2007 . Including  
other non-cash movements of £21.8 million, 
closing net debt increased from £524.3 million 
to £669.3 million.
The Group’s equity decreased by £853.7 
million in the year to 31 December 2008. The 
retained loss of £1,107 .8 million was partially 
offset by net income recognised directly in 
equity of £256.5 million, including exchange 
differences on retranslation of the Group’s 
subsidiaries of £270.7 million. Minority interest 
increased during the year by £2.7 million, 
including the minority interest’s share of net 
income recognised directly in equity.
Financial and liquidity risk and  
going concern
The basis on which the consolidated financial

Background to negotiations on revised 
bank agreement and proposals for an 
equity issue
The Group’s primary sources of funding are 
shareholders’ equity and bank borrowings. 
During the second half of 2008, a marked 
deterioration in advertising revenues affecting 
the Group’s profitability indicated that the 
Group’s leverage was too high for the current 
economic conditions.
In December 2008, the Group announced 
its intention to reduce borrowings and, at the 
same time, entered into an agreement with its 
lending banks to defer the testing of financial 
covenants in its bank facilities agreement 
from 31 December 2008 to 28 February 2009 
(which was subsequently deferred further to 31 
March 2009, then further to 30 April 2009 and 
further to 31 May 2009, as explained below) 
and engaged in discussions to renegotiate the 
terms of its bank facilities. 
The Group announced the disposal of its 
German operations in January 2009 for 
consideration of €152.0 million (£147.0 million) 
and of its northwest Norwegian operations in 
February 2009 for NOK559.3 million (£55.5 
million) as part of its strategy to reduce its 
borrowings. The cash proceeds from these 
disposals were received by the Group on 27 
March 2009 and 2 April 2009, respectively.
The Group announced on 23 March 2009 that 
it has been examining the merits of an equity 
fund-raising.
The Group announced on 1 April 2009 that 
it had also agreed with the holders of its 
convertible loan notes an extension to the 
maturity of these notes from 12 April to 12 
May 2009, although it was agreed that this 
extension would accelerate to 30 April 2009 
under certain conditions.  
On 29 April 2009, the Group entered into 
an agreement with its lending banks for a 
further deferral of the testing date of financial 
covenants until 31 May 2009 and the Group

on the banks but each of the banks has

the same and the Group believes that it is 
highly likely that full documentation will be 
signed in May 2009; and
received non-binding commitments from •	
current and prospective shareholders 
(which will be conditional upon, inter alia, 
the Group agreeing acceptable banking 
terms with its lenders, publishing a 
prospectus and obtaining shareholder 
approval) to subscribe to a proposed 
equity issue of approximately £140 million 
(before expenses). The Group intends 
repaying the convertible loan notes from 
these proceeds.
The Group expects to complete and to sign 
full banking documentation during May 2009, 
after which it expects that a prospectus for the 
issue of new shares will be issued with a view 
to receiving the proceeds of the equity issue 
during June 2009.
In the event that full banking documentation is 
not completed on the terms currently agreed 
or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Group would continue discussion 
with its bank lenders with a view to agreeing 
alternative banking terms, but the directors 
cannot determine at this stage whether, or 
on what basis, alternative terms would be 
agreed.
In the event that full banking documentation is 
not completed on the terms currently agreed 
or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Group would also expect to 
enter into discussions with the holders of the 
Group’s convertible loan notes to restructure 
the maturity of these notes, which would then 
be due currently and which the Group would 
be unable, in the absence of the agreement 
of the Group’s lending banks, to repay. The 
directors cannot determine at this stage what 
the outcome of these discussions would be.
In the event that the full banking documentation 
is not completed on the terms currently 
agreed or that the proposed equity issue 
does not happen, the Group’s ability to 
continue operating as a going concern would 
be dependent, therefore, on the outcome of 
these discussions with its lending banks and 
with the holders of the convertible loan notes.

In assessing the Group’s ability to remain in 
compliance with the terms of the revised 
facility agreement in the foreseeable future, 
the directors have taken into account the fact 
that the leverage, interest cover and operating 
cash flow covenants would not be tested 
under the proposed revised facility agreement 
within twelve months of the date of these 
financial statements. 
The directors have also considered the 
Group’s financial projections for the twelve 
month period from these financial statements 
as they affect the proposed revised bank 
facility agreement in respect of conditions 
other than the leverage, interest cover and 
operating cash flow covenants. In making 
its financial projections for these purposes, 
the Group has taken into account that it 
currently generates around 50 per cent of 
its revenue from advertising, the markets for 
which have tended in the past to reflect the 
general economic conditions of the countries

Overview
in which the Group operates. The remainder 
of the Group’s revenue includes circulation 
revenue (around 35 per cent of total revenue), 
which has more stable characteristics 
compared with advertising revenue and has 
not previously been affected by prevailing 
economic conditions to the extent that 
advertising revenue has been.
The Group’s advertising markets have 
experienced a considerable and systematic 
downturn in recent months and, although the 
experience of recent weeks’ trading suggests 
that some stabilisation at these lower levels 
has occurred, the advertising environment 
remains challenging and uncertain.  
In making assumptions of future advertising 
revenue for the purposes of assessing its ability 
to comply with the terms of the proposed 
revised facility agreement, the Group has 
used a combination of long-term trends, 
industry and third-party forecasts and internal 
estimates which reflect recent experience 
in each of our markets. If the actual outturn 
is adverse to these assumptions, the Group 
has identified a number of further mitigating 
actions that it could take to reduce costs or 
borrowings further.
Going concern basis in the financial 
statements
The directors believe that the combination 
of the circumstances described above, 
in particular (a) the uncertainty as to the 
completion of a revised facility agreement on 
the terms currently agreed (b) the uncertainty 
as to whether the non-binding commitments 
of investors to underwrite the issue of new 
share capital will result in new shares being 
issued, with the completion of the revised 
facility arrangements and the issue of equity 
being inter-conditional, and (c) the uncertainty, 
in the event that the revised facility agreement 
is not completed on terms currently agreed 
or that the new share capital is not issued, 
as to whether the Group could reach 
satisfactory agreement with the holders of 
its convertible loan notes as to an extension 
of the maturity of those notes, all of which 
three factors existing within a highly uncertain 
advertising environment, represent a material 
uncertainty that casts significant doubt on 
the Group’s and the Company’s ability to 
continue as a going concern. Nevertheless, 
after making enquiries, and considering the 
uncertainties described above, the directors 
have a reasonable expectation that the Group 
and the Company have adequate resources 
to continue in operational existence for the 
foreseeable future. For these reasons, they 
continue to adopt the going concern basis in 
preparing the Annual report and accounts.
Treasury
Details of the Group’s bank borrowing 
facility, which is the main source of the 
Group’s funding, are given in Note 26 to the 
consolidated financial statements. The Group 
agreed an amendment to the terms of this 
facility on 18 December 2008, which had the 
effect of deferring the testing of the year-end 
financial covenants under the facility from 31 
December 2008 to 28 February 2009 as well 
as restricting the Group’s ability to draw on the 
revolving credit facility. The Group paid £2.3 
million as a fee to the banks in connection with 
this amendment.
The Group manages treasury matters centrally, 
through the Group Treasurer and the treasury 
function in the Group’s head office in London. The 
Group treasury function manages the Group’s 
borrowings facilities and short- and medium-
term liquidity position and monitors the Group’s 
treasury risks. A Treasury Committee, which 
includes the Group Finance Director, the Group 
Treasurer, the Group Head of Corporate Finance 
and the Group Financial Controller, provides 
guidance on treasury matters and oversees risk 
management.
The Group is exposed to treasury risks arising 
from exposure to movements in market interest 
rates and to foreign currency rates. 
The Group has a policy of keeping between 40 
per cent and 80 per cent of its borrowings at 
fixed rates, so as to provide some certainty on its 
interest costs while leaving open the opportunity 
to benefit from any future reductions in interest 
rates.
The Group has drawn its borrowings in the 
operating currencies of its businesses, principally 
in euros and in Danish and Norwegian krone, 
to match the currency of interest payments 
and anticipated repayments of principal with 
the Group’s operating cash flows. The foreign 
currency borrowings also provide a balance 
sheet hedge for the Group’s operating assets and 
liabilities, all of which are denominated in foreign 
currencies. 
The Group’s principal performance indicators 
in respect of financing and treasury matters are 
the ratios of net debt to adjusted EBITDA and of 
adjusted EBITDA to adjusted net interest expense. 
As well as being well-recognised measures for 
monitoring the strength of financial condition, 
these two measures form the basis of covenants 
in the Group’s bank borrowing arrangements.

ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 38 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Overview
Principal 
risks and 
uncertainties 
The Group’s principal risks and uncertainties, together with the actions that management 
is taking to mitigate each, are set out below. In the current economic climate the 
Board considers that the mitigating actions have increased in relevance and progress  
in each area is therefore being closely monitored by executive management with regular  
Board updates.
The Group recognises that risk is an inherent part of doing business and has therefore  
adopted a process for identifying, evaluating and managing the risks faced by its business 
(as described in the Corporate governance report). The risks to which the Group is potentially 
exposed cover a wide range of factors: competition, legislation, fiscal, regulatory, political, 
financial, terrorism, economic, social and operational. Each could impact on the Group’s 
revenue, operating profit, net assets and liquidity.
Risk Description Management action
Market place Short term – Reduction in advertising revenue in the current economic downturn
In common with the majority of publishing businesses, the 
Group’s revenues are traditionally heavily dependent on 
advertising which comprised approximately 50 per cent of 
total revenue in 2008. 
The economic crisis, which started in 2008, has attacked all 
categories of advertising with print adverts for employment, 
property and motor vehicles more affected than other 
groups. The Group experienced approximately a 10 per 
cent reduction in advertising revenue during the second half 
of 2008 and this trend has continued and deepened into  
early 2009.
The Group has already commenced urgent steps to mitigate 
the shortfall in advertising by setting up programmes to take 
considerable costs out of its businesses and in accelerating 
the development of new revenue from alternative sources. 
However, it may not be able to do this quickly or sufficiently 
leading to reduced profitability in the short term.
Medium term – Negative effect of internet advertising on traditional advertising
Across the market, the print media’s share of advertising is 
declining and this trend is likely to continue into the medium 
term as customers exercise their choice to advertise over the 
internet rather than in newspapers.
The Group is taking decisive action to accelerate its 
transformation from a pure print company into a consumer 
content business and seeking new digital revenue streams  
and new media products as fast as possible. Management 
expects that new consumer products and services will 
be introduced in line with its required time schedules, but 
cannot yet assess whether the new revenue streams will fully 
compensate for the traditional revenues that have already 
been lost.
Long term – Erosion of demand for printed newspapers
The Group’s newspapers have experienced circulation volume 
declines over recent years, in common with the newspaper 
industry in general. To date we have been able to offset  
these volume declines by cover price and subscription rate 
increases such that circulation revenue has remained  
broadly constant.
However, there is now a risk that the rate of volume decrease 
will be exacerbated as a result of the current economic 
conditions and that the Group will be less successful than  
in the past at compensating volume declines with increases 
in cover price and subscription rates.
Given the Group’s in-depth understanding of the markets in 
which it operates, it is able to withstand some of the downward 
pressures being felt on newspaper volumes across media 
businesses by maintaining and improving the quality of its 
portfolio of strong premium products in the marketplace.
The Group is leveraging its expert knowledge of its local 
markets and customers to maximum advantage by improving 
the relevance of its papers to the readers in the individual 
markets in which it operates.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 39
Overview
Risk Description Management action
Operational 
performance
The Group’s margins will be eroded if its cost base is not 
reduced quickly to offset the detrimental effects of inflation 
on salaries, given the Group’s high proportion of staff costs, 
and on the cost of its raw materials, most notably newsprint.
The Group’s strategy for protecting margins relies on 
identifying operating synergies which are often achieved 
through reorganisations, the introduction of more efficient 
work practices and realising economies of scale. However, the 
cost of structural change in continental European economies 
is potentially very high. In addition, the Group operates in 
countries with labour laws and agreements that differ from 
the UK and where employees generally enjoy stronger 
protection. The Group’s ability to generate cost savings on 
a timely basis may therefore be hampered by strikes, illegal 
industrial action or new regulation from governments in any 
of the jurisdictions in which we operate.
The Group continually seeks ways of improving its productivity 
to protect its margins. In addition it has established priority 
programmes in all divisions in the light of the economic 
downturn. These programmes will drive improvements in our 
business models by making our businesses more innovative, 
securing better ways of working, leveraging cross-Group 
benefits from scale and removing old “industry practices”. 
For example, outsourcing and partnering arrangements 
have already been agreed to make best use of underutilised 
capacity. In considering the best option, attention is always 
given to the cash impact as well as to optimising the return.
To tackle rising costs the Group has already carried out a 
strategic review of procurement which has enabled it to: secure 
more competitive prices for raw materials and other key supplies; 
reduce discretionary spend and improve demand management. 
To ensure that the Group is able to implement the structural 
changes needed in its business, it is committed to working 
constructively with governments and other regulatory bodies. 
It is challenging previous collective bargaining and industry 
practices to make its cost base more flexible and is engaging 
in constructive dialogue with unions and works councils to 
develop effective relationships in each case.
Business 
continuity
The Group is highly dependent on the continuous 
operation of its print plants, packing lines and supporting IT 
infrastructure to get its print products to its customers. It also 
depends on the high availability of its many websites which 
allow its customers access to online products and services. 
A significant and extended loss of a major facility, whether 
through natural causes, deliberate acts or breakdown, could 
result in a loss of revenue.
All divisions are required to maintain business continuity 
plans and to update these to reflect the re-organisations and 
restructurings taking place within its business. Each division is 
also required to develop a programme for the testing of these 
plans to ensure their effectiveness and relevance.
The Group is also reviewing its printing plant maintenance 
programmes and maintains insurance to protect against 
catastrophic risks.
Funding The Group is financed by significant bank borrowings, as well 
as shareholders’ equity. As explained in the Group Finance 
Director’s report and Note 4 to the consolidated financial 
statements, the Group has agreed “in principle” terms for a 
revision and extension to the its bank borrowings. Further as 
explained in Note 4 to the consolidated financial statements, 
the Group faces the risk, in the short term, that these “in 
principle” terms do not result in a signed revised facility 
agreement. The Group also faces the risk, in the medium- 
to longer-term, that it is not able to comply with financial 
covenants in the proposed revised bank facility agreement, 
the key financial covenants being tested first at June 2010. 
The Group expects that the “in principle” terms agreed 
with its lending banks will result in a signed revised facility 
agreement, since the key terms (which cover substantially all 
major commercial and financial matters) have been agreed 
by the credit committees of each of its lending banks and the 
remaining steps to conclude full bank documentation should 
not be contentious.
The Group has initiated a number of actions to reduce its 
borrowings and to provide the financial stability needed to 
operate within the terms of its banking agreements in the 
current difficult economic conditions. Cost reduction plans 
are underway and the Group operates a policy of strict 
management of cash expenditure. The Group has completed 
or announced disposals in recent months to reduce the 
absolute levels of its bank borrowings and to improve its 
leverage ratios.
Exchange 
rates
The Group will report its results in euro from 1 January 2009. 
The Group will then be exposed in its reported results and 
balance sheet position to movements in exchange rates 
between the euro and the other currencies in which the Group 
operates, principally the Norwegian krone and Polish zloty.
The Group has borrowed in Norwegian krone to reduce its 
net balance sheet exposure to movements between the  
euro and the krone.
Key
management
The Group’s success depends on its ability to attract, 
motivate and retain highly qualified employees who have 
extensive experience and knowledge of the industry at a 
strategic level.
T o attract, retain and motivate the best talents, the Group provides 
a competitive remuneration package for its key management  
and employees. Succession planning from the level of Country 
CEOs up to the Chief Executive has also been put in place.
Certain risks and uncertainties arise through factors that are outside the control of management, for example, inflation or interest rates. 
Nevertheless in each case management seeks to minimise the impact on the Group from such external events, for example, by hedging through 
interest rate swaps as set out in the Group Finance Director’s report under the heading of “Treasury”. In other cases risks may appear that are 
presently unanticipated as the Group develops its new business models.

Overview
Corporate 
social 
responsibility
Mecom is committed to responsible corporate 
behaviour. As a dedicated media group 
Mecom believes that its reputation is based 
on maintaining high standards of business 
conduct in its relationships with employees 
and stakeholders, being customers, readers, 
shareholders, suppliers, governments, 
competitors and the local communities in 
which Mecom operates.
To underwrite Mecom’s commitment, a 
Code of Business Conduct (the “Code”) has 
been implemented across the Group to help 
employees develop a clear understanding of 
the principles and ethical values that Mecom 
wants to uphold. The Code is available on 
Mecom’s website. Each division has translated 
the Code into its local language and made 
it available to employees on their intranets. 
Compliance with the Code is important for 
maintaining and building the reputation of 
the Group as a responsible and trustworthy 
business partner, employer, supplier and 
corporate citizen.
The Code forms the core element of the 
Group’s corporate responsibility framework 
which comprises a set of policies and 
controls that govern how Mecom acts as an 
organisation and how Mecom interacts with 
its stakeholders in conducting business. It is 
not possible to anticipate every situation that 
may arise. The Code is therefore necessarily 
broad and general in nature and is not 
intended to replace more detailed policies 
and procedures within individual divisions.  
A whistleblowing policy is also in place  
within the Group for employees to raise 
concerns, in confidence, about possible 
wrongdoing, dishonest or unethical behaviour. 
The Code protects anyone choosing to make 
such a disclosure.
The following report is aimed at providing 
further insight and highlighting a variety of 
social, ethical, environmental, health and safety 
policies within which Mecom’s businesses 
operate.
Employees
Mecom’s employees are key contributors 
towards the Group’s success. The 
responsibility for formulating, implementing and 
ensuring adherence to employment policies 
and relevant legislation is the responsibility of 
the Human Resources (“HR”) director of each 
division. During the year, a HR Steering Group 
consisting of HR directors of each division was 
established by the Company Secretary with 
the aim of sharing knowledge and exchanging 
ideas regarding employee matters. 
Each division in the Group fully supports the 
principle of equal opportunity for all and is 
committed to a policy of equal opportunity for 
employees at all levels. Employees are treated 
equally in all employment-related aspects 
regardless of their gender, age, race, religion, 
nationality, political opinion, social origin, ethnic 
origin, sexual orientation or any disability. The 
Group as a whole has over 40 per cent of the 
workforce which are women. Each division 
opposes all forms of discrimination and has 
policies to ensure it meets its legal obligations. 
It is also the policy of each division to give 
full and fair consideration to the recruitment 
of disabled persons. In an annual employee 
survey carried out by our Norwegian division, 
it was shown that the employees feel that there 
are no significant differences between the 
genders on how they perceived the treatment 
and opportunities in the workplace.
Employees across all divisions enjoy various 
rights and protection through collective 
employee involvement and representation 
achieved via local forums, such as works 
councils and meetings with recognised 
unions. Procedures for electing employee 
representatives vary across the divisions, and 
on balance reflect the views of the workforce. 
Meetings are held between employee 
representatives and management to consult 
on matters essential to the operation of the 
business and to allow employees to raise 
any concerns they may have. Furthermore, 
in Denmark and Norway, employees are 
entitled to be represented on the boards of the  
local operating companies.
In addition to divisional practices, emphasis 
was placed on building the relationship 
between central management and Mecom’s 
European Works Council (“EWC”) during 2008 
and this led to the signing of a new European 
Works Council (“EWC”) agreement for the 
enlarged Mecom group. The EWC comprises 
10 representatives from the Group’s divisions 
and meets three times a year without, 
and three times a year with, the central 
management team. The central management 
team comprises of representatives from the 
Group’s divisions and the Company Secretary 
or any person nominated by Mecom. The 
Company Secretary or any person nominated 
by Mecom is responsible for managing the 
relationship with the EWC on behalf of the 
Board. The EWC’s focus is on transnational 
matters (as opposed to national matters where 
the principal mechanisms for information and 
consultation operate at divisional level) and its 
relationship with central management is good 
with open dialogue and a solutions-oriented 
approach to the matters discussed.
Each division believes in open and continuous 
communication as an important part of the 
employee engagement process and seeks to 
achieve this through a variety of channels. All 
the divisions except Germany have a well-used 
intranet and publish newsletters to employees. 
The Country CEOs in Denmark, Norway and 
Germany write to all employees and the 
Dutch Country CEO held roadshows to keep 
employees informed of the development plans 
of the division. A monthly HR breakfast meeting 
between the HR director and the employees 
was initiated in 2008 in Presspublica, one of 
Mecom’s businesses in Poland, to discuss 
current employee issues and this led to the 
publication of a quarterly newsletter for the 
employees. Furthermore, in co-operation 
with an external consultant, our Norwegian 
division runs an annual employee survey 
which is used as an employee feedback tool, 
providing management an insight to develop, 
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 41
Overview
conduct and improve communications with 
employees. 
Each division recognises that the development 
of its employees is important for the success 
of that division as well as the Group, and their 
aim is to encourage and wherever possible to 
develop employees to realise their potential. 
Each division, wherever possible, advertises 
job vacancies on the intranet and internal 
notice boards so that the number of positions 
filled from within the Group is maximised 
and opportunities are created for internal 
promotion. For example in 2008, 20 per cent 
of all vacancies across the Group have been 
filled with internal candidates.
Each division invests in a range of training 
and development programmes that are 
offered to employees in order to maintain a 
broad portfolio of skills and to help each one 
maximise their effectiveness in the workplace. 
Most divisions run training programmes aimed 
at online journalism, sales and enterprise sales, 
all of which supports the transformation of the

Leadership capability at all levels of the

of each division and the Group as a whole. 
Each division except for Presspublica has a

leadership talent in order to meet the current 
and future needs of the Group. 
Community
Social and community involvement is 
inseparable from Mecom and its businesses 
because of the substantial and crucial impact 
of media on society and the communities they 
serve. As a European content and consumer 
business operating in various countries and 
regions, each division builds its reputation 
as a local enterprise through involvement in 
the local community and a broad variety of 
charitable activities, examples of which are 
set out below.
Wegener is one of the founding members 
of Fonds Slachthofferhulp, a charitable 
foundation established for the benefit of 
victims of crime, traffic accidents and disasters 
in the Netherlands. The foundation supports 
and seeks to improve the circumstances 
of victims and survivors and their families. 
Wegener also lends its support to many other 
national and regional charitable organisations 
including the Free Voice (a media organisation 
which strives for balanced and reliable media 
in eastern European, African and Latin 
American countries), Red Cross, the Dutch 
Hart Foundation, Ronald McDonald House in 
Zwolle (a house for children with cancer and 
their families) and Koningin Wilhelmina Fonds 
(an organisation which fights against cancer). 
Wegener supports the academic programme 
for student journalists in collaboration with 
the University of Groningen, a few other 
universities and higher education schools. 
LMG supports the Toon Hermans House 
foundation which was founded in Limburg 
in 1988. This foundation houses people with 
cancer, their next of kin or survivors and 
provides various facilities to support them. 
LMG also supports various other community 
initiatives, including two finalists from Limburg 
for the audition of the lead in the musical  
Evita and a local pole vault world champion 
from Limburg, Rens Blom, in his preparation 
for the recent Olympic Games, as well 
as producing a successful book entitled  
“20 years of PinkPop” recording the history of 
the PinkPop Festival, one of the oldest festivals 
in the world, which has been held in Limburg 
every year since 1970. 
Berlingske Media runs Den Berlingske Fond. 
This foundation supports activities of national, 
religious, cultural, social or scientific interest, 
as well as research, training and education in 
journalism. Two honorary prizes are presented 
each year by the foundation based on 
applications submitted. The “journalist prize” 
is presented to a journalist who has made 
an outstanding contribution to journalism 
and the “prize of honour” is presented to an 
outstanding Danish public figure. In 2008, 
Berlingske’s free-sheet URBAN launched a 
national campaign against violence in the city 
after several tragic fights at night in the centre 
of Copenhagen. The campaign was a success 
with thousands of young people taking an 
active role by submitting their own stories to 
the campaign website. Since 1972 Berlingske 
Media has held the Berlingske Music Awards 
for Young Talents (age 17 and under) in co-

operation with the Royal Music Academy. A 
number of very significant musicians have

Edda Media participates in the annual

representatives from top Polish companies 
present at this ceremony, Presspublica used 
this opportunity to raise funds by organising 
the auction. During the ceremony, “Good 
Company 2008” prizes for managers of 
the best Polish companies were issued. 
Presspublica has also supported many other 
charitable events throughout the year.
At the end of each year, Berliner Verlag awards 
a prize in recognition of the outstanding 
contribution of politicians, actors, artists 
or businessmen to cultural, political and 
economic life in the city of Berlin. Berliner 
Verlag also operates a free cultural or social 
event for the public at their offices in Berlin. 
These events are held monthly and attract 
1,000 visitors per event. Berliner Verlag also 
developed a project called “Paper in the 
Schools”. Through this project schools receive 
Berliner Zeitung for one year. Each quarter, the 
teachers are invited to a teachers’ club meeting 
where they can exchange their experiences 
in the project with the other participants as 
well as popular personalities from economic, 
culture and media backgrounds. Students are 
encouraged to write their own articles which 
are published in the paper. They also visit the 
editors of Berliner Zeitung to have a look at 
the daily work at a newspaper. In 2008, this 
project received an award, the “Media Max 
Special Prize” for its achievements in the field 
of education.
During 2008, the Group made donations 
to various community and charitable 
organisations totalling £83,000 (2007: 
£73,000). 
Health and safety
The Group strives to create a positive working 
environment by observing all applicable 
health and safety regulations and providing all 
employees with a safe working environment. 
Each division has a health and safety 
committee and/or representatives and has 
monitoring and reporting processes in place. 
The health and safety committee meets 
to discuss issues that arise and establish 
measures to correct and improve health and 
safety standards. 
The table below indicates the total number of 
injuries in the printing plants of all divisions. 
The increase of major injuries in 2008 was due 
to various factors. One being an improved 
reporting system for health and safety 
incidents which has led to a slight increase in 
reported cases. Additional training, guidance 
and emphasis on more careful approach 
have also been given in particular to newly 
employed staff to prevent further injuries.

Overview
Environment 
The Group aims to achieve good environmental 
practice and to minimise adverse 
environmental impacts. Due to the nature of 
Mecom’s business, the primary focus is on 
the reduction of environmental impact in the 
production and printing of newspapers. Each 
division was an established business prior 
to joining Mecom and accordingly operates 
various environmental practices in compliance 
with local regulations.
An Environmental Steering Group (the “ESG”) 
consisting of representatives from each 
division was established by the Company 
Secretary in 2008 to improve the focus and 
leadership of the Group in environmental 
matters. The ESG met during the course of 
2008 to share knowledge and develop a more 
consistent approach to policies and reporting 
on environmental matters across the Group. 
The Group identified the principal key areas 
relevant to our environmental footprint as 
sustainable sourcing with particular focus 
on paper, energy consumption and waste 
management. Mecom considers these 
areas as a way to link social responsibility 
with corporate efficiency. Responsibility for 
the development and implementation of 
environmental policies and initiatives lies with 
each division.
As a European content and consumer  
business, the Group’s aim is to identify and 
assess the risks and reduce the environmental 
impact of its operations. To progress this 
objective, the Group has commissioned 
Trucost, a leading environmental research 
organisation, to assess the Group’s 
environmental impact and this research will 
be used to review the position of the Group 
going forward.
As well as striving to improve the environment 
in which it works, Mecom also aims to promote 
greater environmental responsibility through 
its publications. Thus, Berlingske Tidende, 
launched a new website www.berlingske.dk/
klima dedicated to environmental activities 
and has formed a partnership with Mandag 
Morgen, Scandinavia’s largest independent 
think-tank, in order to increase the focus on 
climate issues in the run-up to Denmark’s 
hosting of the United Nations Climate 
Conference in 2009. Berlingske Tidende has 
also initiated a “Climate Cup” competition 
focusing on business and the environment 
and encouraging Danish companies to enter 
the competition to be designated as the “most 
climate friendly company”. 
Sourcing
The aim of the Group is to purchase from 
suppliers who have obtained or are working 
towards obtaining an environmental 
management accreditation or systems 
(including ISO14001). In establishing any 
Group-wide purchasing arrangements, we 
will seek to include suppliers who share our 
aims for responsible and sustainable sourcing 
as far as possible. Thus, for example, all the 
suppliers of the Group’s plates and ink have 
ISO14001 certification.
In 2008, the Group set the aim to purchase 
75 per cent of its paper from recycled fibre 
or certified, sustainable managed production 
forests. The Danish division purchases the 
majority of its paper through The Danish  
Press Joint Purchasing organisation which 
has a policy of buying paper from suppliers 
primarily in the local Nordic region with 
environmental certification. 
The policy of the Group is to continuously 
seek alternative chemicals and methods that 
are environmentally superior when purchasing 
new chemicals or introducing new methods. 
Each division will prior to ordering any new 
chemical carry out a risk assessment to 
determine the suitability of the new product. 
In 2008, the printing plants in Denmark 
worked intensively on a project with the target 
of mapping and reducing the number of 
CRAN (Carcinogenic, Reprotoxic, Allergenic 
and Neurotoxic) substances. The project 
was successfully finalised, the total number 
of chemicals used were reduced, and some 
were changed to less harmful products. The 
German print plant substituted petrol cleaning 
fluid used for cleaning the mailroom equipment 
with a new and safe type of cleaning fluid. In 
2008 the Norwegian print plants switched 
from “Transport 100” to “Rig wash” detergent 
used for cleaning press components because 
the latter was more environmentally friendly.
Energy 
All the Group’s printing plants use electricity, 
gas, oil, other energy sources and water as 
efficiently as possible and monitor the energy 
consumption associated with its activities. 
As shown in the next table, the use of 
electricity per ton of printed paper has 
increased marginally in 2008 primarily as a 
result of the increased demand for full colour 
printing, which consumes more energy than 
single colour printing. In addition, building and 
testing of new print presses in the Netherlands 
led to the increase of energy consumption. 
However, once completed, these new 
presses should result in greater efficiency 
leading to better control and a reduction 
of energy consumption. The increase of 
energy consumption in Denmark has arisen 
because print volume has decreased more 
than expected and faster than the possible 
optimisation of production and presses. Such 
optimisation is continuing in order to reduce 
energy consumption.

Waste 
The policy of the Group is to reduce wastage 
insofar as possible given the needs of the 
business, and to recycle all waste materials 
that are recyclable. 
Recyclable waste
In 2008, the Group recycled 100 per cent of 
waste paper, cores and reel-ends. One of 
the first projects initiated by the ESG was to 
share knowledge on the reduction of start-up 
waste while maintaining the print quality. Half 
of the sites which took part in this project had 
a steady improvement throughout the project 
period which lasted for four months. Five of 
the sites showed more than 20 per cent 
improvement from the start of the project. 
At the end of the project period, the amount 
of press start waste was reduced by 7 per 
cent corresponding to a yearly amount of 456 
tonnes reduction in paper use. The importance 
of accurate production reporting is clearly 
demonstrated through this project and all the 
sites now have better analytical tools at hand 
in order to fight start waste. 
Paper waste from the printing process and 
returned unsold newspapers are sold for 
recycling. Paper waste statistics are provided 
in the table below. The 2007 figures in the table 
below were adjusted and recalculated from 
last year following a review of the definitions to 
ensure like-for-like comparisons between the 
divisions. The definition of waste paper has 
been amended to include cores and reel-ends 
and exclude inserts and all other paper waste 
which does not relate to newsprint. 
The percentage of waste paper has reduced 
slightly in 2008. The differences in waste 
rates between the countries can be explained 
by the differences in the printed products. 
The smaller the circulation of a print run 
and the more colour in that run, the larger 
the percentage of waste. This is particularly 
applicable to Media Regionalne whose printed 
products are primarily regional weeklies, bi-
weeklies and monthlies with low circulation, 
and to some extent Edda Media whose daily 
local newspapers have low circulation.

Non-recyclable waste
Hazardous wastage is kept to a minimum 
and where usage of hazardous substances is 
unavoidable, they are stored and disposed of 
in accordance with local laws and regulations. 
Each division in the Group also seeks where 
possible to use and/or develop energy-
saving materials and environmentally friendly 
technologies with particular focus on key 
chemicals. 
As stated last year, Computer to Plate (“CTP”) 
processes to eliminate the chemicals used 
during the old film-to-plate processes had 
been implemented in all but two plants in 
the Netherlands and three plants in Poland. 
The remaining plants in the Netherlands 
and another plant in Poland successfully 
implemented CTP processes in 2008. 
In Norway, the transition from silver-based to 
polymer-based printing plates was finalised 
during 2008. The plates are significantly more 
environmentally friendly and the waste from 
the processors is now free of silver residues. 
The amount of processor waste was reduced 
by 52 per cent. The waste is collected in 
closed tanks and delivered for destruction.
ARTWORK NOTE: BASELINE GRID IS BEING USED ON THIS JOB 45
Overview
Environmental management systems
In 2008, the Group operated 25 printing plants 
of which seven are in the Netherlands, five in 
Denmark, four in Norway, eight in Poland (six 
of which are owned by Media Regionalne and 
two by Presspublica) and one in Germany. 
Of these, five of the plants in the Netherlands 
and one of Presspublica’s plants are already 
ISO14001 certified. In addition, a further 
two plants in Denmark have 9001:2001 
certification. The Group continues to carry 
out a risk assessment of each print plant once 
every two years.
One of the Group’s objectives is that all 
printing plants will work towards obtaining an 
ISO14001 certification in the next two years. 
Three printing plants in Denmark obtained 
ISO14001 certification in 2008. During 2008, 
the Norwegian printing plants also applied 
for the “Svanemerket” (a Scandinavian Eco-
label which can be used on paper and other 
products which fit certain environmental 
standards). 
A number of Media Regionalne printing plants 
have installed movement sensors in the 
administration area of the printing plants in 
order to save energy. 
Our Dutch division is working on obtaining the 
Forest Stewardship Council (“FSC”) Standard 
for Chain of Custody Certification for one of 
their print plants. Not only does this support 
our environmental aims and policies, products 
carrying an FSC label are independently 
certified to assure consumers that they come 
from forests that are managed to meet the 
social, economic and ecological needs of 
present and future generations.

Governance
The Board
Alasdair Locke (55)
Chairman
Alasdair Locke joined Mecom in June 2006 
as a non-executive director and became the 
Chairman in January 2009. He is executive 
chairman of Abbot Group Limited and, in 
addition to having been involved in the oil 
and shipping industry since 1974, has held 
senior executive positions within the banking 
industry. 
Chairman of the Remuneration and 
Nomination Committees and member of the 
Audit Committee.
David Montgomery (60)
Chief Executive 
David Montgomery founded Mecom in 
2000 and was the Executive Chairman until 
January 2009. He has worked on a number 
of acquisitions in Europe to establish Mecom 
as one of the leading European publishing and 
content businesses. Prior to becoming editor 
of the News of the World in 1985, he was 
managing director of News UK Limited, editor 
of the Today newspaper and a non-executive 
director of Satellite Television plc. Between 
1992 and 1999, he was chief executive 
of Mirror Group plc, where he oversaw its 
substantial restructuring. 
Keith Allen (48)
Chief Operating Officer 
Keith Allen joined Mecom in 2004, became 
Group Finance Director in June 2006, and 
then Chief Operating Officer in March 2008. A 
chartered accountant, he joined the corporate 
finance division of Hambros Bank Limited 
in 1989, becoming a director and head 
of the media team in 1997. In 1998 he left 
Hambros to become joint head of the newly 
established corporate finance division at BNP, 
and following BNP’s acquisition of Paribas in  
2000 he assumed responsibility for the UK 
media team. 
Henry Davies (41)
Group Finance Director
Henry Davies joined the Board of Mecom 
in January 2009 as acting Group Finance 
Director and was appointed the Group Finance 
Director in February 2009. He qualified as an 
accountant and spent 10 years with Price 
Waterhouse. Before joining Mecom as Group 
Financial Controller in 2007, he had been 
group controller at DS Smith plc and Eastern 
Group plc.
Stephen Davidson (53)
Senior Independent Director
Stephen Davidson joined Mecom in January 
2009 as Senior Independent Director. He is 
currently the chairman of Datatec Ltd and 
Digital Marketing Group plc, and a non-
executive director of Inmarsat plc. He has 
held various positions in investment banking, 
most recently at West LB Panmure where 
he was global head of media and telecoms 
investment banking, then vice chairman of 
investment banking. From 1992 to 1998 he 
was finance director, then chief executive 
officer of Telewest Communications plc. He 
was chairman of the Cable Communications 
Association from 1996 to 1998. 
Chairman of the Audit Committee and 
member of the Remuneration and Nomination 
Committees.

who was the Group Finance Director became the Chief Operating

executive director, became a non-executive director with effect from

As announced on 16 January 2009, John Allwood, Robin Miller, Jan 
Houwert, John McNeil, Richard North and Rob Pieterse resigned as 
directors of the Company. John Allwood also resigned as Group 
Finance Director on the same day. At the same time, the Company 
also announced that Alasdair Locke would become Chairman of 
the Company with David Montgomery remaining as Chief Executive 
thereby separating the roles of Chairman and Chief Executive. 
Stephen Davidson was appointed the Senior Independent Director 
on 16 January 2009. Henry Davies joined the Board as acting Group 
Finance Director on 16 January 2009 and became the Group 
Finance Director on 13 February 2009.
In accordance with the Articles of Association, David Montgomery 
and Keith Allen retire by rotation and, being eligible, will offer 
themselves for re-election at the 2009 Annual General Meeting 
(“AGM”). At the same meeting, Stephen Davidson and Henry Davies, 
who were appointed as directors on 16 January 2009, will retire in 
accordance with the Articles of Association and offer themselves 
for re-appointment.
Directors’ insurance
As permitted by the Companies Act 2006, the Company purchases 
and maintains Directors’ and officers’ insurance cover against 
certain legal liabilities and costs incurred by the directors and 
officers of the Group companies in the execution of their duties.
The Company also granted an indemnity to each of its directors in 
accordance with section 232 of the Companies Act 2006 in relation 
to the directors’ exercise of their powers, duties and responsibilities 
as directors of the Company, save to the extent that any such 
indemnity would be void under the Companies Act 2006.
Directors’ conflicts of interest
The Company’s Articles of Association were amended at the 2008 
Annual General Meeting to enable the Board to authorise conflicts 
of interest matters pursuant to section 175 of the Companies Act 
2006. The Board has put in place the procedures as recommended 
by the GC100 that any potential conflicts of interest are authorised 
by the Board and such procedures have been complied with.

Takeovers Directive
Pursuant to section 992 of the Companies Act 2006, which 
implements the EU Takeovers Directive, the Company is required to 
disclose the following additional information:
Appointment and replacement of directors
The Articles of Association of the Company (“Articles”) provide that 
the number of directors shall be no less than two and no more than 
15. Directors may be appointed by the Company by ordinary 
resolution or by the Board. A director appointed by the Board shall 
hold office only until the next annual general meeting and shall then 
be eligible for election, but shall not be taken into account in 
determining the directors or the number of directors who are to 
retire by rotation at that meeting. The Board may from time to time 
appoint one or more directors to hold executive office with the 
Company for such period (subject to the provisions of the Companies 
Acts) and upon such terms as the Board may decide and may 
revoke or terminate any appointment so made. In addition, any 
director who would not otherwise be required to retire shall retire by 
rotation at the third annual general meeting after his last appointment 
or re-appointment. 
At every annual general meeting of the Company, a minimum of 
one-third of the directors shall retire by rotation. The first directors to 
retire by rotation shall be those who wish to retire and not offer 
themselves for re-election. Any further directors so to retire shall be 
those of the other directors subject to retirement by rotation who 
have been longest in office since their last election or re-election 
but, as between persons who became or were last elected or re-
elected directors on the same day, those to retire shall (unless they 
otherwise agree among themselves) be determined by lot. 
The shareholders of the Company may by ordinary resolution 
remove any director before the expiration of his term of office. No 
special notice need be given of any resolution to remove a director 
in accordance with the Articles and no director proposed to be 
removed in accordance with the Article has any special right to 
protest against his removal. A person ceases to be a director as 
soon as: 
(i) that person ceases to be a director by virtue of any provision of 
the Companies Act 2006 or is prohibited from being a director 
by law; 
(ii) a bankruptcy order is made against that person; 
(iii) a composition is made with that person’s creditors generally in 
satisfaction of that person’s debts; 
(iv) a registered medical practitioner who is treating that person 
gives a written opinion to the Company stating that that person 
has become physically or mentally incapable of acting as a 
director and may remain so for more than three months; 
(v) by reason of that person’s mental health, a court makes an 
order which wholly or partly prevents that person from personally 
exercising any powers or rights which that person would 
otherwise have; 
(vi) notification is received by the Company from the director that 
the director is resigning or retiring from office, and such 
resignation or retirement has taken effect in accordance with its 
terms, or his office as a director is vacated pursuant to Article 
119; or  50 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Governance
(vii) that person receives notice signed by not less than three-
quarters of the other directors stating that that person should 
cease to be a director. In calculating the number of directors 
who are required to give such notice to the director, (a) an 
alternate director appointed by him acting in his capacity as 
such shall be excluded; and (b) a director and any alternate 
director appointed by him and acting in his capacity as such 
shall constitute a single director for this purpose, so that notice 
by either shall be sufficient.
Powers of the directors
Subject to the Company’s Memorandum of Association and the 
Articles, the Companies Acts and any directions given by special 
resolution, the business of the Company will be managed by the 
Board who may exercise all the powers of the Company, whether 
relating to the management of the business of the Company or not, 
including powers relating to the issue and/or buying back of the 
Company’s shares. In particular, the Board may exercise all the 
powers of the Company to borrow money and mortgage or charge 
any of its undertakings, property and assets and uncalled capital 
and to issue debentures and other securities for any debt, liability or 
obligation of the Company to any third party. The directors have 
authority in place for them to allot relevant securities (as defined in 
section 80 of the Companies Act 1985) up to an aggregate nominal 
amount of £2,594,131. This authority expires at the 2009 AGM.
The directors have the authority for purchase by the Company of its 
own shares up to a maximum of 10 per cent of the issued share 
capital of the Company. No purchases have been made under this 
authority as at the date of this report. This authority expires at the 
2009 AGM.
Further details on the renewal of authorities are contained in  
the Chairman’s letter to shareholders accompanying the Notice  
of AGM.
Significant agreements
Under the new Takeover Directive, a company is required to disclose 
any significant agreements to which the Company is party that take 
effect, alter or terminate upon a change of control of the Company 
following a takeover bid, and the effects of any such agreements. 
On 31 October 2007 (as amended by an amendment and 
restatement agreement dated 6 November 2007), the Company 
entered into a €1 billion credit facility agreement between, amongst 
others, the Company, ING Bank NV (as “Facility Agent”) and the 
banks and institutions named therein as original lenders (the 
“Facility”), whereby upon a change of control (subject to an 
agreement not being reached with the Company within 15 days of 
the Facility Agent notifying the lenders of such change of control) 
the total commitments of the original lenders under the Facility will 
be cancelled and all outstanding utilisations, ancillary outstandings, 
accrued interest and other amounts accrued under the finance 
documents shall become immediately due and payable. 
The Company is in the process of negotiating amendments to this 
credit facility with the original lenders. It is not expected that the 
provision relating to a change of control and its effect on the total 
commitments outstanding will change.
For these purposes, a change of control occurs if any person or 
group of persons acting in concert gains control of the Company. 
The change of control provisions for the various share schemes 
operated by the Company are provided in the Remuneration report 
on pages 58 to 63.
Rights attaching to shares
The Company has one class of ordinary shares and the rights 
attaching to the ordinary shares in addition to those conferred on 
their holders by law are defined in the Articles, copies of which can 
be obtained from the Company Secretary. A shareholder whose 
name appears on the Company’s register of members can choose 
whether his shares are evidenced by share certificates (in certificated 
form) or held in electronic (uncertificated) form in CREST (the 
electronic settlement system in the United Kingdom).
Subject to any restrictions below, shareholders may attend any 
general meeting of the Company and, on a show of hands, every 
shareholder (or his representative) who is present at a general 
meeting has one vote on each resolution and, on a poll, every 
shareholder (or his representative) who is present has one vote on 
each resolution for every ordinary share of which they are the 
registered shareholder. A resolution put to the vote of a general 
meeting is decided on a show of hands unless (before or on the 
declaration of the result of a vote on a show of hands) a poll is 
demanded by the chairman of the meeting, or by at least five 
shareholders (or their representatives) present in person and having 
the right to vote, or by any shareholders (or their representatives) 
present in person having at least 10 per cent of the total voting 
rights of all shareholders, or by any shareholders (or their 
representatives) present in person holding ordinary shares on which 
an aggregate sum has been paid up of at least 10 per cent of the 
total sum paid up on all ordinary shares.
Shareholders can declare final dividends by passing an ordinary 
resolution but the amount of the dividends cannot exceed the 
amount recommended by the Board. The Board can pay interim 
dividends on any class of shares of the amounts and on the dates 
and for the periods they decide provided the distributable profits of 
the Company justify such payment. The Board may, if authorised by 
an ordinary resolution of the shareholders, offer any shareholder the 
right to elect to receive new ordinary shares, which will be credited 
as fully paid, instead of their cash dividend.
Voting at general meetings
Any form of proxy sent by the Company to shareholders in relation 
to any general meeting must be delivered to the Company, whether 
in written form or in electronic form, not less than 48 hours before 
the time appointed for holding the meeting or adjourned meeting at 
which the person named in the appointment proposes to vote.
No shareholder is, unless the Board decides otherwise, entitled to 
attend or vote either personally or by proxy at a general meeting or 
to exercise any other right conferred by being a shareholder if he or 
any person with an interest in shares has been sent a notice under 
section 793 of the Companies Act 2006 (which confers upon public 
companies the power to require information with respect to interests 
in their voting shares) and he or any interested person failed to 
supply the Company with the information requested within 14 days 
after delivery of that notice. The Board may also decide where the 
relevant shareholding comprises at least 0.25 per cent of the 
nominal value of the issued shares of that class that no dividend is 
payable in respect of those default shares and that no transfer of 
any default shares shall be registered.
Transfers of shares
The Board may refuse to register a transfer of a certificated share 
which is not fully paid, provided that the refusal does not prevent 
dealings in shares in the Company from taking place on an open 
and proper basis. The Board may also refuse to register a transfer 
of a certificated share unless: (i) the instrument of transfer is lodged, 
Directors’ report continued 51
Governance
duly stamped (if stampable), at the registered office of the Company 
or any other place decided by the Board, accompanied by the 
certificate for the share to which it relates and such other evidence 
as the Board may reasonably require to show the right of the 
transferor to make the transfer; (ii) is in respect of only one class of 
shares; and (iii) is in favour of not more than four transferees.
Transfers of uncertificated shares must be carried out using CREST 
and the Board can refuse to register a transfer of an uncertificated 
share in accordance with the regulations governing the operation  
of CREST.
Variation of rights
If at any time the capital of the Company is divided into different 
classes of shares, the special rights attaching to any class may be 
varied or revoked either: (i) with the written consent of the holders of 
at least 75 per cent in nominal value of the issues shares of the 
class; or (ii) with the sanction of a special resolution passed at a 
separate general meeting of the holders of the shares of the class. 
Without prejudice to any rights conferred on the holders of any 
existing shares or class of shares, any share may be issued with or 
have attached to it such rights and restrictions as the Company may 
from time to time by ordinary resolution determine, or in the absence 
of such a resolution, as the Board may determine.
Exercise of Rights in Employee Share Schemes
The Company operates an employee benefit trust (“EBT”) for the 
benefit of past, current and future employees of the Group. It was 
primarily established for the operation of the Share Incentive Plan 
(“SIP”). During the year a linking agreement has been entered into 
between the trustee of the EBT and the Company so that the shares 
required to satisfy the Company’s obligations under the Executive 
Share Option Plan and Deferred Bonus Plan may be acquired by the 
EBT. Further details on the number of ordinary shares to be acquired 
by the trustee of EBT for the purpose of the SIP are detailed in the 
Remuneration report on page 60. The trustee has not acquired or 
been granted any shares at the date of this report. No shares are 
currently held by the EBT therefore the trustees do not have any 
voting rights currently.
Directors’ compensation
In accordance with the new Takeover Directive, the Company is 
required to disclose any agreements between the Company and  
its directors or employees providing for compensation for loss of 
office or employment that occurs because of a takeover bid. The 
agreements between the Company and its Executive Directors 
which satisfy this requirement are disclosed in the Remuneration 
report on pages 58 to 63.
