Statement of directors’ responsibilities in relation to 
the preparation of financial statements
The directors are responsible for preparing the Annual report and 
accounts in accordance with applicable United Kingdom law and 
those International Financial Reporting Standards as adopted by 
the European Union, or in the case of the Company’s financial 
statements, the applicable accounting standards in the United 
Kingdom.
In relation to the consolidated financial statements, the directors are 
required to prepare financial statements for each financial year 
which present fairly the financial position of the Group and its 
financial performance and cash flows for that period. In relation to 
the Company’s financial statements, the directors are required by 
law to prepare financial statements for each financial year that give 
a true and fair view of the state of the affairs of the Company and its 
profit and loss for that period. In preparing the consolidated and 
Company financial statements, the directors are required to: 
select suitable accounting policies and then apply them •	
consistently;
present information including accounting policies in a manner •	
that provides relevant, reliable, comparable and understandable 
information;
provide additional disclosures when compliance with the •	
specific requirements in applicable accounting standards are 
insufficient to enable users to understand the impact of particular 
transactions, other events and conditions of the entity’s financial 
position and performance; and
state that the Group has complied with the applicable accounting •	
standards, subject to any material departures disclosed and 
explained in the financial statements. 
The directors are responsible for keeping proper accounting records 
which disclose with reasonable accuracy at any time the financial 
position of the Group and of the Company, and enable them to 
ensure that the financial statements comply with the Companies 
Acts. They are also responsible for safeguarding the assets of the 
Group and hence for taking reasonable steps for the prevention and 
detection of fraud and other irregularities.
The Annual report and accounts of the Group and of the Company 
are also published on Mecom’s website. The maintenance and 
integrity of Mecom’s website is the responsibility of the directors. 
Legislation in the United Kingdom governing the preparation and 
the dissemination of financial statements may differ from legislation 
in other jurisdictions.
Responsibility statement
The directors confirm to the best of their knowledge that:
(a) the financial statements for the year ended 31 December 2008, 
prepared in accordance with the applicable United Kingdom 
law and those International Financial Reporting Standards as 
adopted by the European Union, give a true and fair view of the 
assets, liabilities, financial position and profit or loss of the Group 
and the undertakings included in the consolidation taken as a 
whole; and 
(b) the business review includes a fair review of the development 
and performance of the business and the position of the Group, 
together with a description of the principal risks and uncertainties 
that they face.

Governance
The Board is committed to maintaining high standards of corporate 
governance. The Board considers that the Company has during 
2008 complied with the provisions of the Combined Code on 
Corporate Governance (the “Code”), save for areas where an 
explanation has been provided below. Further details of how the 
principles of the Code have been applied for the year 2008 are set 
out below and in the Remuneration report on pages 58 to 63. 
The Board
The Board is collectively responsible for the success of the Company 
and sets the strategy and objectives of the Group. It formulates the 
values and standards within the Code of Business Conduct which 
is available on Mecom’s website and ensures that the Company’s 
obligations to its shareholders and other stakeholders are 
understood and met. 
At the beginning of 2008, the Board comprised eight members 
being the Executive Chairman, two other executive directors and 
five non-executive directors. At the end of 2008, the Board consisted 
of nine members, six of whom were non-executive directors. Keith 
Allen, who was previously Group Finance Director, became the 
Chief Operating Officer with effect from 14 March 2008 and John 
Allwood who had joined the Board on 27 February 2008 was 
appointed as Group Finance Director on 14 March 2008. Jan 
Houwert, who was previously an executive director, became a non-
executive director with effect from 8 May 2008. All other directors 
served throughout 2008. 
As announced on 16 January 2009, John Allwood, Robin Miller, Jan 
Houwert, John McNeil, Richard North and Rob Pieterse resigned as 
directors of the Company. At the same time Stephen Davidson was 
appointed the Senior Independent Director and Henry Davies was 
appointed acting Group Finance Director. Henry Davies became the 
Group Finance Director on 13 February 2009. The Board currently 
comprises three executive directors and two non-executive directors 
including the Chairman and biographies of each Board member are 
presented on page 47. 
The Code recommends the separation of the roles of the Chairman 
and the Chief Executive and as disclosed last year, the Company 
has given an undertaking that the roles will be separated. Accordingly 
on 16 January 2009 the Company announced that Alasdair Locke 
would become the Chairman of the Company and David Montgomery 
would remain as Chief Executive. There is a clear division of 
responsibility between the Chairman and the Chief Executive set 
out in writing and agreed by the Board. Alasdair Locke as Chairman, 
is responsible for leadership of the Board, ensuring its effectiveness 
on all aspects. He also ensures effective communication with 
shareholders. David Montgomery, the Chief Executive reports to the 
Board and is responsible for running the Group’s business.
The Chief Executive’s other business commitments are disclosed in 
the Remuneration report on page 61 and there have been no 
significant changes during the year relating to these commitments.
There is a schedule of matters reserved for the decision of the Board 
including the approval of acquisitions and disposals, investment 
strategy, dividend policy, capital expenditure, significant contractual 
commitments, Group borrowings, issues of securities, approval of 
the annual report and financial statements, and the Group annual 
operating plan and budget. Certain decision-making and operational 
matters are delegated to senior management including Country 
CEOs and CFOs, who are responsible on a day-to-day basis for the 
operation of their division as well as the application of the processes 
and procedures supporting the strategic objectives. The Board also 
Corporate governance
considered reports from the Executive Chairman and the Group 
Finance Director at each of its scheduled meetings for the year 
under review. 
The Board delegates specific responsibilities to the Audit, 
Nomination and Remuneration Committees. Each Committee has

available on Mecom’s website. Reports of these Committees are 
set out on pages 54 to 56. All directors received copies of all 
Committee minutes and the Chairman of each Committee provides 
an update on matters of significance at the Board meeting following

The Board is provided with timely information in a form and of a

The Board is committed to ensuring that directors continually

became a member of the Committee. Stephen Davidson was

Meeting
The Committee meets at least three times a year and met five times 
during the year under review. Attendance of the Committee 
members is shown on page 53. Only members of the Committee 
have the right to attend the meetings of the Committee. However, 
other individuals such as the Group Finance Director, Head of Group

Role
The Committee’s terms of reference are available on Mecom’s 
website and are reviewed annually to ensure that they continue to 
meet best practice. The principal responsibilities of the Committee 
include: 
Monitoring the integrity of the financial statements, including •	
annual and half-year reports, interim management statements, 
preliminary results announcements and any other formal 
announcement relating to financial performance.
Reviewing the effectiveness of systems of internal control and •	
management of risks, including approving statements 
concerning internal control and risk management in the annual 
report.
Reviewing the activities, organisational structure and the •	
effectiveness of the internal audit function.
Reviewing and approving changes to the Group’s key accounting •	
policies.
Making recommendations to the Board, to be put to •	
shareholders, for approval at the annual general meeting, in 
relation to the appointment, re-appointment and removal of the 
external auditor.
Reviewing and monitoring of the external auditors’ independence, •	
objectivity and effectiveness of the audit process.
Setting and approving policy on non-audit services, and •	
approving audit fees and non-audit services.
The Group’s internal audit function which is led by the Head of 
Group Audit reports to the Committee and the Group Finance 
Director. The purpose of the Group’s internal audit function is to 
review and test key internal controls on which management seeks 
to place reliance in its mitigation of risk. Where necessary it will 
make recommendations for improvement in controls and follow up 
with management to ensure that agreed actions are taken on a 
timely basis. The Committee receives internal audit reports from the 
Head of Group Audit at every Committee meeting covering areas 
such as effectiveness of financial and IT controls that support 
reliable financial reporting, project management of change initiatives 
which are driving the Group’s transition to a content and consumer 
business and security over the websites of the Group which allow 
customers access to the online services and products of the Group. 
The Committee chairman reports on the key items at Board 
meetings. Following the creation of an internal audit function in 
2007, the Committee has reviewed its effectiveness in 2008 and will 
continue to monitor, and provide direction to its activities.
The Committee regularly monitors and approves all services being 
provided to the Group by its external auditors and has established 
a pre-approval requirement for the provision of non-audit services 
to ensure that there is no impairment of auditor independence. For 
this purpose auditing the accounts of subsidiaries and associates 
pursuant to legislation and other services provided pursuant to 
legislation are regarded as audit services. The pre-approval 
requirement is subject to annual review by the Committee. The fees 
for audit services and non-audit services provided by the external 
auditors are disclosed in Note 7 to the consolidated financial 
statements. 
An evaluation of the effectiveness of the external audit process was 
carried out in 2008 by the Head of Group Audit taking into account 
the views of the relevant senior management and the Committee 
members. The results of evaluation were discussed with the external 
auditors. Ernst & Young LLP was appointed external auditors of the 
Company in 2005. Since then the Committee has not considered 
tendering the audit given the significant changes that have taken 
place within the Group that required continuity and an in-depth 
knowledge of the Group by its auditors. Going forward, the Audit 
Committee intends to tender the external audit every five years.
The Committee is also responsible for reviewing the arrangement 
for employees to raise any concerns they may have, in confidence, 
about possible wrongdoing, dishonest or unethical behaviour. A 
whistleblowing policy is in place and the Code of Conduct protects 
anyone that steps forward to make such a disclosure. Should a 
disclosure be made, the Head of Group Audit, in consultation with 
the Company Secretary will decide an appropriate method and level 
of investigation. The Committee is notified of all disclosures, results 
of investigations and actions taken, and has the power to conduct 
further inquiries itself or order additional actions as it sees fit. 
Internal control and risk management
The Board (through delegation to the Audit Committee) recognises 
that it has ultimate responsibility for the Group’s system of internal 
control and maintains a sound system of internal control to safeguard 
shareholders’ investment and the Group’s assets. No system of 
internal control can provide absolute assurance against material 
misstatement or loss. Instead the Company operates a system 
which is designed to manage rather than eliminate the risk of failure 
to achieve business objectives and to provide the Board with 
reasonable assurance that problems are identified on a timely basis 
and dealt with appropriately. 
The Group follows a process of identifying, assessing and managing 
the significant risks faced by divisional businesses and by the Group 
as a whole. The key aspects of this process are summarised as 
follows:
The Board and management
The Group carries out a comprehensive annual strategy review 
which is supported by a budgeting and planning process whereby 
detailed operating budgets for the following financial year are 
prepared by divisional and corporate management for approval by 
the Board. The day-to-day management is undertaken by the senior 
management of the divisions and of the Group who have the 
responsibility for providing visible leadership and ensuring that risk 
management is integrated into all operations and functions. 56 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Governance
Organisational structure and authorisation procedure
The Group has an established organisation structure with clearly 
stated delegated responsibility and reporting. Authorisation 
procedures in respect of matters such as capital expenditure, 
acquisitions, investments or disposals and treasury transactions 
are clearly defined and communicated across the Group. 
Risk assessment
In reviewing the effectiveness of the Group’s system of internal 
control, the Board first considers the risk management system and 
all aspects of risks which include strategic, financial, operational 
and compliance risks. It then considers whether the key controls 
designed to mitigate these risks are working as intended for both 
“business as usual” and the “strategic initiatives” that will drive 
change across the divisions, business units and joint-ventures. This 
approach improves the effectiveness of control without necessarily 
increasing the number or cost of controls in the business. 
The Corporate Risk Register (the “Register”) provides a consistent 
method for managing and reporting risks across the Group and 
ensures that significant risks are understood and visible to divisional 
and corporate management, as well as to the Board. The Register 
sets out the top risks as defined by divisional and corporate 
management. The Head of Group Audit discusses risk with the 
Country CEOs and prioritises the top risks against the likelihood of 
occurrence and impact on achievement of the Group’s objectives. 
The Register, which also sets out the mitigating controls and actions, 
is reviewed and assessed on a quarterly basis by the Board. A 
summary of the principal risks and uncertainties facing the Group is 
provided on pages 38 to 39.
In line with the Turnbull Guidance, the process for identifying, 
monitoring and reporting risks is reviewed regularly by the Board 
based on the recommendations of the Audit Committee. The 
process described has been in place for the year under review and 
up to the date of the approval of this Annual report and accounts.
Financial and management reporting
The results of the business units are reported to the Group on a 
monthly basis and monitored against budget and latest forecasts. 
The controls that support the Group’s financial reporting procedures 
are considered as part of the Group’s ongoing risk assessment 
process and are reviewed for effectiveness by the Group’s internal 
audit function.
Reviewing and monitoring the effectiveness of internal controls
The Group’s internal control framework is based on the Board’s 
assessment of risk and comprises a combination of self-assessment, 
management oversight and independent review by the Group’s 
internal audit function. 
In having regard to this framework, the Audit Committee’s activities 
during the year under review included:
Reviewing the work of management and the Group’s reporting •	
accountants in preparing for the move of the Company’s shares 
from AIM to the main list of the London Stock Exchange in April 
2008. This included a review of the Group’s risk management 
system, financial reporting procedures and working capital 
projections at that time.
Monitoring the implementation of standard policies and •	
procedures across the Group. These policies and procedures 
relate primarily to financial reporting, accounting policies, risk 
management and internal control. Each business had, at the 
time of acquisition by Mecom, its own set of financial policies 
and procedures which, whilst providing for locally-oriented 
financial reporting and internal control, were necessarily not 
common across the enlarged Group and required improvement 
to deal with the standards expected of a fully listed company in 
the United Kingdom. New systems implementations and the 
effect of business reorganisations have delayed the complete 
roll-out in the Group’s Danish and Norwegian businesses, but 
continues to receive management priority. During the year the 
Committee received, and continues to receive, regular reports 
from the Head of Group Audit on the status of this  
implementation.
Considering recent guidance issued by the Financial Reporting •	
Council on the financial control and reporting implications in  
the light of the current economic conditions. The Committee 
has received reports on relevant issues from management and 
at each of its meetings since the guidance was issued has 
reviewed a schedule of the Group’s position for each of the 
questions raised.
The Board is satisfied that the information it received throughout  
the year enabled it to formally complete its annual review of the 
effectiveness of the Group’s system of internal control. In conducting 
its review, the Board has identified certain aspects of internal control 
which require improvement. Progress in these areas continues to 
be reviewed on a regular basis and additional steps have been 
taken to further embed risk management and internal control into all 
operations of the Group.
Financial reporting
Through the detailed reviews of the Group’s performance  
and financial position, together with the Directors’ report and  
the financial statements thereto, the Board seeks to present a 
balanced and understandable assessment of the Group’s position 
and prospects. A statement of the directors’ responsibilities in 
preparing the financial statements and a statement by the external 
auditors on their reporting responsibilities are presented on pages 
52 and 65 accordingly. 
Communication with shareholders
The Board as a whole has the responsibility for ensuring that a 
satisfactory dialogue with shareholders takes place. It encourages 
two-way communication with both its institutional and private 
shareholders and responds quickly to all queries received orally or 
in writing. During the year under review, Robin Miller as the Senior 
Independent Director, was available to the shareholders to 
understand their views and to address any issues they may have 
had. From 16 January 2009, Alasdair Locke as Chairman and 
Stephen Davidson as the Senior Independent Director have been 
and are available to the shareholders. In order to develop an 
understanding of the views of the major shareholders, the Board 
receives, with the papers circulated before each Board meeting, 
analysts’ and brokers’ reports and briefings as well as a summary of 
the main movements in shareholdings. 
Corporate governance continued 57
Governance
Shareholders are kept informed of the progress and performance of 
the Group through the annual report, half-year results, interim 
management statements and the AGM. This information and other 
significant announcements of the Group are released to the London 
Stock Exchange and are made available on Mecom’s website.
Notice of the AGM and related papers are sent to shareholders at 
least 20 working days before the meeting. The Chairmen of the 
Audit, Remuneration and Nomination Committees will be available 
at the AGM to answer any queries. In addition, the Chairman 
encourages all directors to attend the AGM so shareholders will 
have an opportunity to meet them. Voting on resolutions is 
conducted by polls at general meetings and voting results are 
announced through the London Stock Exchange and are available 
on Mecom’s website or on request.
At the 2008 Annual General Meeting, the Company’s Articles of 
Association were amended to permit the Company to send or 
supply communications to shareholders electronically and the 
Company now supplies information such as notices of meetings, 
forms of proxy and the Annual report via the website. Shareholders 
will be notified by email or post when new information is available on 
the website. The Company will continue to send hard copy 
communications to those shareholders who have requested to 
receive communication in hard copy form. Shareholders may at any 
time revoke a previous instruction in order to receive hard copies or 
electronic copies of shareholder information. 58 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Governance
The Directors present their Remuneration report for the year ended 
31 December 2008, which will be submitted to shareholders for 
approval at the forthcoming Annual General Meeting. This report 
has been prepared in accordance with the requirements of Schedule 
7A of the Companies Act 1985 and describes how the principles set 
out in the Combined Code (the “Code”) have been applied. Apart 
from the information relating to the directors’ remuneration, share 
options and share interests on pages 60, 62 and 63, this report is 
not subject to audit.
In this report, the expression “Executive Directors” includes the 
Executive Chairman (for his appointment up to 16 January 2009), 
unless otherwise stated.
Remuneration Committee
Composition
The Remuneration Committee is appointed by the Board and 
consists of independent non-executive directors. John McNeil 
chaired the Remuneration Committee during 2008 (up to his 
resignation on 16 January 2009) and the other members of the 
Committee were Alasdair Locke and Robin Miller (up to his 
resignation on 16 January 2009). Richard North and Rob Pieterse 
were members of the Committee from the beginning of 2008 up  
to April 2008. The Company Secretary acts as Secretary to  
the Committee.
With effect from 13 February 2009, Alasdair Locke was appointed 
the Chairman of the Committee and Stephen Davidson became  
a member of the Committee. The Company recognises the 
recommendation of the Code that the Chairman of the Company 
should not chair the Remuneration Committee. The position will be 
reviewed when new non-executive directors join the Board.
Meetings
The Committee met formally three times during the year under 
review. The attendance of the Committee members is shown on 
page 53. Members of the Committee consulted with relevant parties 
internally, and the Executive Chairman and Group Finance Director 
were invited to attend Committee meetings as appropriate during 
the year under review, although no individual was present during 
discussions relating to his own remuneration.
Role
The Committee’s terms of reference are available on Mecom’s 
website and reviewed annually to ensure that they continue to meet 
best practice. The Committee is responsible for setting the 
framework and policy for the remuneration of the Executive Directors 
and reviewing them annually for appropriateness and relevance. It is 
also responsible for determining the specific elements of the 
Executive Directors’ remuneration, their contractual terms and their 
compensation arrangements. In addition, the Committee monitors 
the level and structure of remuneration for the next most senior 
category of executives and approves the structure and targets for 
their bonus plans. It also oversees any major changes in employee 
benefit structures. 
Independent advice
The Committee has appointed Deloitte LLP (“Deloitte”) as its 
principal external adviser. During the course of the year Deloitte 
provided advice with regard to general remuneration levels and 
comparator group benchmarking to ensure that remuneration 
remains competitive and in line with best practice. Deloitte have 
also provided ad hoc finance and tax advice to the Company and 
the Group during the year. 
Remuneration policy
The Committee’s primary objective is to ensure that reward 
packages for directors and senior managers are competitive in 
order to attract and retain the best talents, and are directly  
linked to the achievement of performance targets that extend 
beyond budget. 
The Committee undertakes an annual review of market practice 
and considers the remuneration levels of directors in companies of 
similar size and complexity both within and outside the industry 
sector. The Group also aims to incentivise and reward its Executive 
Directors in a way that is consistent with the Group’s commercial 
objectives and to align the interests of the directors with those  
of shareholders. To achieve this, the Executive Directors’ total 
remuneration comprises both fixed and variable elements, details of 
which are set out below. 
During 2008 the remuneration packages for the Executive Directors 
consisted of basic salary, benefits and participation in the annual 
bonus scheme and the Deferred Bonus Plan (“DBP”). As founder 
executives of the Company, David Montgomery and Keith Allen also 
participated in the Share Incentive Plan (“SIP”) which was approved 
by shareholders at the time of the Company’s admission to the 
Alternative Investment Market (“AIM”) of the London Stock Exchange 
in 2005. Further details of these arrangements are provided below.
In the event of outstanding performance, the performance-related 
incentives (excluding participation in the SIP) for David Montgomery 
and Keith Allen will equate to approximately 60 per cent of total 
remuneration. If performance is below budget, then no cash bonus 
is payable. 
As disclosed in the Annual Report last year, the remuneration of Jan 
Houwert, an executive director of the Company until 8 May 2008, 
was governed by his pre-existing contract with Wegener. From that 
date, Jan Houwert stepped down as CEO of Wegener and became 
a non-executive director of the Company on the same terms of 
appointment as the other non-executive directors. Jan Houwert’s 
pre-existing contract was superseded when he stepped down as 
CEO of Wegener. In addition to his non-executive directorship fees, 
he receives a fixed salary, pension and other benefits in consideration 
for providing consultancy services and advice to Wegener’s 
Supervisory Board under a contract entered into with Wegener on 
3 March 2008. 
Salary
Basic salaries are reviewed annually by the Committee. The aim of 
the Group is to provide a competitive remuneration package to 
attract, retain and motivate key executives. Basic salaries are 
intended to provide market competitive levels of reward for the role 
and individual contribution. Basic salaries for 2008 and 2009 have 
been set within a market competitive range derived from analysis of 
salaries paid by companies within the FTSE All Share index, taking 
account of the relative complexity and size of the index constituents 
compared with Mecom. 
When positioning the Executive Directors’ basic salaries the 
Committee considers:
salary levels for similar jobs in relevant comparator companies; •	
specific factors relating to the individual (including personal •	
performance, experience and the individual’s role within the 
Group);
an enhanced or reduced scope or responsibility compared with •	
the norm for a given role;
Remuneration report 59
Governance
the balance between fixed and variable reward; and •	
relative remuneration levels throughout the Group. •	
Basic salaries during 2008 were £540,000 for David Montgomery, 
£350,000 for John Allwood and £325,000 for Keith Allen. With effect 
from 1 January 2009, these remain unchanged. Following the 
resignation of John Allwood, he is entitled to receive his medical 
insurance benefit and his pension entitlement up to 31 March 2009. 
Jan Houwert, who was an executive director from 1 January 2008 
up to 8 May 2008, received a basic annual salary of €412,452. With 
effect from 8 May 2008, he received a fee of £45,000 per annum as 
a non-executive director. Henry Davies, who was appointed Group 
Finance Director on 13 February 2009, receives a basic salary of 
£250,000 with effect from his appointment to the Board.
The Committee is of the view that in each case these basic salary 
levels reflect the competitive market level for the role and the 
individual’s contribution.
Annual bonus and Deferred Bonus Plan (“DBP”)
The purpose of the annual bonus and DBP is to incentivise and 
reward Executive Directors and senior executives for the  
achievement of annual Group and divisional targets, to encourage 
share ownership and to facilitate retention of key individuals.
Annual bonuses for Executive Directors and senior executives  
(in particular Country CEOs) are determined by reference to 
performance targets set by the Remuneration Committee. The 
performance targets are reviewed annually and relate to financial 
budgets, which are commercially sensitive and are therefore not 
disclosed in this report. 
The maximum 2008 annual cash bonus that could be earned by the 
Executive Directors and senior executives was 100 per cent of basic 
salary (Jan Houwert was not entitled to any bonus in the year under 
review). For the Executive Directors, their potential annual cash 
bonus was based on achieving or exceeding Group adjusted profit 
before tax (that is, profit before tax stated before exceptional items 
and the amortisation of acquired intangibles). 
In order to encourage share ownership amongst the most senior 
executives, participants are invited to express a preference to 
receive all or part of their bonus in shares, rather than cash, under 
the terms of the DBP prior to the determination of any bonus that 
might be paid. To the extent that a participant opts to receive shares 
rather than cash, he or she will receive an award over shares worth 
150 per cent of the cash bonus that might otherwise have been 
paid. Rights attaching to share awards under the DBP are exercisable 
at the end of a three-year period following the date of the award. In 
the event of a change of control, awards vest in full and may be 
exercised within six months of the change of control (or such earlier 
date as may be specified).
No bonus was payable in cash or shares to the Executive Directors 
who served during 2008 in respect of the year ended 31 December 
2008.
The Committee intends to review the structure and performance 
conditions for the 2009 annual bonus. The level of bonus awarded 
will continue to depend on the level of performance achieved  
and appropriately challenging targets will be set for the level of 
bonus contemplated.
Executive Share Option Plan (“ESOP”)
The purpose of the ESOP is to incentivise and reward Executive 
Directors and senior executives and to align their interests with 
those of shareholders.
There is no consideration payable for the grant of an option, and 
exercise is not conditional upon satisfaction of any performance 
condition for grants made to senior executives. Options will not 
normally be capable of exercise prior to the third anniversary of the 
date of grant and, to the extent not exercised, will lapse no later than 
the tenth anniversary of the date of grant. In the event of a change 
of control occurring within three years of the date of grant, the 
proportion of any option that may be exercised will be determined 
by reference to the period of time elapsed since the date of grant.
Options under the ESOP are not granted to participants in the SIP, 
a category which includes two of the Executive Directors. Prior to 
granting any options to Executive Directors, the Board will consult 
with shareholders as to the appropriate form of performance 
conditions to be attached to the exercise of those options, and 
would subsequently make full disclosure of the performance 
measures adopted. 
The criteria for making grants of share options to senior executives 
is reviewed by the Committee on an annual basis. In 2008, options 
worth up to 100 per cent of salary, with a small number of exceptional 
grants at 125 per cent of salary, were granted to 48 participants 
over approximately 1.4 per cent of the Company’s issued share 
capital.
The Committee intends to review the structure, criteria and quantum 
of long-term incentive awards to senior executives prior to the grant 
(if any) of share options during 2009.
Share Incentive Plan (“SIP”)
The SIP provides the founder executives with a long-term incentive 
linked to the delivery of shareholder value. It is operated via an 
offshore employee benefit trust (“EBT”), established by the Company 
for the benefit of the past, present and future employees of the 
Group following admission of the Company’s shares to trading on 
AIM in 2005.
The Company has granted an option over ordinary shares to the 
Trustee of the EBT generally, the exercise price being the nominal 
value of a share. The number of ordinary shares to be acquired by 
the Trustee on exercise of this option is calculated in accordance 
with a formula that entitles the Trustee to acquire ordinary shares 
with an aggregate value equivalent to 10 per cent of the increase in 
market capitalisation of the Company, less the market value at the 
date of issue of any new equity issued by the Company but adding 
back dividends paid, either five years from the date of admission to 
AIM or earlier in the event of an offer for the Company. This formula 
ensures there is a direct link between the reward that would be  
paid out to the founder executives and the value delivered  
to shareholders.
At the Extraordinary General Meeting held on 5 March 2007 the 
terms of the SIP were amended in certain minor respects relating to 
leaver provisions and the period within which options granted under 
the SIP can be exercised. 60 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Governance
The founder executives who participate in the SIP are David 
Montgomery (35 per cent share), Keith Allen (15 per cent share), 
Robin Miller (7.5 per cent share) and one senior manager. The SIP is 
not open to any other participants and no further awards will be 
made under the SIP. Following the resignation of Robin Miller from 
the Board on 16 January 2009, he is no longer a beneficiary in the 
SIP. In accordance with the SIP plan rules, the interest of the other 
participants will not increase as a consequence of another 
beneficiary ceasing to be a participant.
Had the option vested on 31 December 2008, based on the 
Company’s market capitalisation at that date (calculated by 
reference to the prevailing share price of 1.05 pence), no benefit 
would have been realised by any participant in the SIP.

Dilution
The Company has, at all times, complied with the dilution limit 
contained within the rules of each share plan (principally a limit of 10 
per cent of the issued share capital of the Company in any 10 year 
period) and the Committee reviews the position before any proposed 
grant to ensure this limit is not breached.
Subsisting options granted under the ESOP and DBP to date equate 
to approximately 1.3 per cent of the Company’s current issued 
share capital. As stated above, if the SIP had vested on 31 December 
2008, no shares would have been issuable under the option granted 
to the Trustee. Based on the issued share capital of the Company at 
31 December 2008 but (for the purposes of assessing potential 
dilution) assuming a share price of 75 pence at the date of vesting 
of the SIP awards, the number of shares issuable under the SIP 
would equate to approximately 0.68 per cent of the Company’s 
issued share capital at that date.
Directors’ pension arrangements
The Company has not put in place any pension arrangement for 
Keith Allen. During the year 2008, the Company contributed £100 
per month to a defined contribution pension arrangement for David 
Montgomery. This arrangement was originally set up whilst David 
Montgomery was employed at the Mirror Group plc and was later 
assigned to the Company. With effect from 6 November 2008 this 
arrangement has now ceased. John Allwood received an amount 
equal to 20 per cent of his basic annual salary from the Company as 
a contribution to a pension arrangement nominated by him. 
Following the resignation of John Allwood from the Board on 16 
January 2009, his pension contribution will lapse after 31 March 
2009. Henry Davies who was appointed Group Finance Director on 
13 February 2009 receives 15 per cent of his basic salary from the 
Company as a contribution to a pension arrangement nominated by 
him.
Jan Houwert is entitled to a pension equivalent at age 65 of 2.25 per 
cent of pensionable salary for each year’s pensionable service. 
Pensionable salary is fixed annual salary less the amount covered 
by the Dutch state pension provision. This pension promise is 
funded partly through the Wegener General Pension Fund (“APW”), 
which provides 1.75 per cent of pensionable salary up to the 
maximum allowed under the rules of the APW, and partly through a 
separate top-up arrangement. The APW is a collective defined 
contribution arrangement, and the contribution rates applicable for 
2008 were 16.1 per cent (employer) and 9.6 per cent (employee), 
making 25.7 per cent in total. The cost of the top-up arrangement is 
met by Wegener. Jan Houwert also participates in the FWG VUT (a 
collective bargaining early-retirement arrangement), which provides 
an early retirement pension between the ages of 63 and 65, funded 
by employee and employer contributions. Jan Houwert can take 
early retirement from the age of 62, in which case Wegener will pay 
him the difference between the FWG VUT early retirement pension 
and 70 per cent of his final fixed annual salary until he reaches age 
65. The aggregate pension contributions made by Wegener for the 
benefit of Jan Houwert are disclosed in the Directors’ remuneration 
table on page 62. 
Directors’ service contracts
Each of the Executive Directors has a service contract with the 
Company which can be terminated by either party on 12 months’ 
written notice. Upon leaving service at the request of the Company 
(other than for gross misconduct) the Executive Director is entitled 
to receive predetermined compensation equivalent to 12 months’ 
basic salary and benefits. In the event of a change of control of the 
Company, the Executive Director must be offered employment by 
the Company’s successor or by any company in the Group on 
terms in all respects no less favourable than those applicable 
immediately prior to such change of control. If the Executive Director 
declines this offer, then the Company is entitled to terminate his or 
her contract either by giving the specified notice or by payment of 
the remuneration entitlement corresponding to that notice period.
Jan Houwert’s pre-existing contract of employment with Wegener 
was terminable by either party on six months’ written notice. Had he 
left service at the request of Wegener (other than for gross 
misconduct) or in the event of a change of control of Wegener or as 
a result of internal restructuring, he would have been entitled to 10 
months’ fixed salary and benefits plus 18 months’ variable salary 
and bonus, calculated by reference to his average variable salary 
and bonus over the preceding three years. Jan Houwert’s new 
contract with Wegener, which came into effect on 8 May 2008, is for 
a fixed term expiring on 1 February 2011, subject to statutory 
termination rights. In the event that Wegener wishes to terminate 
Jan Houwert’s new contract (other than for gross misconduct) prior 
to 1 February 2011, application will be made to the courts in the 
Netherlands to determine the appropriate level of compensation.
The Executive Directors are subject to non-compete and non-
solicitation restrictive covenants which endure for six months after 
termination of employment, and to confidentiality undertakings of 
unlimited duration.
The contract of employment between the Company and David 
Montgomery came into effect on 15 March 2005, as did the contract 
of employment between the Company and Keith Allen. John 
Allwood’s contract of employment with the Company came into 
effect on 8 May 2007 when he joined the Company and was 
amended with effect from 27 February 2008 when he joined the

Policy on external appointments
Executive Directors may only hold external appointments with the 
prior agreement of the Nomination Committee.
David Montgomery is currently a non-executive director of Tournigan 
Energy Limited and Roto Smeets de Boer. He retains the earnings 
relating to his appointment in Tournigan Energy Limited but not in 
Roto Smeets de Boer. During 2008, David Montgomery’s earnings 
from external appointments were: £8,125 from Northern Ireland 
Energy Holdings Limited where he was a non-executive director up 
to 31 March 2008; CND7,500 from Tournigan Energy Limited; and 
€33,000 from Roto Smeets de Boer. Keith Allen held no external 
appointments. 
John Allwood is a member of the Council of the University of Exeter 
which is unremunerated. Jan Houwert is a non-executive director of 
Eden Design & Communication and of De Goudse NV, from which 
he received fees of €2,800 and €8,800 respectively for the period 
when he was an executive director of the Company. He also serves 
on the boards of a number of Dutch organisations promoting the 
arts, education and commerce. These posts are unremunerated, 
save for the College of Higher Education of Arnhem and Nijmegen, 
which paid Jan Houwert €1,800 for the period when he was an 
executive director of the Company. Jan Houwert retains his earnings 
from these external appointments. He is also an executive director 
of Van der Loeff Beheer B.V. an investment vehicle for the extended 
Houwert family.

We have audited the consolidated financial statements of Mecom 
Group plc for the year ended 31 December 2008 which comprise 
the consolidated income statement, the consolidated statement of 
recognised income and expense, the consolidated balance sheet, 
the consolidated cash flow statement and the related Notes 1 to 43. 
These consolidated financial statements have been prepared under 
the accounting policies set out therein.
We have reported separately on the parent company financial 
statements of Mecom Group plc for the year ended 31 December 
2008 and on the information in the Remuneration report that is 
described as having been audited. That report is modified by the 
inclusion of an emphasis of matter. 
This report is made solely to the Company’s members, as a body, 
in accordance with Section 235 of the Companies Act 1985. Our 
audit work has been undertaken so that we might state to the 
Company’s members those matters we are required to state to 
them in an auditors’ report and for no other purpose. To the fullest 
extent permitted by law, we do not accept or assume responsibility 
to anyone other than the Company and the Company’s members 
as a body, for our audit work, for this report, or for the opinions we 
have formed. 
Respective responsibilities of directors and auditors
The directors’ responsibilities for preparing the Annual report and 
accounts in accordance with applicable United Kingdom law and 
International Financial Reporting Standards (IFRSs) as adopted by 
the European Union are set out in the Statement of Directors’ 
Responsibilities.
Our responsibility is to audit the consolidated financial statements in 
accordance with relevant legal and regulatory requirements and 
International Standards on Auditing (UK and Ireland).
We report to you our opinion as to whether the consolidated financial 
statements give a true and fair view and whether the consolidated 
financial statements have been properly prepared in accordance 
with the Companies Act 1985 and Article 4 of the IAS Regulation. 
We also report to you whether in our opinion the information given 
in the Directors’ report is consistent with the financial statements. 
The information given in the Directors’ report includes that specific 
information presented in the Chairman’s statement, the Chief 
Executive’s review, the Market overview, the Divisional reviews, the 
Group Finance Director’s report, Principal risks and uncertainties 
and Corporate social responsibility that is cross referred from the 
Directors’ report.
In addition we report to you if, in our opinion, the Group has not kept 
proper accounting records, if we have not received all the information 
and explanations we require for our audit, or if information specified 
by law regarding director’s remuneration and other transactions is 
not disclosed.
We review whether the Corporate governance report reflects the 
Company’s compliance with the nine provisions of the 2006 
Combined Code specified for our review by the Listing Rules of the 
Financial Services Authority, and we report if it does not. We are not 
required to consider whether the Board’s statements on internal 
control cover all risks and controls, or form an opinion on the 
effectiveness of the Group’s corporate governance procedures or 
its risk and control procedures.
We read other information contained in the Annual report and 
accounts and consider whether it is consistent with the audited 
consolidated financial statements. The other information comprises 
only the following sections: Introduction, Transformation, New 
revenues, Titles, Our people, Our divisions, the Chairman’s 
statement, Group highlights, the Chief Executive’s review, Market 
overview, the Divisional reviews, the Group Finance Director’s 
report, Principal risks and uncertainties, Corporate social 
responsibility, The Board, the Directors’ report, Corporate 
governance, the unaudited part of the Remuneration report and 
Shareholder information. We consider the implications for our report 
if we become aware of any apparent misstatements or material 
inconsistencies with the consolidated financial statements. Our 
responsibilities do not extend to any other information.
Basis of audit opinion
We conducted our audit in accordance with International Standards 
on Auditing (UK and Ireland) issued by the Auditing Practices Board. 
An audit includes examination, on a test basis, of evidence relevant 
to the amounts and disclosures in the consolidated financial 
statements. It also includes an assessment of the significant 
estimates and judgments made by the directors in the preparation 
of the consolidated financial statements, and of whether the 
accounting policies are appropriate to the Group’s circumstances, 
consistently applied and adequately disclosed.
We planned and performed our audit so as to obtain all the 
information and explanations which we considered necessary in 
order to provide us with sufficient evidence to give reasonable 
assurance that the consolidated financial statements are free from 
material misstatement, whether caused by fraud or other irregularity 
or error. In forming our opinion we also evaluated the overall 
adequacy of the presentation of information in the consolidated 
financial statements.
Opinion
In our opinion:
the consolidated financial statements give a true and fair view, in •	
accordance with IFRSs as adopted by the European Union, of 
the state of the Group’s affairs as at 31 December 2008 and of 
its loss for the year then ended; 
the consolidated financial statements have been properly •	
prepared in accordance with the Companies Act 1985 and 
Article 4 of the IAS Regulation; and
the information given in the Directors’ report is consistent with •	
the consolidated financial statements.
Emphasis of matter – Going concern
In forming our opinion on the consolidated financial statements, 
which is not qualified, we have considered the adequacy of the 
disclosure made in Note 4 concerning the amendments to the 
existing bank facility agreement, the raising of additional equity and 
the repayment of the convertible loan notes. These conditions, 
along with the other matters explained in Note 4 to the consolidated 
financial statements, indicate the existence of material uncertainties 
which may cast significant doubt about the Group’s ability to 
continue as a going concern. The consolidated financial statements 
do not include the adjustments that would result if the Group was 
unable to continue as a going concern.

1. Corporate information
Mecom Group plc (the “Company”) is a public limited company 
incorporated and domiciled in England and Wales. The registered 
office of the Company is 70 Jermyn Street, London, SW1Y 6NY. Its 
ordinary shares are traded on the London Stock Exchange (LSE). 
The listing of the Company’s shares moved from the Alternative 
Investment Market (AIM) list to the main LSE list in April 2008. 
These consolidated financial statements for the year ended 31 
December 2008 were approved by the Board of Directors on 29 
April 2009. 
2. Definitions of terms
The Group uses the following terms, with the definition given, in 
these consolidated financial statements and in its internal monitoring 
of financial performance:
Adjusted EBITDA/Adjusted EBITDA margin
The Group monitors the performance of its segments on an earnings 
before interest, tax, depreciation and amortisation (“EBITDA”) basis. 
This measure includes any profit or loss from associates but 
excludes any exceptional items. Adjusted EBITDA margin (expressed 
as a percentage) is defined as adjusted EBITDA for a period divided 
by revenue for the same period.
Adjusted operating profit/Adjusted operating profit margin
Adjusted operating profit or loss is stated before exceptional items 
and amortisation of acquired intangibles. Adjusted operating profit 
margin (expressed as a percentage) is defined as adjusted operating 
profit for a period divided by revenue for the same period. 
Exceptional items
The Group presents as exceptional items on the face of the income 
statement those material items of income and expense which, 
because of their nature and/or expected infrequency of the events 
giving rise to them, merit separate presentation to allow shareholders 
to understand better the elements of financial performance in the 
period, so as to facilitate comparison with prior periods. 
Net debt
The Group presents as “net debt” the net of cash and cash 
equivalents, borrowings, obligations under finance leases and 
derivative financial instruments. The Group also includes in net debt 
any of the above items that have been classified as held for sale.

4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation)
Statement of compliance
The Group’s consolidated financial statements have been prepared 
in accordance with International Financial Reporting Standards 
(“IFRS”) as adopted by the European Union as they apply to the 
financial statements of the Group for the year ended 31 December 
2008. A summary of the Group’s significant accounting policies 
now follows. 
Basis of preparation: (i) Preparation of the consolidated 
financial statements on the going concern basis
The basis on which the consolidated financial statements have been 
prepared on the going concern basis, and the uncertainties related 
to the Group’s ability to continue in operational existence in the 
foreseeable future, are set out below.
The Group’s financial risk factors are set out in Note 27 to the 
consolidated financial statements.
Background to negotiations on revised bank agreement and 
proposals for an equity issue
The Group’s primary sources of funding are shareholders’ equity 
and bank borrowings. During the second half of 2008, a marked 
deterioration in advertising revenues affecting the Group’s 
profitability indicated that the Group’s leverage was too high for the 
current economic conditions.
In December 2008, the Group announced its intention to reduce 
borrowings and, at the same time, entered into an agreement with 
its lending banks to defer the testing of financial covenants in its 
bank facilities agreement from 31 December 2008 to 28 February 
2009 (which was subsequently deferred further to 31 March 2009, 
then further to 30 April 2009 and further to 31 May 2009, as 
explained below) and engaged in discussions to renegotiate the 
terms of its bank facilities. 
The Group announced the disposal of its German operations in 
January 2009 for consideration of €152.0m (£147.0m) and of its 
northwest Norwegian operations in February 2009 for NOK559.3m 
(£55.5m) as part of its strategy to reduce its borrowings. The cash 
proceeds from these disposals were received by the Group on 27 
March 2009 and 2 April 2009, respectively.
The Group announced on 23 March 2009 that it has been examining 
the merits of an equity fund-raising.
The Group announced on 1 April 2009 that it had also agreed with 
the holders of its convertible loan notes an extension to the maturity 
of these notes from 12 April to 12 May 2009, although it was agreed 
that this extension would accelerate to 30 April 2009 under certain 
conditions. 
On 29 April 2009, the Group entered into an agreement with its 
lending banks for a further deferral of the testing date of financial 
covenants until 31 May 2009 and the Group agreed a further 
extension of the maturity of the convertible loan notes to 12 July 
2009, although it was agreed that this extension would accelerate 
to 31 May 2009 under certain conditions. 
In principle agreement with lending banks on proposed  
revised bank facility agreement and with investors on  
proposed equity issue
On 29 April 2009, the Group:
reached ‘in principle’ agreement with its lending banks (subject •	
to the completion and signing of full documentation and subject 
to the completion of the proposed equity issue by no later than 
14 July 2009) on the terms of a proposed revised bank facility 
agreement. The agreement given by the banks on the key terms 
of the proposed revised facility agreement are not binding on 
the banks but each of the banks has received credit committee 
approval for the same and the Group believes that it is highly 
likely that full documentation will be signed in May 2009; and
received non-binding commitments from current and •	
prospective shareholders (which will be conditional upon, inter 
alia, the Company agreeing acceptable banking terms with its 
lenders, publishing a prospectus and obtaining shareholder 
approval) to subscribe to a proposed share issue of approximately 
£140m (before expenses). The Group intends repaying the 
convertible loan notes from these proceeds.
The Group expects to complete and to sign full banking 
documentation during May 2009, after which it expects that a 
prospectus for the issue of new shares will be issued with a view to 
receiving the proceeds of the equity issue during June 2009.
In the event that full banking documentation is not completed on the 
terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Group would continue discussion with its bank lenders 
with a view to agreeing alternative banking terms, but the directors 
cannot determine at this stage whether, or on what basis, alternative 
terms would be agreed.
In the event that full banking documentation is not completed on the 
terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Group would also expect to enter into discussions with 
the holders of the Group’s convertible loan notes to restructure the 
maturity of these notes, which would then be due currently and 
which the Group would be unable, in the absence of the agreement 
of the Group’s lending banks, to repay. The directors cannot 
determine at this stage what the outcome of these discussions 
would be.
In the event that the full banking documentation is not completed on 
the terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does 
not happen, the Group’s ability to continue operating as a going 
concern would be dependent, therefore, on the outcome of these 
discussions with its lending banks and with the holders of the 
convertible loan notes.
Key terms of the proposed revised bank facility agreement
The key terms of the revised bank deal (on the basis that share issue 
proceeds and after applying the proceeds of the share issue) will be 
as follows:
total facilities of circa €600m, including a term facility maturing •	
in October 2013 of €350.0m, a revolving credit facility of up to 
€200.0m maturing in October 2013 and an additional term loan 
facility of circa €50m;
the amount of the revolving credit facility will vary according to •	
the Group’s projected working capital requirements and to the 
amount of gross cash on the Group’s balance sheet; 72 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
margin on the term loan facility of 350 basis points over the relevant •	
inter-bank rate, with a 200 basis points additional non-cash margin 
on the additional term loan facility accruing from 1 January 2010 
and increasing by a further 200 basis points on 1 June 2010 and by 
a further 200 basis points on 1 January 2011;
margin on the revolving credit facility of 300 basis points; •	
cash margin under both the term and revolving credit facilities •	
are subject to downward adjustment in the event that the 
Group’s leverage falls below 3.0 times or 2.0 times, 
respectively;
leverage, interest cover and operating cash flow covenants •	
tested at 30 June 2010, 31 December 2010 and quarterly 
thereafter; 
June 2010 leverage covenant of 5.25 times, falling to 4.50 times •	
at 31 December 2010;
covenants on the total capital expenditure and exceptional items •	
of the Group, tested annually from 31 December 2009; and
warrants over the Company’s shares issued to the banks which •	
would represent 5% of the existing (pre-equity issue) share 
capital of the Company.
In assessing the Group’s ability to remain in compliance with the 
terms of the revised facility agreement in the foreseeable future, the 
directors have taken into account the fact that the leverage, interest 
cover and operating cash flow covenants would not be tested under 
the proposed revised facility agreement within twelve months of the 
date of these financial statements. 
The directors have also considered the Group’s financial projections 
for the twelve month period from these financial statements as they 
affect the proposed revised bank facility agreement in respect of 
conditions other than the leverage, interest cover and operating 
cash flow covenants. In making its financial projections for these 
purposes, the Group has taken into account that it currently 
generates around 50% of its revenue from advertising, the markets 
for which have tended in the past to reflect the general economic 
conditions of the countries in which the Group operates. The 
remainder of the Group’s revenue includes circulation revenue 
(around 35% of total revenue), which has more stable characteristics 
compared with advertising revenue and has not previously been 
affected by prevailing economic conditions to the extent that 
advertising revenue has been.
The Group’s advertising markets have experienced a considerable 
and systematic downturn in recent months and, although the 
experience of recent weeks’ trading suggests that some stabilisation 
at these lower levels has occurred, the advertising environment 
remains challenging and uncertain. 
In making assumptions of future advertising revenue for the 
purposes of assessing its ability to comply with the terms of the 
proposed revised facility agreement, the Group has used a 
combination of long-term trends, industry and third-party forecasts 
and internal estimates which reflect recent experience in each of our 
markets. If the actual outturn is adverse to these assumptions, the 
Group has identified a number of further mitigating actions that it 
could take to reduce costs or borrowings further.
Going concern basis in the financial statements
The directors believe that the combination of the circumstances 
described above, in particular (a) the uncertainty as to the completion 
of a revised facility agreement on the terms currently agreed (b) the 
uncertainty as to whether the non-binding commitments of investors 
to underwrite the issue of new share capital will result in new shares 
being issued, with the completion of the revised facility arrangements 
and the issue of equity being inter-conditional, and (c) the uncertainty, 
in the event that the revised facility agreement is not completed on 
terms currently agreed or that the new share capital is not issued, 
as to whether the Group could reach satisfactory agreement with 
the holders of its convertible loan notes as to an extension of the 
maturity of those notes, all of which three factors existing within a 
highly uncertain advertising environment, represent a material 
uncertainty that casts significant doubt on the Group’s and the 
Company’s ability to continue as a going concern. Nevertheless, 
after making enquiries, and considering the uncertainties described 
above, the directors have a reasonable expectation that the Group 
and the Company have adequate resources to continue in 
operational existence for the foreseeable future. For these reasons, 
they continue to adopt the going concern basis in preparing the 
Annual report and accounts.
Basis of preparation: (ii) Other
The consolidated financial statements have been prepared on a 
historical cost basis, except for available-for-sale financial assets, 
derivative financial instruments and share-based payments that 
have been measured at fair value.
These consolidated financial statements are presented in sterling 
and all values are shown in millions, rounded to the nearest one 
hundred thousand pounds, except when otherwise indicated. The 
significant exchange rates for the Group, applied during the current 
and prior periods, are as follows:

4. significant accounting policies (including basis of
