Basis of consolidation
The consolidated financial statements comprise the financial 
statements of the parent company (Mecom Group plc) and its 
subsidiary undertakings (the “Group”). Subsidiaries are fully 
consolidated from the date of acquisition, being the date on which 
the Group obtains control, and continue to be consolidated until the 
date such control ceases. All intra-group balances, transactions, 
income and expenses and profits and losses resulting from intra-
group transactions are eliminated in full.
Minority interest represents the portion of profit or loss and net 
assets not held by the Group and is presented within equity in the 
consolidated balance sheet, separately from parent shareholders’ 
equity. 
Business combinations 
The acquisition of subsidiaries is accounted for using the purchase 
method. The cost of the acquisition is measured at the aggregate of 
the fair values, at the date of exchange, of assets given, liabilities 
incurred or assumed, and equity instruments issued by the Group 
in exchange for control of the acquiree, plus any costs directly 
attributable to the business combination. The acquiree’s identifiable 
assets, liabilities and contingent liabilities that meet the conditions 
for recognition under IFRS 3 Business Combinations are recognised 
at their fair values at the acquisition date.
In certain circumstances, the initial accounting for a business 
combination is only determined on a provisional basis. The Group 
has up to 12 months from the date of an acquisition to complete its 
work on the fair values of assets and liabilities acquired and finalise 
the cost of the acquisition. Any adjustments the Group makes to the 
provisional values are recognised as if they had occurred at the date 
of the acquisition, causing certain comparative numbers in the 
financial statements to be restated. 
Goodwill arising on acquisition is recognised as an asset and initially 
measured at cost, being the excess of the cost of the business 
combination over the Group’s interest in the net fair value of the 
acquiree’s identifiable assets (including other intangible assets) and 
liabilities. Any negative goodwill is recognised immediately in the 
income statement. The interest of minority shareholders in the 
acquiree is initially measured at the minority’s proportion of the 
acquiree’s net fair value of the assets, liabilities and contingent 
liabilities.
Foreign currencies
Transactions in foreign currencies are translated at the average rate 
applicable during the financial year, unless by doing so a material 
difference arises versus using the spot rate. In this instance, spot 
rates are used. At each balance sheet date, items denominated in 
foreign currencies are retranslated at the rates prevailing on the 
balance sheet date. Exchange differences arising on settlement 
and on retranslation of foreign currency items are included in the 
income statement for the period.
Differences on the retranslation of the Group’s net investment in a 
foreign operation at the balance sheet date are recognised directly 
in equity. In the event of the disposal of the net investment, cumulative 
foreign currency differences recorded in equity related to that 
investment are recognised in the income statement as part of the 
gain or loss on disposal.
Revenue recognition
Revenue is recognised to the extent that it is probable that the 
economic benefits will flow to the Group and the revenue can be 
reliably measured. Revenue is measured at the fair value of the 
consideration receivable for the sale of goods and rendering of 
services, net of discounts, rebates and excluding other sales taxes 
or duty. The following criteria must also be met before revenue  
is recognised: 
(a) Sale of goods
Sale of goods consists of the sale of advertising, newspapers and 
other goods to newspaper and website customers. Revenue from 
the sale of goods is recognised at the time of delivery. Estimated 
returns on non-subscription sales are deducted from revenue.
(b) Rendering of services
Rendering of services consists primarily of the sale of printing and 
distribution services. This revenue is recognised as and when 
services are provided. 
(c) Revenue from barter transactions
Revenue includes amounts recognised from barter transactions. 
The majority of the Group’s barter transactions involve advertising 
services. The Group recognises revenue in relation to barter 
transactions involving advertising services only when the services 
exchanged are dissimilar in nature and when the fair value of the 
advertising services it provides in a barter transaction can be reliably 
measured by reference only to non-barter transactions that:
involve advertising similar to the advertising in the barter •	
transaction;
occur frequently; •	
represent a predominant number of transactions and amount •	
when compared to all transactions to provide advertising that is 
similar to the advertising in the barter transaction;
involve cash and/or another form of consideration that has a •	
reliably measurable fair value; and 
do not involve the same counterparty as in the barter transaction. •	
If the above criteria are met, the Group recognises revenue, with an 
equal and opposite cost recognised as a cost of sale, adjusted for 
any cash payments made from/to the Group. 
(d) Deferred revenue
The proportion of sales revenue relating to the future provision of 
services and goods is recorded as deferred revenue and recognised 
in the income statement as and when the services and goods  
are provided. 
(e) Finance income
Finance income primarily comprises bank interest receivable. This is 
recognised as interest accrues, using the effective interest method.
Tax
(a) Income tax
The tax expense/credit represents the sum of current income tax 
and deferred tax.
The current income tax amount is based on taxable profit for the 
period. Taxable profit differs from profit before tax as reported in the 
income statement because it excludes items of income or expense 
that are taxable or deductible in other years and it further excludes 
items that are not taxable or deductible. 74 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
(b) Deferred tax assets and liabilities
Deferred tax is the tax expected to be payable or recoverable on 
differences between the carrying amounts of assets and liabilities in 
the financial statements and the corresponding tax bases used in 
the computation of taxable profit, and is accounted for using the 
liability method. Deferred tax liabilities are generally recognised for 
all taxable temporary differences and deferred tax assets are 
recognised to the extent that it is probable that taxable profits will be 
available against which deductible temporary differences can be 
utilised.
Deferred tax liabilities are recognised for all taxable temporary 
differences, except where the deferred tax liability arises from the 
initial recognition of goodwill or of an asset or liability in a transaction 
that is not a business combination and, at the time of the transaction, 
affects neither the accounting profit nor taxable profit and loss.
Deferred tax liabilities are recognised for taxable temporary 
differences arising on investments in subsidiaries and associates, 
except where the Group is able to control the reversal of the 
temporary difference and it is probable that the temporary difference 
will not reverse in the foreseeable future.
The carrying amount of deferred tax assets is reviewed at each 
balance sheet date and reduced to the extent that it is no longer 
probable that sufficient taxable profits will be available to allow all or 
part of the asset to be recovered.
Deferred tax assets and liabilities are measured on an undiscounted 
basis at the tax rates that are expected to apply to the year when 
the asset is realised or the liability is settled, based on tax rates (and 
tax laws) that have been enacted or substantively enacted at the 
balance sheet date. Deferred tax is charged or credited in the 
income statement, except when it relates to items charged or 
credited directly to equity, in which case the deferred tax is also 
dealt with in equity.
Leases
Assets acquired under a lease that transfer substantially all of the 
risks and rewards of ownership to the Group are capitalised as 
either property, plant and equipment or software. Lease payments 
are apportioned between the finance charge and the reduction of 
the outstanding liability. The finance charge is allocated to each 
period during the lease term resulting in a constant periodic rate of 
interest on the remaining balance of the liability.
All other leases are classified as operating leases and rentals 
payable are charged in the income statement on a straight-line 
basis over the lease term.
Government grants
Government grants are recognised when it is reasonable to expect 
that the grants will be received and that all related conditions will be 
met, usually on submission of a valid claim for payment. 
Where a grant relates to the purchase of an asset – typically an item 
of property, plant and equipment – the grant is netted off against 
the cost of the asset, thereby reducing future depreciation 
charges. 
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008
Grants of a revenue nature are credited to income so as to match 
them with the expenditure to which they relate.
Where a grant is received in the form of a tax reduction, the grant is 
recognised as a reduction in the income tax charge for the period. 
Exceptional items
As explained above, the Group presents as exceptional items on 
the face of the income statement those material items of income 
and expense which, because of their nature and/or expected 
infrequency of the events giving rise to them, merit separate 
presentation to allow shareholders to understand better the 
elements of financial performance in the period, so as to facilitate 
comparison with prior periods. 
Continuing and discontinued operations
A discontinued operation is a component of the Group that has 
either been disposed of, or is classified as held-for-sale (see page 
76 for further details) and (i) represents a separate major line of 
business or geographical area or (ii) is part of a single co-ordinated 
plan to dispose of separate major lines of business or geographical 
areas of operations or (ii) was acquired exclusively with a view to 
resale. 
In the consolidated income statement of the reporting period,  
and of the comparable period of the previous year, income and 
expenses from discontinued operations are reported separately 
from continuing income and expenses, even when the Group retains 
a non-controlling interest in the subsidiary after the sale. The 
resulting profit or loss (after taxes) is reported separately in the 
income statement.
In certain Notes to these consolidated financial statements, the 
Group differentiates between items relating to the “continuing 
operations” and items relating to the “discontinued operations”. 
Goodwill
Goodwill acquired in a business combination is initially measured  
at cost, being the excess of the cost of the business combination 
over the Group’s interest in the net fair value of the identifiable 
assets, liabilities and contingent liabilities. Following initial 
recognition, goodwill is measured at cost less any accumulated 
impairment losses. 
As required by IFRS, goodwill is tested for impairment at least 
annually or at other times when circumstances indicate that the 
carrying value of goodwill may be impaired.
Where goodwill forms part of a cash-generating unit (or group of 
cash-generating units) and the cash-generating unit or an operation 
within that unit is disposed of, the goodwill associated with the 
cash-generating unit or operation disposed of is included in the 
carrying amount when determining the gain or loss on disposal.
Other intangible assets
An intangible asset acquired as part of a business combination  
is recognised outside goodwill if the asset is separable or arises 
from contractual or other legal rights and its fair value can be 
measured reliably. 75
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
The cost of intangible assets acquired in a business combination  
is the fair value as at date of acquisition. Following initial  
recognition, intangible assets are carried at cost less any 
accumulated amortisation and any accumulated impairment losses. 
Amortisation is calculated on a straight-line basis over the useful life 
of the assets.
Intangible assets acquired separately from a business are measured 
on initial recognition at cost. 
Internally developed IT infrastructure and software assets (for own 
use) are recognised on clearly defined projects when the recognition 
criteria of IAS 38 Intangible Assets, are met. Otherwise such 
expenditure is written off as incurred. 
Intangible assets with finite lives are amortised over their useful lives 
and assessed for impairment whenever there is an indication that 
the intangible asset may be impaired. The amortisation period and 
the amortisation method for an intangible asset with a finite useful 
life are reviewed at least at each financial year end. 
Intangible assets are amortised over the following periods:
Customer relationships    2–14 years
Brands    4–20 years
Purchased and developed software   2–7 years
No intangible assets are assessed as having indefinite lives.
Property, plant and equipment
Property, plant and equipment is stated at cost, less accumulated 
depreciation and accumulated impairment in value. Depreciation is 
calculated on a straight-line basis over the useful life of the assets. 
Costs associated with assets under construction are capitalised 
during the implementation period and are not depreciated. On 
completion of the project implementation the asset is transferred  
to another property, plant and equipment asset category  
as appropriate.
The carrying values of property, plant and equipment are reviewed 
for impairment when events or changes in circumstances indicate 
that the carrying value may not be recoverable.
The Group reviews residual values and useful lives on an annual 
basis and any adjustments are made prospectively. 
An item of property, plant and equipment is derecognised upon 
disposal or when no future economic benefits are expected to arise 
from the continued use of the asset. Any gain or loss arising on the 
derecognition of the asset is recorded in the income statement in 
the period of derecognition.
Property, plant and equipment is depreciated over the following 
periods:
Buildings 10–50 years
Leasehold improvements Shorter of 20 years  
 and term of lease
Machinery and equipment 6–20 years
Fixtures and fittings, motor vehicles, computers  
 and other operational assets    3–10 years
Interests in associates
The Group’s interests in its associates are accounted for using the 
equity method of accounting.
Under the equity method, the investment in the associate is carried 
in the balance sheet at cost plus post-acquisition changes in the 
Group’s share of net assets of the associate less distributions 
received and any impairment in value. Goodwill relating to an 
associate is included in the carrying amount of the investment and 
is not amortised. The income statement reflects the share of the 
results of operations of the associate after tax. Profits and losses 
resulting from the transactions between the Group and the associate 
are eliminated to the extent of the interest in the associate. The 
financial statements of the Group’s associates are prepared for the 
same reporting period as the Group. Where necessary, adjustments 
are made to bring the accounting policies in line with those of  
the Group.
Interests in joint ventures
The Group has interests in joint ventures which are jointly controlled 
entities. The Group recognises its interest in joint ventures using 
proportionate consolidation, under which the Group combines its 
share of each of the assets, liabilities, income and expenses of the 
joint venture with similar items, line-by-line, in its consolidated 
financial statements. The financial statements of the Group’s joint 
ventures are prepared for the same reporting period as the Group. 
Where necessary, adjustments are made to bring the accounting 
policies in line with those of the Group.
Impairment of non-financial assets 
The carrying amounts of the Group’s non-financial assets are  
tested annually for impairment (as required by IFRS in the case of 
goodwill) or when circumstances indicate that the carrying values 
may be impaired. 
If any such indication exists, or when annual impairment testing for 
an asset is required, the Group makes an estimate of the asset’s 
recoverable amount. The recoverable amount is the higher of an 
asset’s or cash-generating unit’s (“CGU”) fair value less costs to sell 
and its value-in-use and is determined for an individual asset, unless 
the asset does not generate cash inflows that are largely independent 
of those from other assets or groups of assets. Where the carrying 
amount of an asset or CGU exceeds its recoverable amount, the 
asset is considered to be impaired and is written down to its 
recoverable amount. In assessing value-in-use, the estimated future 
cash flows are discounted to their present value using a pre-tax 
discount rate that reflects current market assessments of the time 
value of money and the risks specific to the asset or CGU. In 
determining fair value less costs to sell, an appropriate valuation 
model is used. These calculations are corroborated by valuation 
multiples or other available fair value indicators.  76 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
Impairment losses on continuing and discontinued operations are 
recognised in the income statement as exceptional items. 
Inventories
Inventories are stated at the lower of cost, including the cost incurred 
in bringing each product to its present location and condition and 
net realisable value. The cost of inventories is measured on a first-in, 
first-out basis. 
Net realisable value is the estimated selling price in the ordinary 
course of business, less estimated costs of completion and the 
estimated costs necessary to make the sale.
Assets held for sale
Disposal groups are classified as held for sale if their carrying 
amount will be recovered through a sale transaction rather than 
through continuing use. This condition is regarded as met only 
when the sale is highly probable and the disposal group is available 
for immediate sale in its present condition. Management must be 
committed to the sale which should be expected to qualify for 
recognition as a completed sale within one year from the date  
of classification.
Property, plant and equipment and intangible assets once classified 
as held for sale are not depreciated/amortised.
Financial instruments
Financial assets and financial liabilities are recognised in the Group’s 
balance sheet when the Group becomes a party to the contractual 
provisions of the instrument.
(a) Financial assets
Financial assets are recognised when the Group becomes party to 
the contracts that give rise to them and are classified as:
financial assets at fair value through profit or loss; •	
held-to-maturity investments; •	
available-for-sale financial assets; •	
loans and receivables, or as •	
derivatives designated as hedging instruments in an effective •	
hedge, as appropriate. 
(i) Initial recognition
Financial assets are recognised initially at fair value plus, in the case 
of investments not at fair value through profit or loss, directly 
attributable transaction costs.
The Group determines the classification of its financial assets at 
initial recognition and, where allowed and appropriate, reassesses 
this designation at each balance sheet date. 
Purchases or sales of financial assets that require delivery of assets 
within a time frame established by regulation or convention in the 
marketplace (regular way purchases) are recognised on the trade 
date, i.e., the date that the Group commits to purchase or sell  
the asset.
The Group’s financial assets include cash and cash equivalents, 
trade and other receivables, loans and other receivables, quoted 
and unquoted investments and derivative financial instruments.
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008
(ii) Subsequent measurement
The subsequent measurement of financial assets depends on their 
classification as follows:
(iii) Financial assets at fair value through profit or loss 
Financial assets classified as held-for-trading and other assets 
designated as such on inception are included in this category. 
Financial assets are classified as held-for-trading if they are acquired 
for sale in the short term. Once a financial asset has been classified 
into this category, such classification cannot be revoked. 
The Group’s interest rate swaps fall within this category to the extent 
they are not designated as effective hedging instruments. Assets in 
this category are included within derivative financial instruments 
within non-current assets or current assets and are carried in the 
balance sheet at fair value with gains or losses recognised in the 
income statement. At 31 December 2008, the Group had no 
financial assets at fair value through profit or loss because all of its 
derivative financial instruments were designated as effective hedging 
instruments. At 31 December 2007, the Group balance sheet 
included £5.1m of financial assets at fair value through profit or loss 
(see Note 22).
(iv) Held-to-maturity investments
Non-derivative financial assets with fixed or determinable payments 
and fixed maturity are classified as held-to-maturity when the  
Group has the positive intention and ability to hold to maturity. At 
31 December 2008 and 2007, the Group had no held-to-maturity 
investments.
(v) Available-for-sale financial assets
Available-for-sale financial assets are those non-derivative financial 
assets that are either designated in this category or are not classified 
in any of the other categories. They are included in non-current 
assets unless the Group intends to dispose of the investment within 
12 months of the balance sheet date.
The Group’s quoted investments are classified as available-for-sale. 
After initial recognition, they are measured at fair value by reference 
to bid prices at the close of business on the balance sheet date. 
Unrealised gains or losses are recognised, net of related taxes, 
directly in equity via the revaluation reserve until the investment is 
derecognised or until the investment is determined to be impaired 
(see below) at which time the cumulative gain or loss previously 
reported in equity is included in the income statement.
The Group’s unquoted investments are also classified as available-
for-sale. They are carried at cost less impairment since reliable fair 
values are not available for the investments.
(vi) Loans and receivables
Loans and receivables are non-derivative financial assets with fixed 
or determinable payments that are not quoted in an active market, 
do not qualify as trading assets and have not been designated as 
either fair value through profit and loss or available-for-sale. 
They are included in current assets, except for those with maturities 
of more than 12 months after the balance sheet date which are 
classified as non-current assets. Accounts receivable and cash and 
cash equivalents are classified as loans and receivables in the 
balance sheet. 77
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
Such assets are carried at amortised cost using the effective interest 
method if the time value of money is significant. Gains and losses 
are recognised in the income statement when the loans and 
receivables are derecognised or impaired (see below), as well as 
through the amortisation process.
(vii) Derivatives designated as hedging instruments in an 
effective hedge
Refer to page 78 for the accounting policy on items within this 
classification. 
(viii) Impairment of financial assets
The Group assesses at each balance sheet date whether there is 
any objective evidence that a financial asset or a group of financial 
assets is impaired. A financial asset or a group of financial assets  
is deemed to be impaired if, and only if, there is objective evidence 
of impairment as a result of one or more events that has occurred 
after the initial recognition of the asset (an incurred “loss event”)  
and that loss event has an impact on the estimated future cash 
flows of the financial asset or the group of financial assets that can 
be reliably estimated. 
In the case of equity securities classified as available-for-sale, a 
significant or prolonged decline in the fair value of the security below 
its cost is considered as an indicator that the securities are 
permanently impaired. If any such evidence exists for available- 
for-sale financial assets, the cumulative loss – measured as the 
difference between the acquisition cost and the current fair value, 
less any permanent impairment loss on that financial asset previously 
recognised in profit or loss – is removed from equity and recognised 
in the income statement. Impairment losses recognised in the 
income statement on equity instruments are not reversed through 
the income statement – increases in the fair value after impairment 
are recognised directly in equity. 
When securities classified as available-for-sale are sold or 
permanently impaired, the accumulated fair value adjustments 
recognised in equity are recycled through the income statement.
In relation to trade receivables, a provision for impairment is made 
when there is objective evidence (such as the probability of 
insolvency or significant financed difficulties of the debtor) that the 
Group will not be able to collect all of the amounts due under the 
original terms of the invoice. The carrying amount of the receivable 
is reduced through use of an allowance account. Impaired trade 
receivables are derecognised when they are assessed as 
irrecoverable.
(ix) Derecognition of financial assets
A financial asset is derecognised when the contract that gives rise 
to it is settled, sold, cancelled or expires.
(b) Cash and cash equivalents
Cash and cash equivalents in the balance sheet comprise cash at 
bank and in-hand and short-term deposits with an original maturity 
of three months or less. For the purpose of the consolidated cash 
flow statement, cash and cash equivalents consist of cash and cash 
equivalents as defined above, net of outstanding bank overdrafts.
(c) Trade receivables
Trade receivables are stated at their nominal value as reduced by 
appropriate allowances for estimated irrecoverable amounts. A 
provision is made and charged to the income statement where 
there is objective evidence that the Group will not be able to collect 
all amounts due according to the original terms.
(d) Financial liabilities
Financial liabilities and equity instruments are classified  
according to the substance of the contractual arrangements  
entered into. The Group’s financial liabilities include borrowings, 
trade and other payables, compound instruments and derivative 
financial instruments. 
(i) Initial recognition
Financial liabilities are classified as:
loans and borrowings; •	
derivatives designated as hedging instruments in an effective •	
hedge, as appropriate; or as
financial liabilities at fair value through profit or loss, as •	
appropriate.
The Group determines the classification of its financial liabilities at 
initial recognition. Financial liabilities are recognised initially at fair 
value and in the case of loans and borrowings, directly attributable 
transaction costs.
(ii) Subsequent measurement
The measurement of financial liabilities depends on their classification 
as follows:
(iii) Loans and borrowings
After initial recognition, interest bearing loans and borrowings are 
subsequently measured at amortised cost using the effective 
interest rate method.
(iv) Derivatives designated as hedging instruments in an 
effective hedge
Refer to page 78 for the accounting policy on items within this 
classification. 
(v) Financial liabilities at fair value through profit or loss
Financial liabilities at fair value through profit or loss includes financial 
liabilities held for trading and financial liabilities designated upon 
initial recognition as at fair value through profit or loss.
Financial liabilities are classified as held-for-trading if they are 
acquired for the purpose of selling in the near term. This category 
includes derivative financial instruments entered into by the Group 
that do not meet the hedge accounting criteria as defined by IAS 39 
Financial Instruments: Recognition and Measurement. 
Gains or losses on liabilities held for trading are recognised in the 
income statement.
At 31 December 2008 and 2007, the Group has not designated any 
financial liabilities as at fair value through profit or loss. 78 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
Gains and losses are recognised in the income statement when the 
liabilities are derecognised as well as through the amortisation 
process. Gains and losses on the repurchase, settlement or 
otherwise cancellation of borrowings are recognised in finance 
income and finance expense, respectively.
(e) Trade payables
Trade payables are stated at their nominal value.
 
(f) Compound instruments
The component parts of compound instruments issued by the 
Group are classified separately as financial liabilities and equity in 
accordance with the substance of the contractual arrangement. At 
the date of issue, in the case of a convertible bond that will either be 
repaid or converted into ordinary shares of the Company, the 
instrument is split for accounting purposes between the liability 
element and the equity component, representing the fair value of 
the embedded option to convert the liability into equity. The fair 
value of the liability component is estimated using the prevailing 
market interest rate for a similar non-convertible instrument. This 
amount is recorded as a liability on an amortised cost basis using 
the effective interest method until extinguished upon conversion or 
at the instrument’s maturity date. 
The unwinding of the discount in respect of the amount recognised 
as a liability on issue is recognised within finance expense in the 
income statement. 
 
(g) Derivative financial instruments
The Group uses derivative financial instruments, such as interest 
rate swaps, to hedge its risks associated with interest rate 
fluctuations. Such derivative financial instruments are initially 
recognised at fair value on the date on which a derivative contract is 
entered into and are subsequently remeasured at fair value. 
Derivatives are carried as assets when the fair value is positive and 
as liabilities when the fair value is negative. 
Derivative instruments are classified as current or non-current or 
separated into a current and non-current portion based on an 
assessment of the facts and circumstances (i.e., the underlying 
contracted cash flows).
The Group has a policy not to undertake any speculative activity in 
financial instruments.
The fair value of interest rate swaps is determined by reference to 
market values for similar instruments.
(i) Hedge accounting
For those derivatives designated as hedges and for which hedge 
accounting is desired, the hedging relationship is formally designated 
and documented at its inception. This documentation identifies the 
risk management objective and strategy for undertaking the hedge, 
the hedging instrument, the hedged item or transaction, the nature 
of the risk being hedged and how effectiveness will be measured 
throughout its duration. Such hedges are expected at inception to 
be highly effective in offsetting changes in fair value or cash flows 
and are assessed on an ongoing basis to determine that they 
actually have been highly effective throughout the reporting period 
for which they were designated.
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008
For the purpose of hedge accounting, the Group classifies its 
hedges as either:
cash flow hedges •	 when hedging exposure to variability in cash 
flows that is either attributable to a particular risk associated 
with a recognised asset or liability or a highly probable forecast 
transaction; or
hedges of a •	 net investment in a foreign operation.
Any gains or losses arising from changes in fair value of derivatives 
that do not qualify for hedge accounting are taken directly to the 
income statement (see above). 
The treatment of gains and losses arising from revaluing derivatives 
designated as hedging instruments depends on the nature of the 
hedging relationship, as follows:
(ii) Cash flow hedges
The Group applies cash flow hedge accounting when it hedges 
exposure to variability in cash flows associated with a recognised 
asset or liability or a highly probable forecast transaction and where 
the hedge is expected to be highly effective.
The effective portion of the gain or loss on the hedging instrument 
is recognised directly in equity, while any ineffective portion is 
recognised immediately in the income statement (see above).
Amounts taken to equity are transferred to the income statement 
when the hedged transaction affects the income statement. Where 
the hedged item is the cost of a non-financial asset or non-financial 
liability, the amounts previously taken to equity are transferred to the 
initial carrying amount of the non-financial asset or liability.
If a forecast transaction is no longer expected to occur, amounts 
previously recognised in equity are transferred to the income 
statement. If the hedging instrument expires or is sold, terminated 
or exercised without replacement or rollover, or if its designation as 
a hedge is revoked, amounts previously recognised in equity remain 
in equity until the forecast transaction occurs and are transferred to 
the income statement or to the initial carrying amount of a non-
financial asset or liability, as above. 
(iii) Hedges of a net investment in a foreign operation
Hedges of a net investment in a foreign operation, including a hedge 
of a monetary item that is accounted for as part of the net investment, 
are accounted for in a way similar to cash flow hedges. Gains or 
losses relating to the effective portion are recognised directly  
in equity while any gains or losses relating to the ineffective portion 
are recognised in the income statement. On disposal of the  
foreign operation, the cumulative value of any such gains or  
losses recognised directly in equity is transferred to the  
income statement.
(h) Derecognition of financial liabilities
A financial liability is generally derecognised when the contract that 
gives rise to it is settled, sold, cancelled or expires. Where an 
existing financial liability is replaced by another from the same lender 
on substantially different terms, or the terms of an existing liability 
are substantially modified, such an exchange or modification is 
treated as a derecognition of the original liability and the recognition 
of a new liability, such that the difference in the respective carrying 
amounts together with any costs or fees incurred are recognised in 
the income statement. 79
Financials
4. significant accounting policies (including basis of 
preparation) continued
Provisions
Provisions are recognised when the Group has a present obligation 
as a result of a past event, where the obligation can be estimated 
reliably, and where it is probable that an outflow of economic 
benefits will be required to settle that obligation. Provisions are 
measured at the directors’ best estimate of the expenditure required 
to settle the obligation at the balance sheet date, and are discounted 
to present value where the effect is material. Where discounting is 
used, the increase in the provision due to unwinding the discount is 
recognised as a finance expense.
Employee benefits
For defined contribution pension plans, the contribution to employees’ 
pension savings is expensed over the period to which it relates. 
For defined benefit pension plans and other defined benefit 
arrangements, pension expenses and pension liabilities are 
calculated based on the projected unit credit method, which 
attributes entitlement to benefits to the current period and to prior 
periods, using assumptions for various factors including discount 
rates, future salary adjustments, pensions, future return on pension 
plan assets, mortality rates and transfers out of the plan. Pension 
plan assets are valued at fair value and deducted from net pension 
liabilities in the balance sheet. Any surplus is recognised to the 
extent that it is likely that the surplus may be utilised or repaid. 
 
The interest element of the defined benefit cost represents the 
change in present value of scheme obligations resulting from the 
passage of time, and is determined by applying the discount rate to 
the opening present value of the benefit obligation, taking into 
account material changes in the obligation during the period.
The expected return on plan assets is based on the long-term 
market return on scheme assets adjusted for the effect on the fair 
value of plan assets of contributions received and benefits paid 
during the period. The difference between the expected return on 
plan assets and the interest cost is recognised in the income 
statement as part of operating expenses.
Past service costs are recognised in the income statement on a 
straight-line basis over the vesting period or immediately if the 
benefits have vested. Changes in the pension liability due to changes 
in pension plans are expensed immediately if vested. Changes in 
liabilities and pension plan assets due to actuarial gains or losses 
from the estimated assumptions are recognised immediately in the 
statement of recognised income and expense.
Equity instruments 
An equity instrument is any contract that evidences a residual 
interest in the assets of the Group after deducting all of its liabilities. 
Equity instruments issued by the Company are recorded at the 
proceeds received, net of direct issue costs.
Share-based payments 
Equity-settled share-based payments are measured at fair value 
(excluding the effect of non-market-based vesting conditions) at the 
date of grant. The fair value is calculated using either a Monte Carlo 
simulation model or a binomial model depending on the 
appropriateness of the model to the grant in question and is 
expensed on a straight-line basis over the vesting period. There is a 
corresponding amount recognised in reserves, equivalent to the 
expense recorded in the period.
At each balance sheet date before vesting, the cumulative expense 
is calculated, representing the extent to which the vesting period 
has expired and management’s best estimate of the achievement 
or otherwise of non-market performance conditions, and hence the 
number of equity instruments that will ultimately vest. The movement 
in cumulative expense since the previous balance sheet date is 
recognised in the income statement, with a corresponding entry in 
equity.
The dilutive effect of outstanding options is reflected as additional 
share dilution in the computation of earnings per share (see  
Note 14).
5.  significant accounting judgements and key 
sources of estimation uncertainty 
In the application of the Group’s accounting policies, which are 
described in Note 4 above, the directors are required to make 
judgements, estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts 
reported for assets and liabilities as at the balance sheet date and 
the amounts reported for revenues and expenses during the year. 
However, the nature of estimation means that actual outcomes 
could differ from those estimates.
The estimates and underlying assumptions are reviewed on an 
ongoing basis. Revisions to accounting estimates are recognised in 
the period in which the estimate is revised if the revision affects that 
period only, or in the period of the revision and future periods if the 
revision affects both current and future periods. 
Critical judgements in applying the Group’s accounting 
policies
In the process of applying the Group’s accounting policies, the 
directors have made the following judgements, apart from those 
involving estimations, which have the most significant effect on the 
amounts recognised in the financial statements:
(a) Taxation 
The Company and its subsidiaries are subject to routine tax audits 
and also a process whereby tax computations are discussed  
and agreed with the appropriate authorities. Whilst the ultimate 
outcome of such tax audits and discussions cannot be  
determined with certainty, management estimates the level of 
provisions required for both current and deferred tax on the basis  
of professional advice and the nature of current discussions with the 
tax authority concerned. 
(b) Recoverability of deferred tax assets
Deferred tax assets are recognised for all unused tax losses to the 
extent that it is probable that a taxable profit or loss will be utilised. 
Significant management judgement is required to determine the 
amount of deferred tax assets that can be recognised, based upon 
the likely timing and level of future taxable profits. Details of deferred 
tax balances are contained in Note 28.
Estimates and assumptions
The key assumptions concerning the future and other key sources 
of estimation uncertainty at the balance sheet date, that have a 
significant risk of causing a material adjustment to the carrying 
amounts of assets and liabilities within the next financial year are 
discussed below. 80 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
6. segment information
The Group’s primary reporting format is determined to be geographical segments as the Group’s risks and rates of return are affected 
predominantly by the territories in which each of the businesses operates. The Group does not report a secondary segment format as the 
Group considers it has only one business segment, being the operation of newspaper publishing, content and consumer businesses  
in Europe.
The geographical segments are based on the location of the Group’s assets. Sales to external customers disclosed in the geographical 
segments are based on the geographical location of its customers. The segment “Norway” incorporates certain operations in Sweden and 
the segment Poland incorporates certain operations in Ukraine. 
The segment “Central and other” from the start of 2008 comprises only the Group’s head-office activities whereas for the year ended 31 
December 2007 it also included the Group’s Direct Marketing activities, which were disposed of during 2008 (see Note 39 for further 
details). Segment result is shown both before and after exceptional items and amortisation of acquired intangibles. There are no significant 
inter-segment revenues. Finance income and finance expense, gains or losses on disposal of subsidiaries and investments and income tax 
expense/credit are treated as unallocated. 
Segment assets comprise all classes of assets except for cash and cash equivalents, derivative financial instruments, current tax assets 
and deferred tax assets which are treated as unallocated. Segment liabilities comprise all classes of liabilities except borrowings, derivative 
financial instruments, current tax liabilities and deferred tax liabilities which are treated as unallocated. Capital expenditure excludes any 
items purchased via a business combination and for the purposes of this note includes both property, plant and equipment additions and 
software additions. Acquired non-current assets comprise goodwill, other intangible assets and property, plant and equipment purchased 
during the year as part of a business combination. The following tables present the revenue, result and asset and liability information 
regarding the Group’s geographical segments.

5.  significant accounting judgements and key 
sources of estimation uncertainty continued
(a) Impairment of goodwill and acquired intangibles
The Group determines whether goodwill is impaired at least on an 
annual basis. This requires an estimation of the value-in-use of the 
cash-generating units to which the goodwill is allocated. Estimating 
a value-in-use amount requires the directors to make an estimate of 
the expected future cash flows from the cash-generating unit and 
also to choose a suitable discount rate in order to calculate the 
present value of those cash flows. Details of goodwill are contained 
in Note 15. 
As part of the Group’s goodwill impairment review, the Group’s 
acquired intangibles (comprising customer relationships and 
brands) are also assessed for impairment at least annually, using 
the same approach as described in the above paragraph. When a 
CGU’s goodwill is fully impaired, any remaining excess of book 
value over recoverable amount in firstly written-off against the 
CGU’s acquired intangibles. Details of the impairment of acquired 
intangibles are contained in Note 16.
(b) Valuation of acquired intangibles 
The acquisition of subsidiaries is accounted for using the purchase 
method and the purchase consideration is allocated over the net fair 
value of identifiable assets, liabilities and contingent liabilities 
acquired with any excess consideration representing goodwill. In 
determining the fair value of assets, liabilities and contingent liabilities 
acquired, the directors may make significant estimates and 
assumptions, including those with respect to cash flows and 
unprovided liabilities and commitments.
(c) Useful lives of acquired intangibles
On acquisition of subsidiaries the Group will consider the useful 
lives of any intangible assets acquired. The length of useful lives of 
customer relationships is assessed based on the average lives  
of historic customer relationships for all main titles. The length of 
useful lives of brands is assessed based on the directors’ view  
of the market and on the length of the time that the main titles have 
been established.
The amortisation period and the amortisation method for an 
intangible asset with a finite useful life are reviewed at least at each 
financial year end. Details of asset lives are contained in Note 4.
(d) Provisions 
The amounts provided for restructuring and redundancy provisions 
and other provisions are based on the directors’ best estimates of 
costs likely to be incurred to the extent that they are recognisable 
under relevant reporting standards. To the extent that events or 
costs differ in future, the carrying value of provisions may change. 
Details of provisions are contained in Note 30.
(e) Employee benefit obligations
The cost of defined benefit pension plans and other retirement 
benefits is determined using actuarial valuations. The actuarial 
valuation involves making assumptions about discount rates, 
expected rates of return on assets, future salary increases, mortality 
rates and future pension increases. Due to the long-term nature of 
these plans, such estimates are subject to significant uncertainty. 
Details of employee benefit obligations are contained in Note 31.

10. Exceptional items and amortisation of acquired intangibles 
The Group presents as exceptional items separately on the face of the income statement those material items of income and expense 
which, because of their nature and/or the infrequency of the events giving rise to them, merit separate presentation to allow shareholders 
to understand better the elements of financial performance in the period, so as to facilitate comparison with prior periods. The Group also 
separates the amortisation of acquired intangibles on the face of the income statement since, whilst accounting standards require the 
recognition of this amortisation as an expense, it is not an underlying operating expense of the Group’s businesses.

Denmark of £10.0m. Title restructuring costs relate primarily to the change of format of titles in the Netherlands from broadsheet to tabloid. 
Site and other restructuring costs include charges related to the reorganisation and refurbishment of the Copenhagen offices and costs 
associated with the moving of the listing of the Company’s shares from AIM to the main list of the LSE. 86 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008

10. Exceptional items and amortisation of acquired intangibles continued
Impairment charges of £861.3m resulted from the Group’s assessment of the recoverable amount of non-current assets and reflect  
the effect that the current economic climate has had on the value of the Group’s assets. Further details are given in Notes 15, 16, 17,  
18 and 20. 
The mark-to-market losses on interest rate swaps arose on swaps associated with the Group’s previous borrowing facility. These swaps 
were not designated as hedges for accounting purposes and therefore movements in the fair value of the swaps (which were non-cash) 
were recognised in the income statement. These swaps were cancelled and new swaps, which are designated as cashflow hedges of the 
Group’s variable rate borrowings, were entered into in March 2008.
The Group paid a fee to its lending banks of £2.3m and incurred additional related costs of £1.0m on agreeing a deferral of the December 
2008 covenant tests under the Group’s bank borrowings. Of the total amendment fee on renegotiation of borrowings of £3.3m, £2.9m 
relates to continuing operations. 
The Group has recorded exceptional finance costs of £1.2m related to the unwinding of discount on exceptional restructuring provisions.
In addition to the exceptional items noted above, an exceptional tax credit of £7.8m was recorded in 2008. £15.4m of this is due to deferred 
tax credits arising on the amortisation of the Group acquired intangibles. Further credits of £10.4m and £2.2m arose as a consequence of 
impairing Denmark’s and Poland’s acquired intangibles by £41.7m and £11.6m, respectively (see Note 16). A charge of £32.4m arose on the 
write-down of the Group’s Denmark tax assets after it was determined that these were not recoverable. The remaining balance of £12.2m 
relates to exceptional tax credits recorded on exceptional operating and finance items.
Discontinued operations
Staff redundancy costs relate to the discontinued operation’s cost reduction programmes through the reduction of full-time equivalent 
employee numbers. As described in more detail in Note 13, the impairment charge in respect of goodwill results from the write-down of the 
assets of the Group’s Germany operations to the net proceeds of the disposal which completed in March 2009. The finance exceptional 
costs relate to market-to-market losses on interest rate swaps (£0.2m), a share of the amendment fee on renegotiation of borrowings 
(£0.4m) and unwinding of discounts on exceptional provisions (£0.3m). 
In addition to the exceptional items noted above, an exceptional tax charge of £2.9m was recorded in 2008. A charge of £5.4m arose on 
the write-down of Germany’s deferred tax assets after it was determined that these were not recoverable. This was offset by £1.9m due to 
deferred tax credits arising on the amortisation of Germany’s acquired intangibles. £0.6m relates to an exceptional tax credit arising from 
the reversal of an exceptional tax provision made in 2007.

13. Discontinued operations and assets held for sale
Year ended 31 December 2008
On 12 January 2009, the Group entered into a sale agreement to dispose of all of its German operations. On a cash- and debt-free basis, 
the purchase price agreed with the purchaser, M. DuMont Schauberg Expedition der Kölnischen Zeitung GmbH & Co KG, was €152.0m, 
or £147.0m at the closing 2008 exchange rate. The disposal is part of the Group’s strategy to strengthen its balance sheet and to ensure 
the remaining Group is in a stronger position to operate successfully in the current market conditions. To this end, the proceeds from this 
disposal were used to reduce the Group’s borrowings. At 31 December 2008 negotiations for the sale were at an advanced stage and the 
disposal completed on March 27 2009. 
This operation was accounted for as a subsidiary in 2008 before being classified as a discontinued operation and a disposal group held for 
sale. This operation, which represents a major component of the Group, is a separate reportable geographical segment in both 2008 and 
2007 (see Note 6).

13. Discontinued operations and assets held for sale continued
As noted above, the purchase price on a cash- and debt-free basis was £147.0m. The terms of the sale and purchase agreement allowed 
for certain adjustments to be made to this amount in order to arrive at the actual gross proceeds that flowed into the Group on completion 
of the disposal. After deducting £4.5m for debt assumed and £3.9m for estimated selling costs and adding £0.1m for certain working capital 
adjustments, the net proceeds were £138.7m. It should be noted that the amount of £138.7m is net of £5.5m of cash sold with the business 
on a euro-for-euro basis.
On completion of the disposal, the Group was contractually obliged to immediately repay £99.8m (€103.3m) of the net proceeds to the 
lending banks, this being a condition of the 22 December renegotiation (see Note 26 for further details).
As a consequence of the net disposal proceeds being lower than the disposal group’s book value, an impairment charge has been 
recognised in 2008 of £149.3m in order to write the disposal group’s net assets down to their fair value less costs to sell. This amount is 
included within the disposal group’s exceptional operating costs of £159.2m, as set out above. 
Year ended 31 December 2007
During 2007, the Board resolved to dispose of the Group’s De Trompetter operations in the Netherlands and its Direct Marketing operations 
in Norway and Sweden. The disposal of De Trompetter arose because of a condition imposed by the competition authorities in the 
Netherlands related to the Group’s acquisition of Wegener in October 2007. The Group decided to dispose of its Direct Marketing operations 
because management consider it to be a non-core activity. Both of these operations were accounted for as subsidiaries before being 
classified as held for sale.
These operations were classified as disposal groups held for sale and presented separately in the balance sheet at 31 December 2007. The 
De Trompetter and Direct Marketing operations are included in “The Netherlands” and “Central and other” segments, respectively, in the 
segmental analysis in Note 6. 
At 31 December 2007, the disposal proceeds for each of these operations were expected to exceed the book values of the respective 
related net assets. Accordingly no impairment losses were recognised in 2007 on the classification of these operations as held for sale.

14. Earnings per share
Basic earnings per share is calculated by dividing net profit/(loss) for the period attributable to ordinary equity holders of the parent by the 
weighted average number of ordinary shares outstanding during the period.
Basic adjusted earnings per share is calculated by dividing adjusted earnings for the period attributable to ordinary equity holders of the 
parent by the weighted average number of ordinary shares outstanding during the period. Adjusted earnings are the profit/(loss) for the 
period attributed to ordinary equity holders of the parent adjusted to exclude exceptional items and amortisation of acquired intangibles (net 
of related tax and minority interests).
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008 91

issued under convertible loan notes (see Note 26) and the Group’s share-based payment awards (see Note 35). The potential shares did 
not give rise to a decrease in profit per share or an increase in loss per share. As such, potential shares were considered anti-dilutive and 
did not lead to adjustments in diluted earnings per share or diluted adjusted earnings per share.
There have been no other transactions involving ordinary shares or potential ordinary shares between the reporting date and the date of

The CGUs given above to which goodwill arising from business combinations has been allocated are also the reportable segments of the 
Group, since the management of the Group’s operations and the derivation of its cash flows are done at the country level.
Annual impairment test
The Group tests goodwill annually for impairment, or more frequently if there are indications that goodwill might be impaired. The recoverable 
amount of each CGU is determined either from (a) “value-in-use” calculations, using cash flow projections based on the most recent 
financial budgets approved by the Board and management forecasts beyond the period of these budgets or, if higher, (b) current valuations 
of disposal proceeds less costs to sell, based on prospective transactions involving the specific Group assets involved in disposals 
transactions, recent comparable transactions or valuations of publicly traded companies.
The key assumptions to which the value-in-use calculations are most sensitive are:
revenue growth rates (for periods within the cash flow projections and in perpetuity for the calculation of the terminal value); •	
EBITDA margins (as a driver for the cash generation of segments before working capital requirements); •	
future levels of maintenance capital expenditure; and •	
discount rates. •	
Revenue growth rates, EBITDA margins and future levels of capital expenditure are based on past experience and expected future 
developments in the Group’s CGUs. Cash flows for periods beyond the Group’s own budgets and forecasts are projected at rates that take 
into consideration forecast GDP growth rates for each country. Longer-term and perpetuity growth rates do not exceed the average long-
term growth rates for each country of the Group’s operations.
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008 93
Financials

The discount rate applied to each CGU is a pre-tax rate that reflects current market assessments of the time value of money and the risks 
specific to each CGU’s cash flow projections, based on the Group’s weighted average cost of capital.

On 22 December 2008, the Group announced that the 31 December 2008 covenant test date under its banking facilities had been deferred 
to 28 February 2009, by agreement with its lending banks. As part of this agreement, the Group paid its lending banks a covenant 
amendment fee of £2.3m, and also incurred related professional fees of £1.0m. The total charge of £3.3m has been treated as an exceptional 
finance charge for the year ended 31 December 2008 (see Notes 10 and 11). In addition to paying a fee, the Group’s interest rate margin 
increased to 3.5% with immediate effect (see below) and the Group’s RCF was capped at €195.0m. 
In 2008 (up to the 22 December covenant test date extension) and 2007, the interest rates of the facilities were charged by reference to a 
specified margin over the relevant LIBOR or EURIBOR rate. The initial margin was 1.75% per annum for the first six months following the first 
utilisation date in 2007. After this period, the interest rate margin was dependent on the Group’s ratio of net debt to EBITDA (the leverage 
ratio). Below is a summary of how the interest margin would have varied depending on the Group’s leverage up to 22 December covenant 
test date extension.
 
 Interest rate margin per annum up to 22 December 2008 
Leverage ratio covenant test date extension and 2007
Greater than 3.0 times        1.75%
Equal to or less than 3.0 times but greater than 2.5 times       1.50%
Equal to or less than 2.5 times but greater than 2.0 times       1.25%
Equal to or less than 2.0 times but greater than 1.5 times       1.00%
Equal to or less than 1.5 times        0.75%
As noted above, from 22 December to 31 December 2008, the Group’s interest rate margin increased to 3.5%, irrespective of the Group’s

27. Financial risk management
Overview
The Board has overall responsibility for the establishment and oversight of the Group’s risk management, including financial risks. The 
Group has established an Audit Committee with delegated responsibility for developing and monitoring the Group’s risk management 
policies.
The Group’s principal financial instruments comprise bank borrowings, convertible loan notes and cash and cash equivalents, the main 
purpose of which is to provide finance for the Group’s operations. The Group has various other financial assets and liabilities such as trade 
receivables and trade payables, which arise directly from its operating activities.
The Group also enters into derivative transactions, principally interest rate swaps. The purpose is to manage the interest rate risks arising 
from the Group’s operations and its sources of finance. The Group does not trade in derivatives.
The Group’s key financial risks arising from its operating activities and its financial instruments are:
market risk (including interest rate risk, foreign exchange risk and funding risk); •	
liquidity risk; and •	
credit risk. •	
The Group uses derivatives and other financial instruments to reduce these risks in accordance with the Group’s financial policy as set out 
below. 
Interest rate risk
Interest rate risk arises primarily from the Group’s long-term borrowings, being the risk that a movement in interest rates will affect the 
Group’s obligations, cash flows and income.
The Group’s policy is to keep between 40% and 80% of its borrowings at fixed interest rates. This is achieved primarily by entering into 
interest rate swaps which are designated as hedges to the underlying floating rate bank borrowings. The Group classifies such interest rate 
swaps as cash flow hedges and states them at fair value.  102 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials

Interest charges on financial instruments classified as floating rate are repriced at intervals of less than one year. Interest on financial 
instruments classified as fixed rate is fixed until the maturity of the instrument. The other financial instruments of the Group not included in 
the above table are non-interest bearing and therefore not subject to interest rate risk.
Floating rate financial assets comprise cash and deposits on money market deposits at call, seven day and monthly rates. The Group’s 
other financial assets do not accrue interest and have no fixed maturity date.
Interest rate swap contracts
With interest rate swap contracts, the Group enters into an agreement to exchange the difference between floating and fixed rate interest 
amounts calculated on agreed notional principal amounts. Such contracts enable the Group to manage the risk of a change in underlying 
interest rates on the Group’s cash flows. The fair value of the interest rate swaps at the reporting date is determined by discounting the future 
cash flows using yield curves at the reporting date. In 2008 interest rate swaps were entered into fixing the interest rate on €225.0m and 
NOK810.0m of floating rate debt (2007: €60.0m)
On 31 October 2007, the Group’s long-term borrowings were refinanced. On refinancing, the majority of the interest rate swaps that had 
been in place to hedge the previous borrowings ceased to be classified as cash flow hedges. The cumulative amount recorded in equity of 
£6.2m was recognised immediately in the income statement as exceptional finance income, as shown in Note 10. These interest rate swaps 
were closed out in March 2008. Between 31 October and March 2008, changes in fair value of these interest rate swaps were recorded 
directly in the income statement. 
Information related to the Group’s interest rate swaps is shown below. At 31 December 2007, the majority of the Group’s interest rate swaps 
were not accounted for as hedges, as explained above. The information in the table below relates only to interest rate swaps accounted for 
as hedges, which are recorded in the balance sheet at a fair value of £9.4m (liability) (2007: asset of £1.6m). The following tables indicate the 
periods in which the cash flows associated with derivatives that are cash flow hedges are expected to occur:
       More

Interest rates used for determining fair value
Interest rates are linked to LIBOR, EURIBOR, NIBOR or CIBOR, depending on the origin of the underlying instrument.
Foreign exchange risk
Foreign exchange risk arises where the Group entities have an exposure to a currency that is not their functional currency. 
The Group’s operations are in based in the Netherlands, Denmark, Norway, Germany and Poland. The exposure of the Group to operational 
currency risk is limited because in general each of the operating companies sells its products in the territory where they are produced. The 
currency exposure connected with the Group’s ownership of foreign subsidiaries has been limited by aligning interest-bearing borrowings 
with the cash flows generated by the underlying operations of the Group (primarily euro, NOK and DKK), so providing an economic hedge. 
No derivatives have been entered into for this purpose.
Mecom Finance Limited (“MFL ”), a wholly-owned subsidiary of the Group, is the main financing entity of the Group and has a sterling 
functional currency. At 31 December 2008, MFL had foreign currency borrowings of €195.5m, NOK1,597.6m and DKK190.0m (2007: 
€152.5m, NOK1,608.0m and DKK209.5m). These borrowing have been made under the Group’s syndicated credit agreement, as described 
in Note 26. They are designated as a net investment hedge of the Group’s European trading operations and translation differences are 
recorded directly in equity.
At 31 December 2008 and 2007 there are no currency hedges of future cash flows.

Funding risk
Funding risk is the risk associated with maintaining the Group’s long-term borrowing arrangements. These include the risk of obtaining less 
favourable terms on refinancing, the risk of not meeting covenant requirements and the risks associated with a concentration of form, 
maturity or counterparty.
Notes 4 and 26 set out the details of the Group’s discussions with its lending banks over proposed revisions to the facility agreement and 
deferrals to the testing of 31 December 2008 covenants.
Capital management
Capital comprises equity attributable to the equity holders of the parent. The Group’s capital management policy is to ensure healthy 
covenant ratios are maintained in order to support operations and strategic objectives of the business as well as to maximise shareholder 
value. The Group monitors its capital and funding structure using net debt to adjusted EBITDA and adjusted EBITDA to net adjusted interest 
expense ratios. 
Liquidity risk
Liquidity risk is the risk that the Group will not be able to meet its financial obligations as they fall due. The Group aims to mitigate liquidity 
risk by ensuring the presence of flexible borrowing facilities and managing the cash generation of its operations. The Group places the 
majority of its cash in interest-bearing bank accounts and on short-term deposit. The Group monitors short- and medium-term interest rates 
and places cash on deposit for periods to optimise the amount of interest earned while maintaining access to sufficient funds to meet day-
to-day cash requirements.  104 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008
Financials
27. Financial risk management continued
Debt maturities are spread over a range of dates where possible and the Group makes early repayments where possible, thereby ensuring 
that the Group is not exposed to excessive refinancing risk in any one year. The Group’s liquidity risk arises from timing differences between 
cash inflows and outflows. The Group manages these risks through committed credit facilities.
For details of the Group’s credit facilities and of discussions with the Group’s lending banks over proposed versions to the terms of these 
facilities, see Notes 4 and 26.

Refinancing risk management
The Board controls refinancing risk by spreading the financing obligations (both principal and interest) of the Group over a number of years. 
This policy prevents the Group from having an excessively large amount of borrowings to refinance in any given year. Details of discussions 
with the Group’s leading banks on proposed revisions to its facility agreement are set out in Notes 4 and 26.
Credit risk
Credit risk is the risk of financial loss to the Group if a customer or counterparty to a financial instrument fails to meet its contractual 
obligations. The Group has procedures and guidelines in place to limit credit risks for each counterparty or market as follows: 
credit is only extended to new customers after a credit check has been carried out. External agencies are used to assess the credit- •	
worthiness of significant customers; 
credit limits are reviewed at least annually; and •	
new sales orders are not approved if the customer is in excess of its approved credit limit and/or payments are overdue. •	
Credit risk is reduced further by requiring that subscriptions to the Group’s newspapers are payable in advance.

The provision for doubtful debts is used to record provisions unless the Group is satisfied that no recovery of the amount owing is possible; 
at that point amounts outstanding are considered irrecoverable and written-off against the trade receivable directly. 
At 31 December 2008, the Group had trade receivables past due of £55.9m (2007: £59.7m), to which the provision of £13.0m (2007: £9.2m) 
relates, including £41.1m that were less than 90 days overdue (2007: £44.5m).
Fair value of financial assets and financial liabilities
As permitted by IFRS, the Group does not disclose the fair value of its financial assets and financial liabilities for both 2008 and 2007 
because the carrying amounts of these are a reasonable approximation of fair value. 
The fair value of interest-bearing loans is calculated based on discounting expected future principal and finance cash flows using the 
prevailing interest rate applicable to each loan. The fair value of interest rate derivatives is calculated by discounting the expected future cash 
flows using prevailing market interest rates as at the balance sheet date.
Quoted investments are carried at fair value, as calculated by reference to published share prices ruling at the balance sheet date.
Other non-current receivables, non-interest bearing loans and loans to employees are carried at amortised cost. Their fair value is based 
on the effective interest rate method if the time value of money is significant.

31. Employee benefit assets and obligations
Defined contribution plans
The Group participates in defined contribution pension plans in the Netherlands, Denmark and Norway. These include the Wegener General 
Pension Fund (APW) which was established on 1 January 2005 as a defined contribution fund. Wegener made a commitment to make 
contributions to this fund, such that the total employer and employee contributions total 25.7% of the pension entitlement each year, for a 
five year period from 1 January 2005. The contributions made do not cover the financing of increases in conditional entitlements or benefits 
which are attributable to past service. Wegener, at the end of the current five-year term of pension contributions is not liable to supplement 
any shortfalls and is not entitled to repayment of any surplus accrued. An agreement for the payment of pension contributions in the period 
beyond 1 January 2010 is expected to be reached during 2009. 
The Group participates in certain funded multi-employer pension plans in the Netherlands, where the annual pension contribution payable 
by the employer is set independently of the demographic profile of each employing company and benefits are paid from the pooled assets 
contributed by the participating employers. The Group does not have access to sufficient information on which to base a reliable estimate 
of its share of the assets and liabilities of these multi-employer plans (because this is not supplied by the plan) and so accounts for these 
plans on a defined contribution basis.
Defined benefit plans
The Group operates defined benefit plans in the Netherlands and Norway, where the Group is responsible, according to local legislation, 
for the payment of salary-related pension obligations through its funding of separate pension plans. Other defined benefit obligations (for 
example in Germany where a closed scheme exists for a small number of employees) are not material to the Group as a whole.
Pension liabilities and costs for the Group’s defined benefit plans are calculated by independent actuaries, using the project unit credit 
method. The overall expected return on assets is based on best estimates for the expected long-term real rates from the main assets 
classes, where equity is assumed to have a higher rate of return than other plan assets.
The Group expects contributions to defined benefit plans in future years to continue broadly at current levels.

Cash flow hedge reserve
The cash flow hedge reserve is used to record the unrealised gain or loss on the cash flow hedges entered into by the Group. The gain or 
loss is recognised in reserves only to the extent that it is considered to represent an effective hedge of the underlying instrument.
Share-based payment reserve
This reserve represents the accumulated share-based payment expenses the Group has recorded together with the equity component of 
convertible debt instruments (see Note 26).
Revaluation reserve
The Group includes on its balance sheet publicly traded investments, which are classified as available-for-sale. These are carried at market 
value. Temporary unrealised holding gains and losses on such investments are included within the revaluation reserve. Where there is a 
permanent diminution in value of investments, this impairment charge is recognised in the income statement. Any unrealised gains within 
this reserve are undistributable.
As shown in the statement of recognised income and expense on page 67, during the year £0.8m was transferred from the revaluation 
reserve to the income statement on the impairment of available-for-sale investments. This amount is included within the Group’s exceptional 
operating costs of £996.1m.
Notes to the consolidated financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008 113
Financials
34. Reserves continued
Currency translation reserve
The currency translation reserve comprises all foreign exchange differences arising from the translation of the financial statements of foreign 
subsidiaries and borrowings treated as net investment hedges. 
As shown in the consolidated statement of recognised income and expense on page 67, during the year £2.2m was transferred from the 
the currency translation reserve to the income statement on the disposal of foreign operations. This amount is included within the Group’s 
exceptional gain on disposal of subsidiaries and investments of £5.1m.
35. share-based payments 
Mecom Executive Share Option Plan (“ESOP”)
(i) Summary of arrangements
Nature       Grant of options
Service period 3 years
Performance conditions None
Maximum term 10 years
Method of settlement Share distribution
Expected departures (at grant date) 0%
Option exercise price calculation Closing price at the end of the previous trading day
(ii) Information relating to option valuation techniques
Options granted under the Mecom ESOP have been valued using a binomial option pricing model. Assumptions used by the model are  
as follows:
Expected volatility
As shares in Mecom Group plc have been listed for a relatively short period of time, there is insufficient share price history to calculate 
historical volatility. Accordingly, to arrive at a reasonable volatility assumption an analysis of the share price volatility of comparable companies 
was performed.
Expected dividend yield
A dividend yield of 0% has been used as it was not anticipated at the time of the valuation that a dividend would be introduced in the  
near future.
Risk-free rate
The assumption has been based on the yield available on similar dated zero coupon UK government bonds at the time the options were 
granted, using historical information taken from the Bank of England.
Participants’ exercise behaviour
The figures used are based on analysis of the ratio of the share price and exercise price using historical information from companies of a 
similar size to Mecom Group plc.
The weighted average estimated fair values and the inputs into the binomial pricing model for the ESOP are as follows:

Mecom Share Incentive Plan
The SIP provides the founder executives with a long-term incentive linked to the delivery of shareholder value. It is operated via an offshore 
employee benefit trust (“EBT”), established by the Company for the benefit of the past, present and future employees of the Group following 
admission of the Company’s shares to trading on AIM in 2005. 
Nil cost options over ordinary shares in Mecom Group plc were granted to the Trust such that the number of shares to be acquired by the 
SIP on exercise of the options will be calculated on the basis of a formula, the effect of which entitles the Trustees to acquire ordinary shares 
with an aggregate value equivalent to 10% of the increase in market capitalisation of the Company, less the market value of any new equity 
issued by the Company but adding back dividends paid, either five years from the date of admission or in the event of an offer for the 
Company. At the Extraordinary General Meeting held on 5 March 2007 the terms of the SIP were amended in certain minor respects relating 
to leaver provisions and the period within which options granted under the SIP can be exercised.
The Trustees have established discretionary sub-funds for the proposed beneficiaries under the SIP, into which the options will be allocated. 
The Trustees have appointed a reversionary interest in the sub-trusts to the individual beneficiaries concerned such that the sub-trust 
property will vest absolutely to the individuals at the end of the vesting period specified above.
If an individual ceases employment before the reversionary interest vests, the interest in the sub-trust property will lapse and the options 
allocated to that sub-trust could then become available to benefit Group employees generally. Further sub-trusts can be created for future 
employees should the Trustees consider it appropriate. 
In accordance with IFRS 2 Share-based Payment, the Group has recognised a charge which reflects the fair value of the options issued 
under the SIP. The fair value, calculated using a Monte Carlo simulation model, is £2.8m which is being expensed over the period from 23 
March 2005 to 23 March 2010. 
The estimated fair values and the inputs for the valuation of the SIP are as follows:
        
Growth rate per annum        7.0%
Expected volatility        40.0%
Expected dividend yield        0.0%
