38. Business combinations
Acquisitions during the year ended 31 December 2008
HR North AB
On 15 January 2008, the Group acquired 60.0% of the issued share capital of HR North AB (“HR North”), a leading online recruitment 
company incorporated in Sweden. HR North was acquired for £11.0m, comprising £8.3m cash consideration and £2.7m contingent 
consideration. The contingent consideration relates to a put option that the Group issued to the remaining shareholders of HR North, who 
own 40.0% of its equity. This has been included for accounting purposes within the Group’s 100.0% stake in HR North, although these 
shares will not be purchased until 2009 and 2010. For this reason, the Group has not recognised any minority interest on this acquisition. 
This purchase has been accounted for as an acquisition.
The acquisition of HR North is consistent with the Group’s increasing focus on digital platforms in order to secure its market position in a 
changing media environment. By acquiring the company, the Group has the opportunity to establish a platform for growth in the Swedish 
online media market. In addition, the company’s considerable expertise in recruitment classified sales can potentially be leveraged  
across other markets in which the Group operates. For the reasons outlined above, the Group paid a premium on the acquisition, giving 
rise to goodwill. 
Based on the final assessment of the fair values assigned to the cost of the combination and the acquiree’s net assets at the acquisition

Acquisitions during the year ended 31 December 2007
During 2007, the Group made two material acquisitions as described below. 
Berliner Verlag Deutsche Zeitungholding GmbH
On 13 April 2007, the Group acquired 78.0% of the issued share capital of Berliner Verlag Deutsche Zeitungholding GmbH (“Berliner 
Verlag”), a leading newspaper publisher in Berlin, Germany, of which the Group previously owned a further 15.0%. Berliner Verlag was 
acquired for £129.4m, comprising £90.6m cash consideration, £5.3m deferred consideration, £30.6m convertible loan note consideration 
and £2.9m of related acquisition expenses. The deferred consideration related to a put option that the Group issued to the remaining 
shareholders of Berliner Verlag, who owned 7.0% of its equity. This was included for accounting purposes within the Group’s 85.0% stake 
in Berliner Verlag, although these shares were not purchased until January 2008. For this reason, the Group did not recognise any minority 
interest on this acquisition. This purchase was accounted for as an acquisition. 
The acquisition of Berliner Verlag was consistent with the Group’s strategy to build a pan-European newspaper publishing business. 
Berliner Verlag is a leading newspaper publisher in Berlin. Its titles include the quality broadsheet Berliner Zeitung, East Berlin’s leading 
tabloid Berliner Kurier, the leading weekly advertising free-sheet Berliner Abendblatt and TIP, a bi-weekly Berlin entertainment guide. In 
addition, Berliner Verlag owns a modern print plant which prints both Group and third-party publications. For the reasons outlined above, 
the Group paid a premium on the acquisition, giving rise to goodwill. 
This acquisition was treated as a step-acquisition involving two steps, with each step representing a significant investment made by the 
Group. As required by step-acquisition accounting, the fair values of the assets and liabilities acquired, the consideration in relation to the 
acquisition and any subsequent goodwill were determined at each step. 
In the prior period and from 1 January to 12 April 2007, the Group’s stake in Berliner Verlag was treated as an associate because, although 
during these periods the Group exerted significant influence, it did not have control over Berliner Verlag’s operating and financial policies.
The accounting for the second step of this acquisition made on 13 April 2007 had only been determined on a provisional basis at 31 December 
2007 because the Group was still in the process of completing its work on the fair values assigned to the cost of the combination and the 
acquiree’s net assets. As a result of completing this work in 2008, no adjustments to either the cost of the combination or the acquiree’s 
net assets were required.

38. Business combinations continued
Koninklijke Wegener N.V. 
On 13 April 2007, the Group made an investment of £115.6m in Koninklijke Wegener N.V. (“Wegener”), a leading newspaper publisher based 
in Apeldoorn, the Netherlands, representing a stake of 23.6%. The Group acquired a further 29.7% stake in Wegener during the period from 
17 August to 14 September for total consideration of £162.5m. On 25 October 2007, the Group acquired a further stake of 33.1% in Wegener 
for total consideration of £205.8m. At 25 October 2007, the Group owned in total 86.4% of Wegener and gained control over its operating 
and financial policies on this date. 
The acquisition of Wegener represented a further step towards the implementation of the Group’s strategy to build a pan-European 
newspaper publishing business. Wegener is a substantial newspaper publisher in the Netherlands, whose titles include Brabants Dagblad, 
De Gelderlander and de Stentor, and this acquisition offered the Group the potential to create value in conjunction with its assets in Limburg, 
acquired in 2006. For these reasons, the Group paid a premium on the acquisition, giving rise to goodwill. As a consequence of this 
acquisition, the competition authorities in the Netherlands imposed a condition that the Group had to dispose of its De Trompetter operations. 
Further details of this are provided in Notes 13 and 39.
This acquisition was treated as a step-acquisition involving three steps, with each step representing a significant investment made by the 
Group. As required by step-acquisition accounting, the fair values of the cost of the combination and the acquiree’s net assets and any 
subsequent goodwill were determined at each step.
For the period from 13 April to 13 September 2007, the Group’s stake in Wegener was treated as an investment rather than an associate 
because the Group had made a public offer for the entire share capital of Wegener, during which period Mecom’s ability to exercise 
significant influence over Wegener’s policies was restricted due to both the negotiation process and uncertainty with regards to the outcome 
of the offer. 
For the period from 14 September to 24 October, the Group’s stake in Wegener was treated as an associate because, although during this 
period the Group exerted significant influence, it did not have control over Wegener’s operating and financial policies.
With regard to the third step of the acquisition on 25 October 2007 (from which date the Group controlled Wegener’s operating and financial 
policies), total consideration was £205.8m, comprising £112.1m cash consideration, £84.6m share consideration and £9.1m of related 
expenses. The fair value of the shares issued in the Company was based on 109.9 million shares at the fair value of those equity instruments 
at the date of exchange. 
The accounting for the Wegener acquisition had only been determined on a provisional basis at 31 December 2007 because the Group was 
still in the process of completing its work on the fair values assigned to the cost of the combination and the acquiree’s net assets. As a result 
of completing this work in 2008, no adjustments to either the cost of the combination or the acquiree’s net assets were required.
Included within Wegener’s equity at each of the three steps of the acquisition were 4.2 million cumulative financing preference shares, each 
with an issue price of €7.00, to which voting rights are attached. The Group did not acquire any of the cumulative financing preference 
shares on the first and second steps of the acquisition and as such their fair value has been removed from the provisional fair value of 
Wegener’s total net assets at these steps. However, on the third step of the acquisition the Group acquired 100.0% of the cumulative 
financing preference shares for zero goodwill.

41. Events after the balance sheet date
As described in Note 13, on 12 January 2009 the Group entered into a sale agreement to dispose of its German division to M. DuMont 
Schauberg Expedition der Kölnishen Zeitung GmbH & Co. KG for a price of £147.0m (€152.0m) on a cash- and debt-free basis. Completion 
of the disposal took place on 27 March 2009.
On 18 February 2009 the Group also announced the disposal of its Norway Northwestern assets to Polaris Media ASA for cash consideration 
of £55.5m (NOK559.3m). Completion of the disposal took place on 2 April 2009. 
On 27 April 2009, the Group announced that it had, via its Netherlands division, agreed in principle the sale of its joint-venture interest in 
ADNieuwsMedia B.V (“ADNM”) to PCM Uitgevers B.V. (“PCM”). The Group has a 37% economic interest and a 50% controlling interest in 
ADNM. As part-consideration for the disposal, the Group will receive 100% of the shares in PCM Lokale Media B.V., a subsidiary of PCM. 
Both of these transactions are expected to be completed in the first half of 2009.
On 29 April 2009, the Group reached ‘in principle’ agreement with its lending banks (subject to the completion and signing of full 
documentation and subject to the completion of the proposed equity issue) on the terms of a proposed revised bank facility agreement. 
The agreement given by the banks on the key terms of the proposed revised facility agreement are not binding on the banks but the Group 
believes that it is highly likely that full documentation will be signed, in May 2009. The key terms of the new bank deal are provided in Note 
4. On the same date, the Group received non-binding commitments from current and prospective shareholders (which will be conditional 
upon, inter alia, the Group agreeing acceptable banking terms with its lenders, publishing a prospectus and obtaining shareholder approval) 
to subscribe to a proposed share issue of approximately £140m (before expenses). The Group intends repaying the convertible loan notes 
from these proceeds. The Group expects to complete and to sign full banking documentation during May 2009, after which it expects that 
a prospectus for the issue of new shares will be issued with a view to receiving the proceeds of the share issue during June 2009.
In addition to the above, on 29 April 2009, the holders of the convertible loan notes relating to the acquisition of Berliner Verlag which were 
due for payment on 12 April 2009, agreed an extension of the maturity date to 12 July 2009, although it was agreed that this extension 
would accelerate to 31 May 2009 under certain conditions.

Independent auditors’ report to the members  
of Mecom Group plc
We have audited the parent company financial statements of Mecom 
Group plc for the year ended 31 December 2008 which comprise 
the Company balance sheet and the related Notes 1 to 14. These 
parent company financial statements have been prepared under 
the accounting policies set out therein. We have also audited the 
information in the Remuneration report that is described as having 
been audited. 
We have reported separately on the consolidated financial statements 
of Mecom Group plc for the year ended 31 December 2008. That 
report is modified by the inclusion of an emphasis of matter.
This report is made solely to the Company’s members, as a body, 
in accordance with Section 235 of the Companies Act 1985. Our 
audit work has been undertaken so that we might state to the 
Company’s members those matters we are required to state to 
them in an auditors’ report and for no other purpose. To the fullest 
extent permitted by law, we do not accept or assume responsibility 
to anyone other than the Company and the Company’s members 
as a body, for our audit work, for this report, or for the opinions we 
have formed.
Respective responsibilities of directors and auditors
The directors’ responsibilities for preparing the Annual report and 
accounts, the Remuneration report and the parent company 
financial statements in accordance with applicable United Kingdom 
law and Accounting Standards (United Kingdom Generally Accepted 
Accounting Practice) are set out in the Statement of directors’ 
responsibilities.
Our responsibility is to audit the parent company financial statements 
and the part of the remuneration Report to be audited in accordance 
with relevant legal and regulatory requirements and International 
Standards on Auditing (UK and Ireland).
We report to you our opinion as to whether the parent company 
financial statements give a true and fair view and whether the parent 
company financial statements and the part of the Remuneration 
report to be audited have been properly prepared in accordance 
with the Companies Act 1985. We also report to you whether in our 
opinion the information given in the Directors’ report is consistent 
with the parent company financial statements. The information 
given in the directors’ report includes that specific information 
presented in the Chairman’s statement, the Chief Executive’s review, 
the Market Overview, the Divisional reviews, the Group Finance 
Director’s report, Principal risks and uncertainties and Corporate 
social responsibility that is cross referred from the directors’ 
report. 
In addition we report to you if, in our opinion, the Company has not 
kept proper accounting records, if we have not received all the 
information and explanations we require for our audit, or if information 
specified by law regarding directors’ remuneration and other 
transactions is not disclosed.
We read other information contained in the Annual report and 
accounts and consider whether it is consistent with the audited 
parent company financial statements. The other information 
comprises only the following sections: Introduction, Transformation, 
New revenues, Titles, Our people, Our divisions, the Chairman’s 
statement, Group highlights, the Chief Executive’s review, Market 
overview, the Divisional reviews, the Group Finance Director’s 
report, Principal risks and uncertainties, Corporate social 
responsibility, The Board, the Directors’ report, Corporate 
governance, the unaudited part of the Remuneration report and 
Shareholder information. We consider the implications for our report 
if we become aware of any apparent misstatements or material 
inconsistencies with the parent company financial statements. Our 
responsibilities do not extend to any other information.
Basis of audit opinion
We conducted our audit in accordance with International Standards 
on Auditing (UK and Ireland) issued by the Auditing Practices Board. 
An audit includes examination, on a test basis, of evidence relevant 
to the amounts and disclosures in the parent company financial 
statements and the part of the Remuneration report to be audited. 
It also includes an assessment of the significant estimates and 
judgments made by the directors in the preparation of the parent 
company financial statements, and of whether the accounting 
policies are appropriate to the Company’s circumstances, 
consistently applied and adequately disclosed.
We planned and performed our audit so as to obtain all the 
information and explanations which we considered necessary in 
order to provide us with sufficient evidence to give reasonable 
assurance that the parent company financial statements and the 
part of the Remuneration report to be audited are free from material 
misstatement, whether caused by fraud or other irregularity or error. 
In forming our opinion we also evaluated the overall adequacy of the 
presentation of information in the parent company financial 
statements and the part of the Remuneration report to be audited.
Opinion
In our opinion:
the parent company financial statements give a true and fair •	
view, in accordance with United Kingdom Generally Accepted 
Accounting Practice, of the state of the Company’s affairs as at 
31 December 2008; 
the parent company financial statements and the part of the •	
Remuneration report to be audited have been properly prepared 
in accordance with the Companies Act 1985; and
the information given in the directors’ report is consistent with •	
the parent company financial statements.
Emphasis of matter – Going concern
In forming our opinion on the parent company financial statements, 
which is not qualified, we have considered the adequacy of the 
disclosure made in Note 1 concerning the amendments to the 
existing bank facility agreement, the raising of additional equity and 
the repayment of the convertible loan notes. These conditions, 
along with the other matters explained in Note 1 to the parent 
company financial statements, indicate the existence of material 
uncertainties which may cast significant doubt about the Company’s 
ability to continue as a going concern. The parent company financial 
statements do not include the adjustments that would result if the 
Company was unable to continue as a going concern.

1. Accounting policies
A summary of the Company’s significant accounting policies, which 
have been applied consistently, is set out below.
Basis of preparation: (i) Preparation of the Company’s 
financial statements on the going concern basis
The basis on which the Company’s financial statements have been 
prepared on the going concern basis, and the uncertainties related 
to ability of the Company’s principle subsidiaries to continue in 
operational existence in the foreseeable future are set out below. 
References to “Group” mean the Company and all its subsidiaries 
(direct and indirect) on a consolidated basis.
Background to negotiations on revised bank agreement and 
proposals for an equity issue
In December 2008, the Company announced its intention to reduce 
borrowings in its subsidiaries and, at the same time, entered into an 
agreement with its lending banks to defer the testing of financial 
covenants in its bank facilities agreement from 31 December 2008 
to 28 February 2009 (which was subsequently deferred further to 
31 March 2009, then further to 30 April 2009 and further to 31 May 
2009, as explained below) and engaged in discussions to renegotiate 
the terms of its bank facilities. 
The Company announced the disposal of its German operations 
(held indirectly by the Company) in January 2009 for consideration 
of €152.0m (£147.0m) and of its northwest Norwegian operations 
(held indirectly by the Company) in February 2009 for NOK559.3m 
(£55.5m) as part of its strategy to reduce borrowings. The cash 
proceeds from these disposals were received by the Group on 27 
March 2009 and 2 April 2009, respectively.
The Company announced on 23 March 2009 that it has been 
examining the merits of an equity fund-raising.
The Company announced on 1 April 2009 that it had also agreed 
with the holders of its convertible loan notes an extension to the 
maturity of these notes from 12 April to 12 May 2009, although it 
was agreed that this extension would revert to 30 April 2009 under 
certain conditions. 
On 29 April 2009, the Company entered into an agreement with its 
lending banks for a further deferral of the testing date of financial 
covenants until 31 May 2009 and the Company agreed a further 
extension of the maturity of the convertible loan notes to 12 July 
2009, although it was agreed that this extension would accelerate 
to 31 May 2009 under certain conditions. 
In principle agreement with lending banks on proposed revised 
bank facility agreement and with investors on proposed equity 
issue
On 29 April 2009, the Company:
reached ‘in principle’ agreement with its lending banks (subject •	
to the completion and signing of full documentation and subject 
to the completion of the proposed equity issue by no later than 
14 July 2009) on the terms of a proposed revised bank facility 
agreement. The agreement given by the banks on the key terms 
of the proposed revised facility agreement are not binding on 
the banks but each of the banks has received credit committee 
approval for the same and the Company believes that it is highly 
likely that full documentation will be signed in May 2009; and
received non-binding commitments from current and •	
prospective shareholders (which will be conditional upon, inter

alia, the Company agreeing acceptable banking terms with its 
lenders, publishing a prospectus and obtaining shareholder 
approval) to subscribe to a proposed share issue of approximately 
£140m (before expenses). The Company intends repaying the 
convertible loan notes from these proceeds.
The Company expects to complete and to sign full banking 
documentation during May 2009, after which it expects that a 
prospectus for the issue of new shares will be issued with a view to 
receiving the proceeds of the equity issue by during June 2009.
In the event that full banking documentation is not completed on the 
terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Company would continue discussion with its bank 
lenders with a view to agreeing alternative banking terms, but the 
directors cannot determine at this stage whether, or on what basis, 
alternative terms would be agreed.
In the event that full banking documentation is not completed on the 
terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does not 
happen, the Company would also expect to enter into discussions 
with the holders of the Company’s convertible loan notes to 
restructure the maturity of these notes, which would then be due 
currently and which the Company would be unable, in the absence 
of the agreement of the Company’s lending banks, to repay. The 
directors cannot determine at this stage what the outcome of these 
discussions would be.
In the event that the full banking documentation is not completed on 
the terms currently agreed or that the proposed equity issue does 
not happen, the Company’s ability to continue operating as a going 
concern would be dependent, therefore, on the outcome of these 
discussions with its lending banks and with the holders of the 
convertible loan notes.

The key terms of the revised bank deal (on the basis that share issue

as follows:

1. Accounting policies continued
warrants over the Company’s shares issued to the banks which •

capital of the Company.
In assessing the Company’s ability to remain in compliance with the 
terms of the revised facility agreement in the foreseeable future, the 
directors have taken into account the fact that the leverage, interest 
cover and operating cash flow covenants would not be tested under 
the proposed revised facility agreement within twelve months of the 
date of these financial statements. 
The directors have also considered the Group’s financial projections 
for the twelve month period from these financial statements as they 
affect the proposed revised bank facility agreement in respect of 
conditions other than the leverage, interest cover and operating 
cash flow covenants. In making its financial projections for these 
purposes, the Group has taken into account that it currently 
generates around 50% of its revenue from advertising, the markets 
for which have tended in the past to reflect the general economic 
conditions of the countries in which the Group operates. The 
remainder of the Group’s revenue includes circulation revenue 
(around 35% of total revenue), which has more stable characteristics 
compared with advertising revenue and has not previously been 
affected by prevailing economic conditions to the extent that 
advertising revenue has been.
The Group’s advertising markets have experienced a considerable 
and systematic downturn in recent months and, although the 
experience of recent weeks’ trading suggests that some stabilisation 
at these lower levels has occurred, the advertising environment 
remains challenging and uncertain. 
In making assumptions of future advertising revenue for the 
purposes of assessing its ability to comply with the terms of the 
proposed revised facility agreement, the Group has used a 
combination of long-term trends, industry and third-party forecasts 
and internal estimates which reflect recent experience in each of our 
markets. If the actual outturn is adverse to these assumptions, the 
Group has identified a number of further mitigating actions that it 
could take to reduce costs or borrowings further.
Going concern basis in the financial statements
The directors believe that the combination of the circumstances 
described above, in particular (a) the uncertainty as to the completion 
of a revised facility agreement on the terms currently agreed (b) the 
uncertainty as to whether the non-binding commitments of investors 
to underwrite the issue of new share capital will result in new shares 
being issued, with the completion of the revised facility arrangements 
and the issue of equity being inter-conditional, and (c) the uncertainty, 
in the event that the revised facility agreement is not completed on 
terms currently agreed or that the new share capital is not issued, 
as to whether the Company could reach satisfactory agreement 
with the holders of its convertible loan notes as to an extension of 
the maturity of those notes, all of which three factors existing within 
a highly uncertain advertising environment, represent a material 
uncertainty that casts significant doubt on the Company’s ability to 
continue as a going concern. Nevertheless, after making enquiries, 
and considering the uncertainties described above, the directors 
have a reasonable expectation that the Company have adequate 
resources to continue in operational existence for the foreseeable 
future. For these reasons, they continue to adopt the going concern 
basis in preparing the Company’s financial statements.
Basis of preparation: (ii) Other
The financial statements are prepared under the historical cost 
convention, in accordance with the Companies Act 1985 and 
applicable accounting standards in the UK.
Under section 230(4) of the Companies Act 1985 the Company  
is exempt from the requirement to present its own profit and  
loss account.
As consolidated financial information has been disclosed under 
IFRS 7, the parent is exempt from FRS 29 Financial Instrument 
Disclosures. The disclosures in respect of the Company are included 
in the consolidated accounts. The Group accounts have been 
prepared in accordance with International Financial Reporting 
Standards (“IFRS”) as adapted by the European Union and are 
presented on pages 66 to 124.
Change in accounting policy and explanation of prior year 
restatement 
As a result of the listing of the Company’s shares moving from the 
Alternative Investment Market (“AIM”) to the main LSE list in April 
2008, the Company adopted FRS 26 Financial Instruments: 
Recognition and Measurement during the year. As a consequence 
of adopting this Standard, it is now the policy of the Company to 
recognise changes in the fair value of its listed and unlisted 
investments directly in reserves (net of tax) instead of recognising 
such changes in the profit and loss account, unless such a change 
in fair value is deemed to be a permanent diminution of value.
The effect of adopting the Standard is that the Company has had to 
restate its 2007 balance sheet. An amount of £846,000 has been 
debited to the revaluation reserve and the same amount has been 
credited to the profit and loss account, causing that account to 
change from an accumulated loss of £6,108,000 to an accumulated 
loss of £5,262,000 at 31 December 2007. The profit for year ended 
31 December 2007 has also been restated from £4,762,000 to 
£5,608,000. 
Tangible fixed assets
Tangible fixed assets are stated at cost less accumulated 
depreciation and accumulated impairment losses. Depreciation is 
provided on all tangible fixed assets at rates calculated to write-off 
the cost or valuation of each asset on a straight-line basis over its 
expected useful life, as follows:
Leasehold improvements Shorter of 20 years and term of lease
Fixtures and fittings 5 years
Office equipment    3 years
The carrying values of tangible fixed assets are reviewed for 
impairment when events or changes in circumstances indicate the 
carrying value may not be recoverable.
Shares in Group undertakings
Investments in subsidiaries are  valued at cost less provisions for 
impairment. The Company has assessed the recoverable amount of  
its investments in Group undertakings in conjunction with the relevant 
amounts of post-impairment shareholders’ funds in the consolidated 
balance sheet. The required adjustment to the carrying amount of its 
investments in Group undertakings has been recognised in the 
Company’s profit and loss account. 
Listed investments
Listed investments are carried at market value, which is determined 
by reference to bid prices at the close of business at the balance 
sheet date. Revaluation gains and losses on listed investments are  
Notes to the Company financial statements continued
for the year ended 31 December 2008 129
Financials
1. Accounting policies continued
recorded in reserves net of tax. Where an investment is considered 
to have a permanent diminuation in value, the loss is recorded in the 
profit and loss account.
Unlisted investments
Unlisted investments are initially recognised at cost. In future periods 
the rebuttable assumption is that cost approximates fair value. 
Where there is a clear indicator of a change in fair value, then the 
asset is revalued through reserves (net of tax). Where an investment 
is considered to have a permanent diminuation in value, the loss is 
recorded in the profit and loss account.
Foreign currency
Transactions denominated in foreign currencies have been 
translated into sterling at actual rates of exchange ruling at the date 
of the transaction. Monetary assets and liabilities denominated in 
foreign currencies have been translated at rates ruling at the balance 
sheet date. Exchange differences arising on translation are taken to 
the profit and loss account.
Related party transactions
As the results of the Company are being presented together with  
its consolidated financial statements, the Company has taken 
advantage of the exception contained in FRS 8 Related Party 
Disclosures and has therefore not disclosed transactions or 
balances with entities which form part of the Group (or investees of 
the Group qualifying as related parties).
Deferred tax
The tax charge is based on the profit for the period and takes into 
account tax deferred because of timing differences between the 
treatment of certain items for tax and accounting purposes.
Deferred tax is recognised, without discounting, in respect of all 
timing differences that have arisen but not reversed at the balance 
sheet date where transactions or events have occurred at that date 
that will result in an obligation to pay more, or a right to pay less or 
to receive more, tax with the following exceptions:
A provision is made for tax on gains arising from the revaluation •	
(and similar fair value adjustments) of fixed assets, and gains on 
disposal of fixed assets that have been rolled over into 
replacement assets, only to the extent that at the balance sheet 
date, there is a binding agreement to dispose of the assets 
concerned. However, no provision is made where, on the basis 
of all available evidence at the balance sheet date, it is more 
likely than not that the taxable gain will be rolled over into 
replacement assets and charged to tax only where the 
replacement assets are sold.
A provision is made for deferred tax that would arise on •	
remittance of the retained earnings of overseas subsidiaries and 
associates only to the extent that, at the balance sheet date, 
dividends have been accrued as receivable.
Deferred tax assets are recognised only to the extent that the •	
directors consider that it is more likely than not that there will be 
suitable taxable profits from which the future reversal of the 
underlying timing differences can be deducted.
Deferred tax is measured at the tax rates that are expected to •	
apply in the periods in which timing differences reverse, based 
on tax rates and laws enacted or substantively enacted at the 
balance sheet date.
Share-based payments
Equity-settled share-based payments are measured at fair value 
(excluding the effect of non-market-based vesting conditions) at the 
date of grant. The fair value is calculated using either a Monte Carlo 
simulation model or a binomial model depending on the 
appropriateness of the model to the grant in question and is 
expensed on a straight-line basis over the vesting period. There is a 
corresponding amount recognised in reserves, equivalent to the 
expense recorded in the period.
At each balance sheet date before vesting, the cumulative expense is 
calculated, representing the extent to which the vesting period has 
expired and management’s best estimate of the achievement or 
otherwise of non-market performance conditions, and hence the 
number of equity instruments that will ultimately vest. The movement in 
cumulative expense since the previous balance sheet date is recognised 
in the income statement, with a corresponding entry in equity.
The dilutive effect of outstanding options is reflected as additional share 
dilution in the computation of earnings per share.
Financial instruments presentation and disclosure
In accordance with FRS 25 Financial Instruments: Disclosure and 
Presentation, when the Company issues a financial instrument that 
comprises both liability and equity components, such as convertible 
debt, it is treated as a compound instrument. Upon initial recognition, 
the fair value of the liability component is calculated as the present 
value of the contractual stream of future cash flows discounted at  
the market rate of interest that would have applied to an instrument 
of comparable credit quality with substantially the same cash flows, 
on the same terms, but without the conversion option. The 
subsequent accretion of the financial liability is recorded as a finance 
charge in the profit and loss account.
The equity portion is calculated by deducting the initial amount of 
the financial liability from the value of the instrument as a whole. The 
resultant amount is credited to the share-based payment reserve 
and is not re-measured.
Operating leases
Rentals payable under operating leases are charged to the profit 
and loss account on a straight-line basis over the lease term.
Cash flow statement
The Company is exempt under the terms of FRS 1 (Revised 1996) 
Cash Flow Statements from the requirement to publish its own cash 
flow statement, as its cash flows are included within the consolidated 
cash flow statement of the Group.

parent company.

s hares in Group undertakings
As a consequence of the significant impairments of non-current assets in the consolidated financial statements, during the year the 
directors carried out an impairment review of the Company’s investments in Group undertakings. It is the policy of the Company to carry its 
investments in Group undertakings at the lower of cost and the shareholders’ funds in the consolidated balance sheet. At 31 December 
2008, shareholders’ funds in the consolidated balance sheet were £182,900,000, resulting in an impairment charge of £791,385,000 being 
recognised in the Company’s profit and loss account. At 31 December 2008, the cost and valuation of shares in Group undertakings were 
£974,838,000 and £183,453,000, respectively (2007: cost of £974,725,000).

1-for-10 share-split) and at 31 December 2008 had a closing price of 77.50 pence (2007: 16.25 pence). The charge resulting from the 
change in market value of this investment during the year, which was treated as impairment, of £144,500 is included within the Company’s 
result for the year. In 2007, the change in market value of £846,000 was recorded in the revaluation reserve. At 31 December 2008, the cost 
and valuation of the investment in STV Group plc was £1,424,500 and £131,750, respectively (2007: £1,424,500 and £276,250).

Espresso Broadband Limited (“Espresso”) and Hightex Group plc (“Hightex”) to Mecom Group plc. 
Espresso is a private company incorporated in England and Wales. At 31 December 2007, MUK owned 518,179 ordinary shares, 786,137 
A ordinary shares and 2,474,929 B ordinary shares in Espresso, with a total valuation of £411,080. In addition, at 31 December 2007 MUK 
held A loan notes, B loan notes and C loan notes in Espresso, with nominal values of £101,157, £13,966 and £53,277, respectively. These 
investments were transferred to Mecom Group plc on 1 January 2008 at the book value of £579,480. During the year, certain of the loan 
stock with a valuation of £53,277 were redeemed. Also during the year, an impairment charge of £285,305 was recorded against the 
carrying value of this investment. At 31 December 2008, the cost and valuation of the investment in Espresso was £526,203 and £240,898, 
respectively. 
Hightex is listed on the Alternative Investment Market and is incorporated in England and Wales. At 31 December 2007, MUK owned 
205,000 ordinary shares in Hightex, with a total cost of £11,408. This investment was transferred to Mecom Group plc on 1 January 2008 
at the book value of £11,408. During the year, the Company purchased a further 205,000 shares in Hightex, at a cost of £17,938. At 31 
December 2008, the cost of the investment in Hightex was £29,346.

Mecom Executive Share Option Plan (“ESOP”)
(i) Summary of arrangements
Nature Grant of options
Service period 3 years
Performance conditions None
Maximum term 10 years
Method of settlement Share distribution
Expected departures (at grant date) 0%
Option exercise price calculation Closing price at the end of the previous trading day
(ii) Information relating to option valuation techniques
Options granted under the Mecom ESOP have been valued using a binomial option pricing model. Assumptions used by the model are  
as follows:
Expected volatility
As shares in Mecom Group plc have been listed for a relatively short period of time, there is insufficient share price history to calculate 
historical volatility. Accordingly, to arrive at a reasonable volatility assumption an analysis of the share price volatility of comparable companies 
was performed.
Expected dividend yield
A dividend yield of 0% has been used as it was not anticipated at the time of the valuation that a dividend would be introduced in the  
near future.
Risk-free rate
The assumption has been based on the yield available on similar dated zero coupon UK government bonds at the time the options were 
granted, using historical information taken from the Bank of England.
Participants’ exercise behaviour
The figures used are based on analysis of the ratio of the share price and exercise price using historical information from companies of a 
similar size to Mecom Group plc. 134 Mecom Group plc Annual report and accounts 2008

Mecom Share Incentive Plan (“SIP”)
The SIP provides the founder executives with a long-term incentive linked to the delivery of shareholder value. It is operated via an offshore 
employee benefit trust (“EBT”), established by the Company for the benefit of the past, present and future employees of the Group following 
admission of the Company’s shares to trading on AIM in 2005.
Nil cost options over ordinary shares in Mecom Group plc were granted to the Trust such that the number of shares to be acquired by the 
SIP on exercise of the options will be calculated on the basis of a formula, the effect of which entitles the Trustees to acquire ordinary shares 
with an aggregate value equivalent to 10% of the increase in market capitalisation of the Company, less the market value of any new equity 
issued by the Company but adding back dividends paid, either five years from the date of admission or in the event of an offer for the 
Company. At the Extraordinary General Meeting held on 5 March 2007 the terms of the SIP were amended in certain minor respects relating 
to leaver provisions and the period within which options granted under the SIP can be exercised.

12. share-based payments continued
The Trustees have established discretionary sub-funds for the proposed beneficiaries under the SIP, into which the options will be allo-
cated. The Trustees have appointed a reversionary interest in the sub-trusts to the individual beneficiaries concerned such that the sub-trust 
property will vest absolutely to the individuals at the end of the vesting period specified above.
If an individual ceases employment before the reversionary interest vests, the interest in the sub-trust property will lapse and the options 
allocated to that sub-trust could then become available to benefit Group employees generally. Further sub-trusts can be created for future 
employees should the Trustees consider it appropriate.
In accordance with FRS 20 Share-based Payment, the Company has recognised a charge which reflects the fair value of the options issued 
under the SIP. The fair value, calculated using a Monte Carlo simulation model, is £2.8m which is being expensed over the period from 
23 March 2005 to 23 March 2010.

14. Events after the balance sheet date
On 29 April 2009, the Company reached ‘in principle’ agreement with its lending banks (subject to the completion and signing of full 
documentation and subject to the completion of the proposed equity issue) on the terms of a proposed revised bank facility agreement. The 
agreement given by the banks on the key terms of the proposed revised facility agreement are not binding on the banks but the Company 
believes that it is highly likely that full documentation will be signed, in May 2009. The key terms of the new bank deal are provided in Note 1. 
On the same date, the Company received non-binding commitments from current and prospective shareholders (which will be conditional 
upon, inter alia, the Company agreeing acceptable banking terms with its lenders, publishing a prospectus and obtaining shareholder 
approval) to subscribe to a proposed share issue of approximately £140m (before expenses). The Company intends repaying the convertible 
loan notes from these proceeds. The Company expects to complete and to sign full banking documentation during May 2009, after which it 
expects that a prospectus for the issue of new shares will be issued with a view to receiving the proceeds of the share issue during June 
2009.

Identity theft
Criminals may steal your personal information, putting your 
shareholding at risk.
Tips on protecting your shareholding:
Ensure all your certificates are kept in a safe place or hold your •	
shares electronically in CREST via a nominee
Keep all correspondence from the registrars which shows your •	
shareholder reference number in a safe place, or destroy 
correspondence by shredding
If you change address inform the registrars. If you receive a •	
letter from the registrars regarding a change of address and 
have not recently moved, please contact them immediately.  
You may be the victim of identity theft
If you are buying or selling shares, only deal with brokers •	
registered in your country of residence or the UK
Warning to shareholders
Over the last year many companies have become aware that their 
shareholders have received unsolicited phone calls or 
correspondence concerning investment matters which imply a 
connection to the company concerned. These are typically from 
overseas based ‘brokers’ who target UK shareholders offering to 
sell them what often turn out to be worthless or high risk shares in 
US or UK investments.
They can be very persistent and extremely persuasive and a 2006 
survey by the Financial Services Authority (FSA) has reported that 
the average amount lost by investors is around £20,000. It is not  
just the novice investor that has been duped in this way; many of  
the victims had been successfully investing for several years. 
Shareholders are advised to be very wary of any unsolicited advice, 
offers to buy shares at a discount or offers of free reports into  
the company.
If you receive any unsolicited investment advice: 
Make sure you get the correct name of the person and •	
organisation and make a record of any other information they 
give you, e.g. telephone number, address etc 
Check that they are properly authorised by the FSA before •	
getting involved. You can check at www.fsa.gov.uk/register. 
The FSA also maintains on its website a list of unauthorised •	
overseas firms who are targeting, or have targeted, UK investors 
and any approach from such organisations should be reported 
to the FSA so that this list can be kept up to date and any other 
appropriate action can be considered. If you deal with an 
unauthorised firm, you would not be eligible to receive payment 
under the Financial Services Compensation Scheme. The FSA 
can, preferably, be contacted by completing an online form at 
http://www.fsa.gov.uk/pages/doing/regulated/law/alerts/
overseas.shtml or, if you do not have access to the internet, on 
0845 606 1234. 
Inform our Registrars on 0870 664 0300. They are not able to •	
investigate such incidents themselves but will record the  
details and pass them on to Mecom Group plc and liaise with 
the FSA. Details of any share dealing facilities that the  
company endorses will be included in company mailings. More 
detailed information on this or similar activity can be found  
on the FSA website http://www.moneymadeclear.fsa.gov.uk/.
